Absence, Revocation, and Missing Heirs in Bequests
Complex procedural rules for absent parties, revocation, and missing heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules of standing when legatees, heirs, or judges are absent, and when a bequest is revoked.

Core Idea
The standing of parties in bequest disputes changes dramatically when one party is absent or the bequest is revoked.

This passage continues from al-Jami' and introduces al-Jami' al-Saghir, covering more complex scenarios: when the first legatee is absent, when a bequest is revoked, and when a depositary denies knowledge of the testator's death. Each case modifies who can be a contestant and before which judge.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the scenario with absent first legatee
If the first legatee is absent and a second legatee appears, the heir is not a contestant for the second unless the first legatee acknowledges the property as bequest.
The rule differs based on who is absent and which judge hears the case.
2
Understand the effect of acknowledgment
If the first legatee acknowledges the property is from the bequest, he is a contestant. If he denies, he is still a contestant but the burden changes.
3
Study the revocation case
If the testator revoked the first bequest and made a second, the judge takes the property from the first and gives to the second.
Revocation must be proven by witnesses.
4
Examine the Jami' al-Saghir scenario
If a man holds a deposit and the owner is missing, and a claimant says the owner died and bequeathed it to him, the judge does not create a dispute until the heir appears or the holder acknowledges.
This protects the interests of absent parties.
5
Determine the rule when the holder claims ownership
If the holder of the property claims it is his own, he becomes a contestant against the claimant, similar to a sale dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا إذا كان الموصى له غير العبد، فلو كان هو العبد قال في الأصل: رجل مات وترك عبداً وورثة صغاراً وترك ديناً على رجل فأقام العبد بينة أن مولاه أعتقه وأوصى إليه ومن عليه الدين حاضر فالشهادة جائزة ويقضى بالعتق وبالوصايا للعبد. وينبغي في قياس قول أبي حنيفة أن لا تقبل شهادتهما في العتق . وإن كانت الورثة كباراً وأقام العبد بينة على ذلك فالشهادة جائزة ويقضى بالعتق وبالوصايا. هذا على خلاف رواية الأصل . وفي نوادر إبراهيم عن محمد: رجل مات ولرجل عليه دين وأوصى بثلث ماله أو بدرهم سماه لرجل فأخذها الموصى له ثم جاء الغريم والورثة شهود أو غيب وقدم الموصى له إلى القاضي والموصى له لا يكون خصماً للغريم. هذا إذا حصلت الوصية له بقدر الثلث، وإذا حصلت الوصية بما زاد على الثلث إلى جميع المال وصحة الوصية بأن لم يكن للميت وارث فالموصى له خصم الغريم في هذه الحالة. يعتبر الموصى له في هذه الحالة بالوارث. قال محمد رحمه الله في الجامع: رجل هلك ترك ثلاثة آلاف درهم وأقام وارثاً واحداً فأقام رجل البينة أن الميت أوصى له وحجد الوارث ذلك قضى القاضي له بالثلث وأعطاه بذلك وهو ألف درهم، ثم جاء رجلا وأقام البينة أن الميت أرصى له بثلث ماله وأحضر الموصى له إلى القاضي فالقاضي يجعله خصماً ويأمره أن يدفع نص ما في يده إلى الثاني، فإن قضى القاضي على الأول بنصف الثلث ولم يكن عنده شيء بأن هلك الثلث في يده أو استهلكه وهو فقير والوارث لم يكلف الثاني إعادة البينة وكان للموصى له الثاني أن يشارك الوراث فيما في يده ويأخذ خمس ما في يد الوراث. ولو كان الموصى له هو الغائب فأحضر الثاني الوراث إلى القاضي قضى على الأول، وإن كان القاضي قضى بوصية الأول ولم يدفع إليه شيئاً حتى خاصمه الثاني والوارث غائب، فإن خاصمه إلى ذلك القاضي بعينه جعل خصماً، وإن خاصمه إلى قاض آخر لم يجعله خصماً. ولو كان الموصى له بثلث ماله الأول هو الغائب والوارث حاضر لم يدفع المال إلى الأول فالوارث خصم للموصى له الثاني. وهذا كله إذا أقر الموصى له الأول بأن كان المال الذي في يده بحكم الوصية أو كان ذلك معلوم للقاضي، فإذا لم يكن شيء من ذلك فقال الأول هو مالي ورثته عن أبي الميت وما أوصى لي بشيء وما أخذت من ماله شيئاً فإنه يكون خصماً للموصى له الثاني بمنزلة ما لو ادعى رجل عبداً في يد رجل أنه اشتراه من فلان بكذا وقال ذو اليد هو عبدي ورثته عن أبي يكون خمساً ويقضى عليه للمدعي كذا هنا. وإن قال هذا المال عندي وديعة لفلان الميت الذي يدعي الوصية من جهته أو قال غصبته فهو خصم إلا أن يقيم بينة على ما قال. قال رجل أقام بينة على وارث ميت أن الميت أوصى بهذه الجارية بعينها وهي ثلث ماله وقضى القاضي بذلك ودفعها إليه وغاب الوارث، ثم أقام الآخر البينة على الموصى له أن الميت أوصى له بها ذكروا رجوعاً قضى القاضي بكل الجارية للثاني، وإن لم يذكروا رجوعاً قضى بنصفها للثاني للمزاحمة والمساواة ويكون هذا قضاء على الوراث غاب أو حضر حتى إن الموصى له الأول لو أبطل حقه كان كل الجارية للثاني، فإن غاب الموصى له وحضر الوارث لم ينتصب الوارث خصماً للموصى له الآخر خاصمه إلى القاضي الأول أو إلى غيره فإن كان القاضي قضى للأول بالجارية فلم يدفعها إليه حتى خاصم الثاني الوارث، فإن خاصمه فيها إلى القاضي الأول لم يجعله خصماً، وإن خاصمه إلى قاض آخر يجعله خصماً، ثم القاضي إذا سمع بينة الثاني على الوراث في هذا الفصل وهو ما إذا خاصمه الثاني عند قاض آخر قضى للثاني بنصف الجارية، سواء شهد شهوده على الرجوع عن الأول أو لم يشهدوا على الرجوع، وإنما يشكل فيما إذا شهدوا على الرجوع ولو أقام الأول بينة أن الميت أوصى له بثلث ماله ودفعه القاضي إليه ثم أقام الثاني البينة على الأول أن الميت رجع عن الوصية الأولى وأوصى بثلث ماله للثاني فالقاضي يأخذ الثلث من الأول ويدفعه إلى الثاني. قال محمد في الجامع الصغير: رجل له على آخر ألف درهم قرض أو كان غصب منه ألف درهم وكانت في يد الغاصب قائمة بعينها أقام رجل البينة أن فلاناً استودعه ألف درهم وهي قائمة بعينها في يد المودع فأقام رجل البينة أن صاحب المال توفي وأوصى له بهذا الألف التي هي قبل هذا الرجل والرجل مقر بالمال لكنه يقول لا أدري مات فلان أو لم يمت لم يجعل القاضي بينهما خصومة حتى يحضر وارث أو كذلك، ونظيرها إذا دعى عيناً في يد رجل أنه اشتراها من فلان الغائب وصاحب اليد يقول أنا مودع الغائب أو غصبته منه لا: ينتصب خصماً للمودع كذا هنا. وهذا الذي ذكرنا إن كان الذي قبله المال مقراً بذلك، فإن كان الذي في يده المال قال هذا ملكي وليس عندي من مال الميت شيء صار خصماً للمدعي وصار كرجل ادعى عيناً في يد رجل أنه اشتراه من فلان الغائب وصاحب اليد يقول هو لي ينتصب خصماً للمدعي كذا هذا. وإن جعله القاضي خصماً في هذا الوجه قضى له بثلث ما في يد المدعى عليه إلا أن يقيم البينة أن الميت ترك ألف درهم غير هذا الألف وأن الوارث قبض ذلك فحينئذ يقضي القاضي للموصى له بكل هذا الألف. ولو حضر الوارث بعد ذلك وقال لم أقبض من مال الميت شيئاً ما لم يلتفت إلى قوله، فإن أقام البينة أن فلاناً مات ولم يدع وارثاً ولا وصياً يقبل القاضي بينته.
This is when the legatee is not the slave. If he is the slave, he said in al-Asl: A man died leaving a slave and minor heirs, and left a debt owed by a man. The slave established proof that his master freed him and bequeathed to him, and the debtor is present. The testimony is admissible and judgment is given for manumission and the bequests to the slave. According to the analogy of Abu Hanifa's opinion, their testimony regarding manumission should not be accepted. And if the heirs are adults and the slave established proof of that, the testimony is admissible and judgment is given for manumission and the bequests. This is contrary to the narration of al-Asl. And in Nawadir Ibrahim from Muhammad: A man died and a man had a debt against him, and he bequeathed one-third of his property or a specified dirham to a man. The legatee took it. Then the creditor and the heirs, witnesses or absent, came and brought the legatee before the judge. The legatee is not a contestant against the creditor. This applies when the bequest to him is within one-third. And when the bequest exceeds one-third up to the entire property and the validity of the bequest, because the deceased has no heir, then the legatee is a contestant against the creditor in this case. The legatee in this case is considered like an heir. Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said in al-Jami': A man died leaving three thousand dirhams and one heir. A man established proof that the deceased bequeathed to him, and the heir denied it. The judge adjudicated one-third to him and gave him that, which is one thousand dirhams. Then another man came and established proof that the deceased bequeathed to him one-third of his property and brought the first legatee before the judge. The judge makes him a contestant and orders him to pay half of what is in his hand to the second. If the judge adjudicated against the first for half of the one-third and he has nothing, such that the one-third perished in his hand or he consumed it while poor, and the heir did not require the second to re-establish proof, then the second legatee may share with the heirs in what is in their hand and take one-fifth of what is in the hand of the heirs. And if the legatee is absent, and the second brings the heirs before the judge, judgment is given against the first. And if the judge had adjudicated the bequest to the first and did not give anything to him until the second disputed with him while the heir was absent, then if he disputes with him before that same judge, he makes him a contestant; if he disputes before another judge, he does not make him a contestant. And if the first legatee of one-third of his property is absent and the heir is present, and the property was not given to the first, then the heir is a contestant for the second legatee. All of this applies if the first legatee acknowledged that the property in his hand was by virtue of the bequest, or that was known to the judge. If none of that is the case, and the first says, 'It is my property I inherited from my father, the deceased,' and 'He did not bequeath anything to me, and I did not take anything from his property,' then he becomes a contestant against the second legatee, just as if a man claimed a slave in the hand of a man that he bought from so-and-so for such-and-such, and the possessor said, 'He is my slave I inherited from my father,' then he is a contestant, and judgment is given against him for the claimant. The same here. And if he says, 'This property is with me as a deposit for so-and-so, the deceased from whom the bequest is claimed,' or he says 'I usurped it,' then he is a contestant unless he establishes proof for what he said. A man established proof against an heir of a deceased that the deceased bequeathed this specific slave-girl, and she is one-third of his property, and the judge adjudicated it and gave her to him, and the heir was absent. Then another established proof against the first legatee that the deceased bequeathed her to him. If they mention a revocation, the judge adjudicates the entire slave-girl to the second. If they do not mention a revocation, he adjudicates half of her to the second for competition and equality. And this is a judgment against the heirs, whether absent or present, such that if the first legatee relinquishes his right, the entire slave-girl goes to the second. If the legatee is absent and the heir is present, the heir does not become a contestant for the other legatee, whether he disputes before the first judge or another. If the judge had adjudicated the slave-girl to the first but had not given it to him until the second disputed with the heir, if he disputes about her before the first judge, he does not make him a contestant; if he disputes before another judge, he makes him a contestant. Then the judge, when he hears the proof of the second against the heirs in this section, i.e., when the second disputes before another judge, he adjudicates half the slave-girl to the second, whether his witnesses testify about revocation from the first or not. The only difficulty is when they testify about revocation. And if the first established proof that the deceased bequeathed to him one-third of his property and the judge gave it to him, then the second established proof against the first that the deceased revoked the first bequest and bequeathed one-third of his property to the second, then the judge takes the one-third from the first and gives it to the second. Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: A man has a loan of one thousand dirhams against another, or he was usurped one thousand dirhams and it remained in the hand of the usurper as it was. A man established proof that so-and-so deposited one thousand dirhams with him, and they are still in the hand of the depositary. Then a man established proof that the owner of the money died and bequeathed this one thousand to him, which is with this man. And the man acknowledges the property but says, 'I do not know whether so-and-so died or not.' The judge does not create a dispute between them until an heir or similar is present. Its analogy: if a specific property in the hand of a man is claimed that he bought it from an absent person, and the possessor says, 'I am the depositary of the absent person, or I usurped it from him,' he does not become a contestant for the depositor. The same here. This is when the person who holds the property acknowledges that. If the one in whose hand the property is says, 'This is my property, and I have none of the deceased's property,' he becomes a contestant against the claimant, just as if a man claims a specific property in the hand of a man that he bought from an absent person, and the possessor says, 'It is mine,' he becomes a contestant against the claimant. The same here. And if the judge makes him a contestant in this case, he adjudicates one-third of what is in the hand of the defendant to him, unless he establishes proof that the deceased left one thousand dirhams other than this one thousand, and that the heir received that. Then the judge adjudicates all this one thousand to the legatee. And if the heir later appears and says, 'I did not receive anything from the deceased's property,' no attention is paid to his statement. If he establishes proof that so-and-so died leaving no heir or executor, the judge accepts his proof.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This lengthy passage presents a series of detailed case studies (masa'il) from various sources including al-Asl, Nawadir Ibrahim, and al-Jami' by Imam Muhammad. The core issue is determining who has standing (khasm) in court when there are competing claims involving bequests, heirs, and creditors. The first scenario discusses when the legatee is the slave himself. If the slave claims manumission and bequest, his witnesses are accepted, but Abu Hanifa's analogy would suggest rejecting their testimony regarding manumission because it is the slave's right. However, the text notes this is contrary to a narration from al-Asl. The second scenario from Nawadir deals with a debtor and a legatee: if the bequest is within one-third, the legatee cannot contest the creditor; but if the bequest exceeds one-third and there are no heirs, the legatee is like an heir and can contest. The third major scenario from al-Jami' involves two legatees: the first has already received one-third, then a second legatee appears. The judge makes the first legatee a contestant and orders him to share. If the first has consumed the property and is poor, the second can share with the heirs and take one-fifth of what the heirs hold. The rules differ depending on whether the legatee acknowledges the property as coming from the bequest or denies it, and whether parties are absent or present. The passage also covers revocation of bequests, missing heirs, and analogies to claims of sale or deposit. Overall, the text demonstrates the complexity of procedural law in cases of bequests and the importance of determining who has the right to litigate.

Key Terms
الرجوع (al-ruju'): Revocation of a bequest.
الوديعة (al-wadi'a): Deposit; property left with someone for safekeeping.
الوصي (al-wasi): Executor; a person appointed to carry out the testator's will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the slave-girl scenario, if witnesses testify that the testator revoked the first bequest and made a second, what does the judge do?
A) Give half the slave-girl to the second
B) Give the entire slave-girl to the second
C) Give the entire slave-girl back to the heirs
D) Dismiss the case due to conflict

Key Takeaway
The presence, absence, acknowledgment, and revocation all affect who has standing in bequest disputes, requiring careful analysis of each scenario.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Revocation and Competition in Bequests
Ruling on conflicting bequests and khasm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on conflicting bequests: when revocation is proven the second legatee takes all; when not proven they share half; and identify who can be a valid khasm when a legatee is absent.

Core Idea
A proven revocation of a bequest gives the second legatee the entire property; without it, they share equally.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi case: two legatees claim the same slave-girl, which is one-third of the estate. The ruling hinges on whether the testator revoked the first bequest. We also explore the important concept of 'khasm'—who can represent an absent party in court—and how the judge's decision binds heirs even if absent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
Read the scenario: two legatees claim the same slave-girl. Determine what evidence each brings and whether revocation is mentioned.
2
Apply the rule on revocation
If the second legatee proves the testator revoked the first bequest, the judge gives the entire slave-girl to the second. Without revocation, both share equally because they are equal in claim.
The judge's decision is binding on heirs even if absent.
3
Analyze the concept of khasm
When the first legatee is absent and the heir is present, the heir is not a valid khasm for the second legatee. If the second sues before the same judge, the judge does not accept; if sues before a different judge, he does.
This ensures fairness: the second legatee can find a judge who will hear the case.
4
Distinguish the outcome with and without revocation
If the second legatee's witnesses mention revocation, full award. If they don't, half award. The difficulty arises only when they testify to revocation.

Source Text

كتاب الوصايا باب العتق في المرض والوصية بالعتق
أوصى لي بشيء وما أخذت من ماله شيئاً فإنه يكون خصماً للموصى له الثاني بمنزلة ما لو أبي ادعى رجل عبداً في يد رجل أنه اشتراه من فلان بكذا وقال ذو اليد هو عبدي ورثته عن يكون خمساً ويقضى عليه للمدعي كذا هنا. وإن قال هذا المال عندي وديعة لفلان الميت الذي يدعي الوصية من جهته أو قال غصبته فهو خصم إلا أن يقيم بينة على ما قال. قال رجل أقام بينة على وارث ميت أن الميت أوصى بهذه الجارية بعينها وهي ثلث ماله وقضى القاضي بذلك ودفعها إليه وغاب الوارث، ثم أقام الآخر البينة على الموصى له أن الميت أوصى له بها ذكروا رجوعاً قضى القاضي بكل الجارية للثاني، وإن لم يذكروا رجوعاً قضى بنصفها للثاني للمزاحمة والمساواة ويكون هذا قضاء على الوراث غاب أو حضر حتى إن الموصى له الأول لو أبطل حقه كان كل الجارية للثاني، فإن غاب الموصى له وحضر الوارث لم ينتصب الوارث خصماً للموصى له الآخر خاصمه إلى القاضي الأول أو إلى غيره فإن كان القاضي قضى للأول بالجارية فلم يدفعها إليه حتى خاصم الثاني الوارث، فإن خاصمه فيها إلى القاضي الأول لم يجعله خصماً، وإن خاصمه إلى قاض آخر يجعله خصماً، ثم القاضي إذا سمع بينة الثاني على الوراث في هذا الفصل وهو ما إذا خاصمه الثاني عند قاض آخر قضى للثاني بنصف الجارية، سواء شهد شهوده على الرجوع عن الأول أو لم يشهدوا على الرجوع، وإنما يشكل فيما إذا شهدوا على الرجوع ولو أقام الأول بينة أن الميت أوصى له بثلث ماله ودفعه القاضي إليه ثم أقام الثاني البينة على الأول أن الميت رجع عن الوصية الأولى وأوصى بثلث ماله للثاني فالقاضي يأخذ الثلث من الأول ويدفعه إلى الثاني . قال محمد في الجامع الصغير: رجل له على آخر ألف درهم قرض أو كان غصب منه ألف درهم وكانت في يد الغاصب قائمة بعينها أقام رجل البينة أن فلاناً استودعه ألف درهم وهي قائمة بعينها في يد المودع فأقام رجل البينة أن صاحب المال توفي وأوصى له بهذا الألف التي هي قبل هذا الرجل والرجل مقر بالمال لكنه يقول لا أدري مات فلان أو لم يمت لم يجعل القاضي بينهما خصومة حتى يحضر وارث أو كذلك، ونظيرها إذا دعى عيناً في يد رجل أنه اشتراها من فلان الغائب وصاحب اليد يقول أنا مودع الغائب أو غصبته منه لا : ينتصب خصماً للمودع كذا هنا. وهذا الذي ذكرنا إن كان الذي قبله المال مقراً بذلك، فإن كان الذي في يده المال قال هذا ملكي وليس عندي من مال الميت شيء صار خصماً للمدعي وصار كرجل ادعى عيناً في يد رجل أنه اشتراه من فلان الغائب وصاحب اليد يقول هو لي ينتصب خصماً للمدعي كذا هذا. وإن جعله القاضي خصماً في هذا الوجه قضى له بثلث ما في يد المدعى عليه إلا أن يقيم البينة أن الميت ترك ألف درهم غير هذا الألف وأن الوارث قبض ذلك فحينئذ يقضي القاضي للموصى له بكل هذا الألف. ولو حضر الوارث بعد ذلك وقال لم أقبض من مال الميت شيئاً ما لم يلتفت إلى قوله، فإن أقام البينة أن فلاناً مات ولم يدع وارثاً ولا وصياً يقبل القاضي بينته، ثم عاد محمد البحر الرائق ج 9/ م 18 وصي
إلى صدر المسألة فقال : لو أن الموصى له أقام البينة أن فلاناً مات ولم يدع وارثاً وأوصى إليه بالألف التي قبل فلان وقال الشهود لا نعلم له وارثاً والذي قبله المال مقر بالمال الذي قبله فالقاضي يقضي بالمال للموصى له قال محمد في الجامع رجل ألف درهم دين أو كان الألف في يده غصباً أو وديعة أو كانت الألف فهذا فغاب صاحب المال فقام رجلا وادعى أن صاحب المال أوصى له بهذا الألف الذي قبل هذا الرجل ولا بينة له فصدقه الذي قبله المال فهذا على وجهين : أما إن أقر المدعي أن لصاحب المال وارثاً غائباً أو قال لا أدري أله وارث أم لا، أو قال المدعي ليس لصاحب المال وارث. وإن كان صاحب المال رجلاً نصرانياً أسلم ولم يترك أحداً وصدقه الذي قبله المال في ذلك ففي الوجه الأول القاضي لا يقضي على الذي في يديه المال في الوجوه الأربعة الغصب والوديعة والدين والإيصاء إلا أن القاضي يتلوم في ذلك ويتأنى ولا يعجل، فإن جاء مدع أو وارث وإلا قضى القاضي بالمال للمدعي، وإن كان المال وديعة عند رجل كان له أن يضمن القابض بإجماع. وهل له أن يضمن المودع؟ فعل قول محمد رحمه الله كان له ذلك، وعلى قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله ليس له ذلك. وإن كان المال ديناً فلصاحب المال أن يضمن الغريم وليس له أن يضمن القابض، وإن ضمن الغريم كان للغريم أن يرجع على القابض .
وأما إذا كان المال وصل إليه من قبل أبيه أوصى إليه أبوه وصورة هذا وتفسيره إذا كان الرجل ألف درهم دفعها إلى رجل وجعله وصياً فيه ثم مات الموصى له فوصل المال إلى ابن الموصي من جهة أبيه الذي كان أوصى بها إلى ابنه وكان في يديه فدفع إلى هذا المدعي بأمر القاضي. ثم جاء صاحب المال حياً ولكن حضر وارثه فأقام البينة أنه أخوه من أبيه وأمه لا وارث له غيره فلا ضمان على الذي قبله المال في الوجوه كلها وأن الذي في يده المال أقر أن هذا أخ صاحب المال وأنه قد مات إلا أني لا أدري أهذا وارثه أم لا لم يقض القاضي في ذلك زماناً فلم يظهر له وارث آخر ودفع المقر المال إلى المقر له بأمر القاضي ثم جاء صاحب المال حياً قال محمد في الكتاب : فهو بمنزلة الموصى له في جميع ما وصفت لك في حق التضمين ولو بقي صاحب المال حياً لكن جاء رجل وأقام البينة أنه ابنه قال في الكتاب : هذا بمنزلة الموصى له في جميع ما وصفت لك في أنه لا ضمان على الذي قبله المال في الفصول كلها، وأن الضمان على القابض. ولو أن الذي في يده المال أقر لرجل أنه ابن الميت وأن للميت ابناً آخر وقال الابن المقر له ليس له ابن آخر تلوم القاضي زماناً، وإذا تلوم زماناً ولم يحضر وارث آخر دفع المال كله إليه. ثم قال في الكتاب : إذا تلوم القاضي زماناً ولم يظهر للميت ابن آخر أمر القاضي الذي قبله المال أن يدفع المال كله إلى المدعي ويأخذ منه كفيلاً ثقة، وما لم يعطه كفيلاً ثقة لا يدفع المال نظراً للغائب لجواز أن يكون للميت ابن آخر، فمن مشايخنا من قال : هذا قولهما. أما على قول أبي حنيفة لا يأخذ كفيلاً. وقال بعض المشايخ :
Book of Wills, Chapter on Manumission in Illness and Bequest of Manumission. He bequeathed something to me and I took nothing from his property, then he becomes a representative for the second legatee like if he refused. A man claimed a slave in the hand of a man that he bought it from so-and-so for such amount, and the possessor said: 'He is my slave, I inherited him from...' it becomes a fifth and judgment is passed against him for the claimant similarly here. If he said: 'This property is a deposit with me for so-and-so the deceased from whom the bequest is claimed' or said 'I usurped it', he is a representative unless he produces evidence for what he said. A man produced evidence against an heir of a deceased that the deceased bequeathed this particular slave-girl and she is one-third of his property, and the judge decided that and handed her over to him, and the heir was absent. Then another produced evidence against the legatee that the deceased bequeathed her to him; they mentioned a recantation, the judge gave all of the slave-girl to the second. If they did not mention a recantation, he gave half of her to the second due to competition and equality, and this is a judgment against the heirs whether absent or present, such that if the first legatee invalidated his right, all of the slave-girl goes to the second. If the legatee was absent and the heir present, the heir does not become a representative for the other legatee—whether he sues him before the first judge or another. If the judge judged for the first with the slave-girl but did not hand her over until the second sued the heir, if he sued him before the first judge, he does not make him a representative; if he sued before another judge, he makes him a representative. Then the judge, when he hears the evidence of the second against the heirs in this chapter—i.e., when the second sues before another judge—judges for the second half of the slave-girl, whether his witnesses testified to recantation from the first or did not testify to recantation. The difficulty is only when they testify to recantation. If the first produced evidence that the deceased bequeathed to him one-third of his property and the judge gave it to him, then the second produced evidence against the first that the deceased revoked the first bequest and bequeathed one-third of his property to the second, the judge takes the third from the first and gives it to the second. Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: A man has a loan of one thousand dirhams against another, or a usurpation of one thousand dirhams from him, and they are still in the hand of the usurper; a man produced evidence that so-and-so deposited with him one thousand dirhams still in the hand of the depositary; then a man produced evidence that the owner of the money died and bequeathed to him this thousand which is with this man, and the man admits the money but says: 'I do not know whether so-and-so died or not'—the judge does not establish litigation between them until an heir appears or similarly. Its analogue: if someone claims an identifiable thing in the hand of a man that he bought it from absent so-and-so, and the possessor says: 'I am the depositary of the absent one' or 'I usurped it from him', he does not become a representative for the depositary similarly here. This that we mentioned is if the one who holds the money admits that. If the one in whose hand the money says: 'This is my property and I have nothing of the deceased's property', he becomes a representative for the claimant, and becomes like a man who claims an identifiable thing in the hand of a man that he bought it from absent so-and-so, and the possessor says: 'It is mine'—he becomes a representative for the claimant. Similarly this. If the judge makes him a representative in this case, he judges for him one-third of what is in the hand of the defendant unless he produces evidence that the deceased left one thousand dirhams other than this thousand and the heir took that; then the judge gives all of this thousand to the legatee. If the heir later appears and says: 'I received nothing of the deceased's property', his statement is not heeded. If he produces evidence that so-and-so died leaving neither heir nor executor, the judge accepts his evidence. Then Muhammad returned to the beginning of the issue and said: If the legatee produced evidence that so-and-so died leaving no heir and bequeathed to him the thousand that is with so-and-so, and the witnesses say: 'We do not know of any heir for him', and the holder of the money admits the money he holds, the judge gives the money to the legatee. Muhammad said in al-Jami': A man has one thousand dirhams as a debt, or the thousand is in his hand as a usurpation or deposit or it is the thousand—so this, then the owner of the money was absent, and a man came and claimed that the owner bequeathed to him this thousand that is with this man, and he has no evidence; the holder of the money confirmed him. This is in two aspects: either the claimant admits that the owner has an absent heir, or says: 'I do not know if he has an heir or not', or the claimant says: 'The owner has no heir'. If the owner was a Christian who became Muslim and left no one, and the holder confirmed him in that—in the first aspect, the judge does not give a judgment against the one in whose hand the money is in the four cases: usurpation, deposit, debt, and bequest—except that the judge delays in that, waits, and does not hurry. If a claimant or heir comes, otherwise the judge gives the money to the claimant. If the money was a deposit with a man, he has the right to hold the receiver liable by consensus. Does he have the right to hold the depositary liable? According to the saying of Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, he has that; according to the saying of Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, he does not have that. If the money was a debt, the owner has the right to hold the debtor liable and not the receiver; if he holds the debtor liable, the debtor has recourse against the receiver. As for if the money reached him from his father—his father bequeathed to him; its form and interpretation: if a man had one thousand dirhams which he gave to a man and made him an executor over it, then the legatee died, so the money reached the son of the testator from his father who had bequeathed it to his son and it was in his hand, and he gave it to this claimant by order of the judge. Then the owner of the money came alive, but his heir appeared and produced evidence that he is his full brother—he has no other heir—so there is no liability on the one who held the money in all cases, and that the one in whose hand the money admitted that this is the brother of the owner and that he had died, except that I do not know if this is his heir or not. The judge did not give any judgment in that for a time, and no other heir appeared, so the admitter gave the money to the admitted by order of the judge. Then the owner of the money came alive. Muhammad said in the book: He is like the legatee in all that I described to you concerning the matter of liability. Even if the owner of the money remained alive but a man came and produced evidence that he is his son, he said in the book: This is like the legatee in all that I described to you in that there is no liability on the one who held the money in all sections, and that liability is on the receiver. If the one in whose hand the money admitted to a man that he is the son of the deceased and that the deceased has another son, and the admitted son said: 'He has no other son', the judge delays for a time. If he delays for a time and no other heir appears, he gives all the money to him. Then he said in the book: If the judge delays for a time and no other son of the deceased appears, he orders the one who held the money to give all the money to the claimant and take from him a reliable guarantor. As long as he does not give him a reliable guarantor, he does not give the money, out of consideration for the absent one because it is possible that the deceased has another son. Some of our teachers said: This is their saying (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). As for the saying of Abu Hanifa, he does not take a guarantor. And some teachers said: [text incomplete]
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of rulings from the chapter on bequests, specifically dealing with disputes over property when a bequest is claimed. The author, from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, explains multiple scenarios drawn from al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad. The first scenario involves two claimants (legates) to a slave-girl who is one-third of the estate. If the second claimant proves that the testator revoked the first bequest, the judge gives all to the second. If no revocation is proven, they share half each because they are equal in claim. The judge's decision binds the heirs even if absent. The second scenario involves a person holding property (as loan, deposit, or usurpation) and a claimant who has no evidence but is corroborated by the holder. The judge delays and waits for an heir; if none appears, he gives the property to the claimant after obtaining a guarantor in some cases. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad allows the owner to sue the depositary (where the deposit was wrongfully given to someone else), while Abu Yusuf does not. Also, Abu Hanifa does not require a guarantor, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require one to protect the absent heir. These rulings illustrate the Hanafi method of balancing claims, evidence, and protection of absent parties.

Key Terms
موصى له (mūṣā lahu): The person in whose favor a bequest is made; the legatee.
بينة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically testimony of two male witnesses or one male and two females.
خصم (khaṣm): A party in litigation; here it refers to the person who can be sued or can represent the absent person in court.
رجوع (rujūʿ): Revocation or recantation of a bequest.
مزاحمة (muzāḥamah): Competition or conflict of claims; when two claimants have equal right, they share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two legatees claim the same slave-girl which is one-third of the estate, and the second legatee proves that the testator revoked the first bequest, what does the judge do?
A) Gives all of the slave-girl to the second legatee.
B) Gives half to each legatee.
C) Gives all to the first legatee.
D) Gives the slave-girl to the heirs.

Key Takeaway
When conflicting bequests are proven, revocation gives the second legatee the entire property; without revocation, they share equally.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
10 min
Property Claims: Admission, Evidence, and Intra-Hanafi Differences
Exposition of property claim procedures and intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi procedural rules for property claims when the holder admits the claim, distinguish between the positions of Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on suing the depositary, and identify when a guarantor is required.

Core Idea
When a property holder admits a claim but is uncertain of the claimant's status, the judge delays and may require a guarantor before awarding property.

This lesson delves into complex scenarios where a person holds property (as deposit, debt, or usurpation) and a claimant appears with or without evidence. The text from al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Bahr al-Ra'iq outlines the judge's procedure: delaying, waiting for heirs, and sometimes requiring a guarantor. Important intra-Hanafi differences emerge, particularly between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on suing the depositary, and between Abu Hanifa and the two disciples on taking a guarantor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of property held
Determine whether the property is held as loan (debt), deposit, usurpation, or bequest from a father. The ruling on liability varies.
2
Classify the holder's response
Does the holder admit the property and claim ignorance of the testator's death, or does he deny the claimant's right? Admission without knowledge of death leads to no immediate litigation.
3
Apply the judge's procedure
When the holder admits but is uncertain, the judge delays (talawwum) and waits for an heir or other claimant. If no heir appears, the judge may award the property to the claimant after taking a guarantor.
Guarantor requirement is disputed: Abu Hanifa does not require, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do.
4
Determine liability for misdelivery
If the holder wrongly gives property to someone, who is liable? For deposit, the owner can sue the receiver by consensus. But can he sue the depositary? Muhammad says yes, Abu Yusuf says no.
For debt, the owner sues the debtor, not the receiver.
5
Handle the case of an absent heir
If the holder admits to a claimant that he is the son of the deceased, but there is another possible son, the judge delays. If no other heir appears, he awards the property after a guarantor.

كتاب الوصايا باب العتق في المرض والوصية بالعتق
أوصى لي بشيء وما أخذت من ماله شيئاً فإنه يكون خصماً للموصى له الثاني بمنزلة ما لو أبي ادعى رجل عبداً في يد رجل أنه اشتراه من فلان بكذا وقال ذو اليد هو عبدي ورثته عن يكون خمساً ويقضى عليه للمدعي كذا هنا. وإن قال هذا المال عندي وديعة لفلان الميت الذي يدعي الوصية من جهته أو قال غصبته فهو خصم إلا أن يقيم بينة على ما قال. قال رجل أقام بينة على وارث ميت أن الميت أوصى بهذه الجارية بعينها وهي ثلث ماله وقضى القاضي بذلك ودفعها إليه وغاب الوارث، ثم أقام الآخر البينة على الموصى له أن الميت أوصى له بها ذكروا رجوعاً قضى القاضي بكل الجارية للثاني، وإن لم يذكروا رجوعاً قضى بنصفها للثاني للمزاحمة والمساواة ويكون هذا قضاء على الوراث غاب أو حضر حتى إن الموصى له الأول لو أبطل حقه كان كل الجارية للثاني، فإن غاب الموصى له وحضر الوارث لم ينتصب الوارث خصماً للموصى له الآخر خاصمه إلى القاضي الأول أو إلى غيره فإن كان القاضي قضى للأول بالجارية فلم يدفعها إليه حتى خاصم الثاني الوارث، فإن خاصمه فيها إلى القاضي الأول لم يجعله خصماً، وإن خاصمه إلى قاض آخر يجعله خصماً، ثم القاضي إذا سمع بينة الثاني على الوراث في هذا الفصل وهو ما إذا خاصمه الثاني عند قاض آخر قضى للثاني بنصف الجارية، سواء شهد شهوده على الرجوع عن الأول أو لم يشهدوا على الرجوع، وإنما يشكل فيما إذا شهدوا على الرجوع ولو أقام الأول بينة أن الميت أوصى له بثلث ماله ودفعه القاضي إليه ثم أقام الثاني البينة على الأول أن الميت رجع عن الوصية الأولى وأوصى بثلث ماله للثاني فالقاضي يأخذ الثلث من الأول ويدفعه إلى الثاني . قال محمد في الجامع الصغير: رجل له على آخر ألف درهم قرض أو كان غصب منه ألف درهم وكانت في يد الغاصب قائمة بعينها أقام رجل البينة أن فلاناً استودعه ألف درهم وهي قائمة بعينها في يد المودع فأقام رجل البينة أن صاحب المال توفي وأوصى له بهذا الألف التي هي قبل هذا الرجل والرجل مقر بالمال لكنه يقول لا أدري مات فلان أو لم يمت لم يجعل القاضي بينهما خصومة حتى يحضر وارث أو كذلك، ونظيرها إذا دعى عيناً في يد رجل أنه اشتراها من فلان الغائب وصاحب اليد يقول أنا مودع الغائب أو غصبته منه لا : ينتصب خصماً للمودع كذا هنا. وهذا الذي ذكرنا إن كان الذي قبله المال مقراً بذلك، فإن كان الذي في يده المال قال هذا ملكي وليس عندي من مال الميت شيء صار خصماً للمدعي وصار كرجل ادعى عيناً في يد رجل أنه اشتراه من فلان الغائب وصاحب اليد يقول هو لي ينتصب خصماً للمدعي كذا هذا. وإن جعله القاضي خصماً في هذا الوجه قضى له بثلث ما في يد المدعى عليه إلا أن يقيم البينة أن الميت ترك ألف درهم غير هذا الألف وأن الوارث قبض ذلك فحينئذ يقضي القاضي للموصى له بكل هذا الألف. ولو حضر الوارث بعد ذلك وقال لم أقبض من مال الميت شيئاً ما لم يلتفت إلى قوله، فإن أقام البينة أن فلاناً مات ولم يدع وارثاً ولا وصياً يقبل القاضي بينته، ثم عاد محمد البحر الرائق ج 9/ م 18 وصي
إلى صدر المسألة فقال : لو أن الموصى له أقام البينة أن فلاناً مات ولم يدع وارثاً وأوصى إليه بالألف التي قبل فلان وقال الشهود لا نعلم له وارثاً والذي قبله المال مقر بالمال الذي قبله فالقاضي يقضي بالمال للموصى له قال محمد في الجامع رجل ألف درهم دين أو كان الألف في يده غصباً أو وديعة أو كانت الألف فهذا فغاب صاحب المال فقام رجلا وادعى أن صاحب المال أوصى له بهذا الألف الذي قبل هذا الرجل ولا بينة له فصدقه الذي قبله المال فهذا على وجهين : أما إن أقر المدعي أن لصاحب المال وارثاً غائباً أو قال لا أدري أله وارث أم لا، أو قال المدعي ليس لصاحب المال وارث. وإن كان صاحب المال رجلاً نصرانياً أسلم ولم يترك أحداً وصدقه الذي قبله المال في ذلك ففي الوجه الأول القاضي لا يقضي على الذي في يديه المال في الوجوه الأربعة الغصب والوديعة والدين والإيصاء إلا أن القاضي يتلوم في ذلك ويتأنى ولا يعجل، فإن جاء مدع أو وارث وإلا قضى القاضي بالمال للمدعي، وإن كان المال وديعة عند رجل كان له أن يضمن القابض بإجماع. وهل له أن يضمن المودع؟ فعل قول محمد رحمه الله كان له ذلك، وعلى قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله ليس له ذلك. وإن كان المال ديناً فلصاحب المال أن يضمن الغريم وليس له أن يضمن القابض، وإن ضمن الغريم كان للغريم أن يرجع على القابض .
وأما إذا كان المال وصل إليه من قبل أبيه أوصى إليه أبوه وصورة هذا وتفسيره إذا كان الرجل ألف درهم دفعها إلى رجل وجعله وصياً فيه ثم مات الموصى له فوصل المال إلى ابن الموصي من جهة أبيه الذي كان أوصى بها إلى ابنه وكان في يديه فدفع إلى هذا المدعي بأمر القاضي. ثم جاء صاحب المال حياً ولكن حضر وارثه فأقام البينة أنه أخوه من أبيه وأمه لا وارث له غيره فلا ضمان على الذي قبله المال في الوجوه كلها وأن الذي في يده المال أقر أن هذا أخ صاحب المال وأنه قد مات إلا أني لا أدري أهذا وارثه أم لا لم يقض القاضي في ذلك زماناً فلم يظهر له وارث آخر ودفع المقر المال إلى المقر له بأمر القاضي ثم جاء صاحب المال حياً قال محمد في الكتاب : فهو بمنزلة الموصى له في جميع ما وصفت لك في حق التضمين ولو بقي صاحب المال حياً لكن جاء رجل وأقام البينة أنه ابنه قال في الكتاب : هذا بمنزلة الموصى له في جميع ما وصفت لك في أنه لا ضمان على الذي قبله المال في الفصول كلها، وأن الضمان على القابض. ولو أن الذي في يده المال أقر لرجل أنه ابن الميت وأن للميت ابناً آخر وقال الابن المقر له ليس له ابن آخر تلوم القاضي زماناً، وإذا تلوم زماناً ولم يحضر وارث آخر دفع المال كله إليه. ثم قال في الكتاب : إذا تلوم القاضي زماناً ولم يظهر للميت ابن آخر أمر القاضي الذي قبله المال أن يدفع المال كله إلى المدعي ويأخذ منه كفيلاً ثقة، وما لم يعطه كفيلاً ثقة لا يدفع المال نظراً للغائب لجواز أن يكون للميت ابن آخر، فمن مشايخنا من قال : هذا قولهما. أما على قول أبي حنيفة لا يأخذ كفيلاً. وقال بعض المشايخ :
Book of Wills, Chapter on Manumission in Illness and Bequest of Manumission. He bequeathed something to me and I took nothing from his property, then he becomes a representative for the second legatee like if he refused. A man claimed a slave in the hand of a man that he bought it from so-and-so for such amount, and the possessor said: 'He is my slave, I inherited him from...' it becomes a fifth and judgment is passed against him for the claimant similarly here. If he said: 'This property is a deposit with me for so-and-so the deceased from whom the bequest is claimed' or said 'I usurped it', he is a representative unless he produces evidence for what he said. A man produced evidence against an heir of a deceased that the deceased bequeathed this particular slave-girl and she is one-third of his property, and the judge decided that and handed her over to him, and the heir was absent. Then another produced evidence against the legatee that the deceased bequeathed her to him; they mentioned a recantation, the judge gave all of the slave-girl to the second. If they did not mention a recantation, he gave half of her to the second due to competition and equality, and this is a judgment against the heirs whether absent or present, such that if the first legatee invalidated his right, all of the slave-girl goes to the second. If the legatee was absent and the heir present, the heir does not become a representative for the other legatee—whether he sues him before the first judge or another. If the judge judged for the first with the slave-girl but did not hand her over until the second sued the heir, if he sued him before the first judge, he does not make him a representative; if he sued before another judge, he makes him a representative. Then the judge, when he hears the evidence of the second against the heirs in this chapter—i.e., when the second sues before another judge—judges for the second half of the slave-girl, whether his witnesses testified to recantation from the first or did not testify to recantation. The difficulty is only when they testify to recantation. If the first produced evidence that the deceased bequeathed to him one-third of his property and the judge gave it to him, then the second produced evidence against the first that the deceased revoked the first bequest and bequeathed one-third of his property to the second, the judge takes the third from the first and gives it to the second. Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: A man has a loan of one thousand dirhams against another, or a usurpation of one thousand dirhams from him, and they are still in the hand of the usurper; a man produced evidence that so-and-so deposited with him one thousand dirhams still in the hand of the depositary; then a man produced evidence that the owner of the money died and bequeathed to him this thousand which is with this man, and the man admits the money but says: 'I do not know whether so-and-so died or not'—the judge does not establish litigation between them until an heir appears or similarly. Its analogue: if someone claims an identifiable thing in the hand of a man that he bought it from absent so-and-so, and the possessor says: 'I am the depositary of the absent one' or 'I usurped it from him', he does not become a representative for the depositary similarly here. This that we mentioned is if the one who holds the money admits that. If the one in whose hand the money says: 'This is my property and I have nothing of the deceased's property', he becomes a representative for the claimant, and becomes like a man who claims an identifiable thing in the hand of a man that he bought it from absent so-and-so, and the possessor says: 'It is mine'—he becomes a representative for the claimant. Similarly this. If the judge makes him a representative in this case, he judges for him one-third of what is in the hand of the defendant unless he produces evidence that the deceased left one thousand dirhams other than this thousand and the heir took that; then the judge gives all of this thousand to the legatee. If the heir later appears and says: 'I received nothing of the deceased's property', his statement is not heeded. If he produces evidence that so-and-so died leaving neither heir nor executor, the judge accepts his evidence. Then Muhammad returned to the beginning of the issue and said: If the legatee produced evidence that so-and-so died leaving no heir and bequeathed to him the thousand that is with so-and-so, and the witnesses say: 'We do not know of any heir for him', and the holder of the money admits the money he holds, the judge gives the money to the legatee. Muhammad said in al-Jami': A man has one thousand dirhams as a debt, or the thousand is in his hand as a usurpation or deposit or it is the thousand—so this, then the owner of the money was absent, and a man came and claimed that the owner bequeathed to him this thousand that is with this man, and he has no evidence; the holder of the money confirmed him. This is in two aspects: either the claimant admits that the owner has an absent heir, or says: 'I do not know if he has an heir or not', or the claimant says: 'The owner has no heir'. If the owner was a Christian who became Muslim and left no one, and the holder confirmed him in that—in the first aspect, the judge does not give a judgment against the one in whose hand the money is in the four cases: usurpation, deposit, debt, and bequest—except that the judge delays in that, waits, and does not hurry. If a claimant or heir comes, otherwise the judge gives the money to the claimant. If the money was a deposit with a man, he has the right to hold the receiver liable by consensus. Does he have the right to hold the depositary liable? According to the saying of Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, he has that; according to the saying of Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, he does not have that. If the money was a debt, the owner has the right to hold the debtor liable and not the receiver; if he holds the debtor liable, the debtor has recourse against the receiver. As for if the money reached him from his father—his father bequeathed to him; its form and interpretation: if a man had one thousand dirhams which he gave to a man and made him an executor over it, then the legatee died, so the money reached the son of the testator from his father who had bequeathed it to his son and it was in his hand, and he gave it to this claimant by order of the judge. Then the owner of the money came alive, but his heir appeared and produced evidence that he is his full brother—he has no other heir—so there is no liability on the one who held the money in all cases, and that the one in whose hand the money admitted that this is the brother of the owner and that he had died, except that I do not know if this is his heir or not. The judge did not give any judgment in that for a time, and no other heir appeared, so the admitter gave the money to the admitted by order of the judge. Then the owner of the money came alive. Muhammad said in the book: He is like the legatee in all that I described to you concerning the matter of liability. Even if the owner of the money remained alive but a man came and produced evidence that he is his son, he said in the book: This is like the legatee in all that I described to you in that there is no liability on the one who held the money in all sections, and that liability is on the receiver. If the one in whose hand the money admitted to a man that he is the son of the deceased and that the deceased has another son, and the admitted son said: 'He has no other son', the judge delays for a time. If he delays for a time and no other heir appears, he gives all the money to him. Then he said in the book: If the judge delays for a time and no other son of the deceased appears, he orders the one who held the money to give all the money to the claimant and take from him a reliable guarantor. As long as he does not give him a reliable guarantor, he does not give the money, out of consideration for the absent one because it is possible that the deceased has another son. Some of our teachers said: This is their saying (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). As for the saying of Abu Hanifa, he does not take a guarantor. And some teachers said: [text incomplete]
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of rulings from the chapter on bequests, specifically dealing with disputes over property when a bequest is claimed. The author, from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, explains multiple scenarios drawn from al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad. The first scenario involves two claimants (legates) to a slave-girl who is one-third of the estate. If the second claimant proves that the testator revoked the first bequest, the judge gives all to the second. If no revocation is proven, they share half each because they are equal in claim. The judge's decision binds the heirs even if absent. The second scenario involves a person holding property (as loan, deposit, or usurpation) and a claimant who has no evidence but is corroborated by the holder. The judge delays and waits for an heir; if none appears, he gives the property to the claimant after obtaining a guarantor in some cases. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad allows the owner to sue the depositary (where the deposit was wrongfully given to someone else), while Abu Yusuf does not. Also, Abu Hanifa does not require a guarantor, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require one to protect the absent heir. These rulings illustrate the Hanafi method of balancing claims, evidence, and protection of absent parties.

Key Terms
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or guaranty; the obligation to compensate for loss or return property.
مقر (muqirr): A person who admits or acknowledges a claim; the admitter.
قابض (qābiḍ): The receiver; the person who takes possession of property.
مودع (mūdiʿ): The depositary; the person with whom a deposit is left.
تلوُم (talawwum): The judge's act of delaying and waiting for additional claimants or evidence.
كفيل (kafīl): Guarantor; a person who provides surety for the claimant's future return of property if another heir appears.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on suing the depositary (mudiʿ) when he wrongfully delivers a deposit to a receiver?
A) It is allowed by consensus.
B) It is allowed according to Muhammad but not according to Abu Yusuf.
C) It is never allowed.
D) It is allowed only if the owner provides a guarantor.

Key Takeaway
When a property holder admits a claim but is uncertain, the judge delays and may require a guarantor; liability for misdelivery depends on the capacity of property and the imam's view.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
6 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Debt and Manumission in Terminal Illness
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sa'y in terminal illness manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding sa'y when a terminally ill person manumits a slave with debt, and explain the legal reasoning (dalil) for each.

Core Idea
Debt acknowledgment is stronger than manumission; in conflict, the slave must work (sa'y) per Abu Hanifa.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute on the conflict between debt and manumission in terminal illness. You will learn the ruling of each imam, their proofs, and how the stronger right (debt) prevails over the weaker (manumission). The mufta bihi position is that the slave is freed but must work to pay his value.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the core legal question: When a terminally ill person acknowledges a debt and manumits a slave, is the slave required to perform sa'y (working to pay his value) to satisfy the debt?
The debt and manumission occur in the same speech during terminal illness.
2
Identify the Hanafi position and its proof
State Abu Hanifa's ruling: The slave is freed but must work (sa'y). Then analyse his proof: Debt acknowledgment is stronger because it comes from the entire estate, while manumission only from the third. The stronger overcomes the weaker, analogised to a case in health where both are acknowledged.
This is a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) based on strength of rights.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position and proof
State the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: The slave is freed without sa'y. Their proof: Both acts occur simultaneously in one statement; in health, simultaneity does not impose sa'y. They argue that the heir's attestation places both acts on equal footing, so no working is required.
The Sahibayn focus on the simultaneity of the acts.
4
Follow the Hanafi response
Understand how Abu Hanifa rebuts: Debt can be attributed to the state of health because there is no obstacle, while manumission cannot be so attributed due to the restriction to one-third. The debt is prior and stronger, so it overcomes the manumission in meaning (imposing sa'y) even though the manumission is valid.
The principle 'al-aqwa yadfa‘ al-ad‘a' (the stronger repels the weaker) is invoked.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, the slave works; under the Sahibayn, the slave is free without encumbrance. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position, as recorded in al-Hidayah.
This difference affects creditors: they may recover the slave's value under Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا باب العتق في المرض والوصية بالعتق قيمته وتدفع إلى الغريم) وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : يعتق ولا يسعى في شيء لأن الدين والعتق في الصحة ظهرا معاً بتصدق الوارث في كلام واحد فصار كأنهما وجدا معاً أو ثبت ذلك بالبينة والعتق في الصحة لا يوجب السعاية وإن كان على المعتق دين. وله أن الإقرار بالدين أقوى من الإقرار بالعتق ولهذا يعتبر إقراره بالدين من جميع المال وبالعتق من الثلث والأقوى يدفع الأدنى فصار كإقرار المورث نفسه بأن ادعى عليه رجل ديناً . عتقاً وعبده في صحته فقال في مرضه صدقتما فإن يعتق العبد ويسعى في قيمته فكذا هذا وقضية الدفع أن يبطل العتق في المرض أصلاً إلا أنه بعد وقوعه لا يحتمل البطلان فيدفع من حيث المعنى بإيجاب السعاية عليه، ولأن الدين أسبق فإنه لا مانع له من الاستناد فيستند إلى حالة الصحة ولا يمكن استناد العتق إلى تلك الحالة لأن الدين يمنع العتق في حال المرض مجاناً فتجب السعاية، وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا مات وترك ألف درهم فقال رجل لي على الميت ألف درهم دين وقال آخر هذا الألف كان لي عنده وديعة فعنده الوديعة أقوى وعندهما سواء؛ كذا في الهداية.
Book of Wills, Chapter on Manumission in Sickness and Bequest of Manumission. His value and it is given to the creditor; this is according to Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is freed and does not work for anything, because the debt and manumission in health appear together through the heir's attestation in one statement, so it is as if both occurred together or that was established by evidence, and manumission in health does not necessitate working even if the manumitter has a debt. And he (Abu Hanifa) has that acknowledgment of debt is stronger than acknowledgment of manumission, and for this reason his acknowledgment of debt is considered from the entire property, and of manumission from the third, and the stronger overcomes the weaker; so it becomes like the testator himself claiming that a man claimed a debt and a manumission of his slave in his health, and he said in his sickness: you both spoke truthfully, then the slave is freed and works for his value; so this is like that. And the consequence of overcoming is that the manumission in sickness is nullified originally, but since after occurrence it cannot be nullified, it is overcome in meaning by imposing working on him. And because the debt is prior, there is no obstacle to its attribution, so it attributes to the state of health, and the manumission cannot be attributed to that state because debt prevents manumission in sickness gratuitously, so working becomes obligatory. And upon this difference, if he dies leaving a thousand dirhams, and a man says: I have a debt of a thousand dirhams against the deceased, and another says: this thousand was a deposit with me, then according to him (Abu Hanifa) the deposit is stronger, and according to them (the Sahibayn) they are equal; so in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The issue: a terminally ill person acknowledges a debt and also manumits a slave. Abu Hanifa rules that the manumission is valid but the slave must work (sa'y) to pay his value to the creditors, because the acknowledgment of debt is stronger—it comes from the entire estate while manumission comes only from the third. The Sahibayn hold that the slave is freed without any obligation to work, because both acts occur simultaneously in the same speech, and in health such simultaneity would not impose working. Abu Hanifa rebuts by analogizing to a case where in health both debt and manumission are acknowledged: there the slave must work. The underlying principle is that the stronger (debt) overrides the weaker (manumission). The passage also notes that if a man claims debt and another claims deposit, Abu Hanifa considers the deposit stronger, while the Sahibayn consider them equal. This ruling is recorded in al-Hidayah as the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
السعاية (al-sa'y): The obligation of a manumitted slave to work to pay his value to creditors.
الإقرار بالدين (al-iqrar bi al-dayn): Acknowledgment of debt by the testator, which is stronger than acknowledgment of manumission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when a terminally ill person acknowledges a debt and manumits a slave, what is the status of the slave?
A) The slave is freed without any obligation.
B) The slave is freed but must work to pay his value.
C) The manumission is invalid because of the debt.
D) The slave remains a slave until the debt is paid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when debt and manumission conflict in terminal illness, the slave is freed but must perform sa'y because debt acknowledgment is stronger.

Strength of Deposit Claim vs. Debt Claim in Hanafi Law
Critical refinement on wadi'ah vs debt strength

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the strength of a deposit claim compared to a debt claim in the context of heirs' acknowledgments, and explain the reasoning based on dhimmah vs. 'ayn.

Core Idea
The deposit claim is stronger than the debt claim according to the Sahibayn, contrary to al-Hidayah's report, because the deposit pertains to the 'ayn while debt pertains to the dhimmah.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, we encounter a critical refinement of a statement in al-Hidayah regarding the relative strength of a deposit claim versus a debt claim when acknowledged by heirs. The authors of al-Nihayah and al-Kafi correct the earlier work, attributing the stronger position for deposit to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), not to Abu Hanifa. Understanding this correction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of claim priority in inheritance cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of the correction
The passage cites al-Nihayah, which attributes to Fakhr al-Islam and al-Kisani a correction of al-Hidayah.
2
State the corrected position
According to the Sahibayn, the deposit claim is stronger than the debt claim; according to Abu Hanifa, the debt claim is stronger.
3
Understand the reasoning
The testator's own acknowledgment of debt affects the dhimmah, while acknowledgment of deposit pertains to the 'ayn; however, when heirs acknowledge, both debt and deposit pertain to the 'ayn, so deposit is stronger.
4
Note the agreement from al-Kafi
The author of al-Kafi also weakens al-Hidayah's statement and considers the correct view opposite.
5
Practical consequence
The mufta bihi position is that of the Sahibayn, so in practice deposit claims take priority over debt claims when acknowledged by heirs.
This is the relied-upon view for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في النهاية : ذكر فخر الإسلام والكيساني الوديعة أقوى عندهما لا عنده عكس ما ذكر في الهداية بخلاف إقرار المورث نفسه لأن إقراره بالدين يثبت في الذمة وبالوديعة يتناول العين فيكون صاحبها أولى لتعلق حقه بها، وإقرار الوراث بالدين يتناول عين التركة كإقراره بالوديعة يتناول العين، وصاحب الكافي ضعف أيضاً ما ذكره صاحب الهداية وجعل الأصح خلافه. وفي الفتاوى سأل أبو القاسم عمن أوصى إلى رجل فقال إذا أدرك ولدي فأعتق عبدي هذا وأعطه مائتي درهم والعبد معه وهو في لعب منه فرضي العبد أن يعتق في الحال ولا يطلب منه شيئاً قال : لا يجوز عتق العبد قبل الوقت الذي أقر به الوصي. وسأل أبو بكر عمن أوصى بعتق عبده وأوصى له بصلة وللعبد متاع وكسوة من سيده وهبة وهبها له غير المولى قال : لا يكون للعبد من ذلك المتاع إلا ما يواري عورته.
And said in al-Nihayah: Fakhr al-Islam and al-Kisani mentioned that the deposit is stronger according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) not according to him (Abu Hanifa), contrary to what was mentioned in al-Hidayah, unlike the testator's own acknowledgment, because his acknowledgment of debt is established in the dhimmah, and of deposit pertains to the ‘ayn, so its owner is more entitled due to his right attaching to it. And the acknowledgment of heirs of debt pertains to the ‘ayn of the estate just as his acknowledgment of deposit pertains to the ‘ayn. And the author of al-Kafi also weakened what the author of al-Hidayah mentioned and made the correct view its opposite. And in al-Fatawa: Abu al-Qasim asked about one who appointed a wasi who said: when my son reaches maturity, free this slave of mine and give him two hundred dirhams; the slave was with him and he was playing with him, and the slave agreed to be freed immediately and not ask for anything. He said: It is not permissible to free the slave before the time stipulated by the wasi. And Abu Bakr asked about one who bequeathed the manumission of his slave and bequeathed him a gift, and for the slave there was property and clothing from his master and a gift given to him by someone other than the master. He said: The slave does not get from that property except what covers his private parts.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage consists of two parts. First, a critical refinement: al-Nihayah corrects a statement in al-Hidayah regarding the strength of a deposit claim versus a debt claim in inheritance. According to Fakhr al-Islam and al-Kisani, the deposit is stronger according to the Sahibayn, not according to Abu Hanifa. This contradicts what al-Hidayah reported. The author of al-Kafi also considered the correct view to be the opposite of al-Hidayah. The reasoning: the testator's own acknowledgment of debt affects the dhimmah, while deposit affects the ‘ayn; but when heirs acknowledge debt, it pertains to the ‘ayn, similar to deposit. Second, two fatwas: (1) If a wasi is instructed to free a slave when the testator's son reaches maturity, the slave cannot be freed earlier even if the slave consents, because the wasi must follow the stipulated time. (2) If a slave is bequeathed manumission and some property from the master and a gift from a third party, the slave only gets enough clothing to cover his private parts from the property; other bequests to the slave are separate.

Key Terms
الوديعة (al-wadi‘ah): A deposit; a claim that an item held by the deceased was a deposit belonging to the claimant.
الذمة (al-dhimmah): Legal personality or liability; the capacity to owe debts.
العين (al-‘ayn): A specific physical asset or item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correction in al-Nihayah, who holds that the deposit claim is stronger when acknowledged by heirs?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)
C) Both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
D) Neither; the views are equal

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn hold that a deposit claim is stronger than a debt claim when acknowledged by heirs, because the deposit attaches to the 'ayn, unlike the testator's own acknowledgment which affects the dhimmah.

Fatwas on Manumission Timing and Slave's Entitlement from Bequest
Two fatwas on manumission and bequest to a slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a wasi must follow the testator's timing for manumission, and identify the limit of a slave's entitlement from property bequeathed to him.

Core Idea
A wasi cannot free a slave before the specified time even with the slave's consent; a slave given property in a bequest only gets enough to cover his private parts.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents two fatwas from al-Fatawa. The first concerns a wasi who was instructed to free a slave when the testator's son reaches adulthood. The slave requests early manumission and waives compensation, but the fatwa rules it impermissible. The second fatwa deals with a slave who was bequeathed manumission and some property; the ruling limits his entitlement from that property to only what covers his private parts. These rulings illustrate the strict adherence to the testator's wishes and the principle that a slave cannot own property beyond basic necessities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first fatwa scenario
A wasi is appointed by a testator with instructions to free a specific slave when the testator's son reaches maturity. The slave is present and playing; he agrees to be freed immediately and asks for nothing.
2
State the ruling on early manumission
It is not permissible (la yajuz) for the wasi to free the slave before the specified time, even with the slave's consent. The wasi must adhere to the testator's timing.
The slave's consent is irrelevant because the wasi's authority is limited by the will.
3
Identify the second fatwa scenario
A testator bequeaths manumission of his slave and also bequeaths a gift (silah) to the slave. Additionally, the slave has property and clothing from his master and a gift from a non-master (third party).
4
State the ruling on the slave's entitlement
The slave does not get any of that property (the property from the master) except what covers his private parts (i.e., minimal clothing). The other bequests (gift from testator and gift from third party) are separate.
The ruling implies that a slave cannot own property beyond basic necessities; any excess belongs to the master.
5
Understand the underlying principles
The wasi's duty is to execute the will exactly. A slave's legal capacity to own property is limited; he cannot own more than his basic needs, as he himself is property.
These principles protect the testator's intent and maintain the legal status of slaves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في النهاية : ذكر فخر الإسلام والكيساني الوديعة أقوى عندهما لا عنده عكس ما ذكر في الهداية بخلاف إقرار المورث نفسه لأن إقراره بالدين يثبت في الذمة وبالوديعة يتناول العين فيكون صاحبها أولى لتعلق حقه بها، وإقرار الوراث بالدين يتناول عين التركة كإقراره بالوديعة يتناول العين، وصاحب الكافي ضعف أيضاً ما ذكره صاحب الهداية وجعل الأصح خلافه. وفي الفتاوى سأل أبو القاسم عمن أوصى إلى رجل فقال إذا أدرك ولدي فأعتق عبدي هذا وأعطه مائتي درهم والعبد معه وهو في لعب منه فرضي العبد أن يعتق في الحال ولا يطلب منه شيئاً قال : لا يجوز عتق العبد قبل الوقت الذي أقر به الوصي. وسأل أبو بكر عمن أوصى بعتق عبده وأوصى له بصلة وللعبد متاع وكسوة من سيده وهبة وهبها له غير المولى قال : لا يكون للعبد من ذلك المتاع إلا ما يواري عورته.
And said in al-Nihayah: Fakhr al-Islam and al-Kisani mentioned that the deposit is stronger according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) not according to him (Abu Hanifa), contrary to what was mentioned in al-Hidayah, unlike the testator's own acknowledgment, because his acknowledgment of debt is established in the dhimmah, and of deposit pertains to the ‘ayn, so its owner is more entitled due to his right attaching to it. And the acknowledgment of heirs of debt pertains to the ‘ayn of the estate just as his acknowledgment of deposit pertains to the ‘ayn. And the author of al-Kafi also weakened what the author of al-Hidayah mentioned and made the correct view its opposite. And in al-Fatawa: Abu al-Qasim asked about one who appointed a wasi who said: when my son reaches maturity, free this slave of mine and give him two hundred dirhams; the slave was with him and he was playing with him, and the slave agreed to be freed immediately and not ask for anything. He said: It is not permissible to free the slave before the time stipulated by the wasi. And Abu Bakr asked about one who bequeathed the manumission of his slave and bequeathed him a gift, and for the slave there was property and clothing from his master and a gift given to him by someone other than the master. He said: The slave does not get from that property except what covers his private parts.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage consists of two parts. First, a critical refinement: al-Nihayah corrects a statement in al-Hidayah regarding the strength of a deposit claim versus a debt claim in inheritance. According to Fakhr al-Islam and al-Kisani, the deposit is stronger according to the Sahibayn, not according to Abu Hanifa. This contradicts what al-Hidayah reported. (2) If a slave is bequeathed manumission and some property from the master and a gift from a third party, the slave only gets enough clothing to cover his private parts from the property; other bequests to the slave are separate.

Key Terms
الوصي (al-wasi): The executor appointed in a will to carry out the testator's instructions.
العتق (al-‘itq): Manumission; the act of freeing a slave.
المتاع (al-mata‘): Property or possessions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
