Priority of Bequests: Obligatory vs Voluntary and Specific vs Non-Specific
Systematic exposition of priority order among bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule that obligatory bequests override voluntary ones, identify the three intra-Hanafi positions on the order among obligatory bequests (Hajj, Zakat, expiation), and apply the priority hierarchy to a given set of bequests.

Core Idea
Obligatory bequests always precede voluntary ones; among obligations, Abu Hanifa orders Hajj then Zakat then expiation.

When an estate's third is insufficient to cover all bequests and heirs do not consent, a priority system determines which bequests are fulfilled first. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq systematically lays out the Hanafi rules, distinguishing between obligations owed to Allah and voluntary acts, and between specific and non-specific designations. It also records important intra-Hanafi differences on the order among obligatory acts.

Guided Path
1
State the overarching principle
Identify the general rule: obligations (Hajj, Zakat, expiations) take precedence over voluntary acts regardless of the testator's order.
The principle is based on the importance of obligations.
2
Categorize the bequests
Determine whether a bequest is for people or for Allah, obligatory or voluntary, specific (mu'ayyan) or non-specific.
Specificity affects whether proportional sharing applies.
3
Analyze the hierarchy among obligatory acts
Note the three reported views: Abu Hanifa (Hajj, then Zakat, then expiation), Abu Yusuf (Zakat always first), and Abu Bakr al-Balkhi (follow testator's order).
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's order.
4
Apply the rules for mixed cases
When obligatory and voluntary bequests are mixed, obligations take precedence. If both are obligatory, follow the hierarchy; if both are voluntary and specific, proportional sharing; if non-specific, follow the testator's order.
The text provides specific examples like manumission vs charity.
5
Consider the consequences of inability
If a specific voluntary bequest becomes impossible (e.g., slave dies), the other specific voluntary gets the full share.
This shows how validity and impossibility affect distribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الله: ( وبحقوق الله قدمت الفرائض وإن أخرها كالحج والزكاة والكفارات) لأن الفرض أهم من النفل والظاهر منه البداية بالأهم. قال في الأصل : إذا اجتمعت الوصايا فإن كان ثلث المال يوفي بالكل أو أجازت الورثة الوصايا بأسرها نفذت الوصايا بأسرها، وإن لم تجز الورثة الوصايا فإن كانت الوصايا كلها للعباد يقدم الأقوى فالأقوى وإلا بدئ بما بدأ به كما سيأتي في القول التي بعدها فإن كان في الوصايا عتق قدم على غيره، وإن استوت في القوة فإنهم يتحاصون فيها بأن يضرب بقدر حقه في الثلث وقد تقدم وإن كانت الوصايا كلها الله تعالى إن كان النوافل كلها عيناً بأن أوصى أن يتصدق بمائة على فقير بعينه وأوصى بأن يعتق نسمة بعينها تطوعاً فإنهما يتحاصان ولا يبدأ بما بدأ به الميت، فإن كان صاحب النسمة لا يبيع النسمة بما يخصها أو ماتت النسمة في يد صاحبها حتى وقع العجز عن تنفيذ الوصية فإنه يكمل وصية الموصى له بالمائة لأن صحة الوصية للعبد صحت ثم بطلت لأنا نعتبر البطلان بوقوع اليأس عن تنفيذ الوصية للعبد، فأما إذا كانت الوصايا كلها فرائض وقد استوت في الوكالة وليس معها وصية للمعين بأن أوصى بأداء الزكاة وبحجة الإسلام وبأن يعتق عنه عبد عن كفارة يمين فإن على قول الفقيه أبي بكر البلخي يبدأ بما بدأ به الميت بخلاف ما لو أوصى بعتق في كفارة فطر فإنه يبدأ بكفارة الفطر أو القتل وإن أخرها الميت، وقد روى أبو يوسف في الأمالي عن أبي حنيفة والحسن بن زياد عن أبي حنيفة أنه يبدأ بالحج ثم بالزكاة ثم بالعتق عن كفارة اليمين سواء بدأ بالحج أو أخر. وفي الكافي : وروي عن أبي يوسف أنه يقدم عليه الزكاة بكل حال، ثم يقدم الحج على الكفارات، وكفارة الظهار والقتل واليمين مقدم على صدقة الفطر وصدقة الفطر مقدمة على الأضحية، وعلى هذا القياس يقدم بعض الواجبات كالنذر يقدم على الأضحية، وما ليس بواجب يقدم منه ما قدمه الموصي فإن أوصى بعتق في كفارة قتل أو كفارة يمين أو ظهار يبدأ بكفارة القتل وإن أخرها الميت وإن كانت الكفارة كفارة اليمين ساوت كفارة القتل في القوة والوكالة بخلاف ما إذا أوصى بالعتق في كفارة يمين وبالعتق في كفارة ظهار وبكفارة جزاء الصيد وبكفارة الحلف في الأذى فإنه يبدأ بما بدأ به الميت. وروى القاضي الإمام الجليل في شرح مختصر الطحاوي عن أصحابنا أنه يبدأ بالزكاة ثم بالحج ثم بالعتق عن الكفارة. هذا كله إذا لم يكن مع الفرائض نفل فإن كان النفل بغير العين بأن أوصى بأن يحج عنه حجة الإسلام ويعتق عنه نسمة لا بعينها تطوعاً فالفرض أولى وإن أخره الميت، وهذا استحسان والقياس أن يبدأ بالنفل إذا كان الميت بدأ بالنفل، فأما إذا الفرائض عين بأن أوصى بحجة الإسلام وبأن يعتق عنه معين يتحاصان سواء بدأ مع بالعتق أو أخر. هذه جملة ما أورده الشيخ الإمام المعروف بخواهر زاده. وذكر الشيخ الإمام الزاهد أحمد الطواف في شرحه ويسن أن بعد الفرائض تقدم الكفارة على النذور. وفي الذخيرة : تقدم كفارة القتل على غيرها من الكفارات وعلى النذور، وتقدم النذور على الأضحية وصدقة الفطو، وتقدم صدقة الفطر على الأضحية لأنها واجبة بالاتفاق. وإن كان مع الفرض وصية بعتق ونفل ليس بمعين بأن أوصى لرجل بمائة درهم وأوصى بعتق نسمة لا بعينها فإنه يجب التوزيع والمحاصة لتظهر صحة المعين، فإذا ظهر صحة المعين من الثلث خرج المعين عن الوسط بقي بعد هذا فرض ونفل وليس بعين فيقدم الفرض، فإن بقي بعد الفرض شيء ولا يأخذ بذلك نسمة قالوا يصرف إلى الموصى له بالعين. وفي فتاوى الخلاصة : فإن كان مع شيء من هذه الوصايا حق الله نحو أن يقول ثلث مالي في الحج والزكاة والكفارة ولزيد قسم على أربعة أسهم. وفي فتاوى أبي الليث : إذا قال أخرجوا من مالي عشرين ألفاً فأعطوا فلاناً كذا وفلاناً كذا حتى بلغ أحد شعر ألفاً ثم قال والباقي كان
Allah said: 'And with the rights of Allah, the obligatory acts are given precedence even if he delayed them, like Hajj, Zakat, and expiations.' Because the obligatory is more important than the voluntary, and the apparent is to start with the most important. He said in al-Asl: When wills are combined, if the third of the estate suffices for all or the heirs permit all wills, then all wills are executed. If the heirs do not permit, then if all wills are for people, the strongest is given precedence, otherwise start with what he started with as will come in the following statements. If there is manumission among the wills, it is given precedence over others. If they are equal in strength, then they share proportionally by striking a portion of his right in the third, as previously. And if all wills are for Allah, if the voluntary acts are all specific ('ayn) such as bequeathing charity of one hundred to a specific poor person and bequeathing manumission of a specific slave voluntarily, then they share proportionally and do not start with what the deceased started. If the owner of the slave does not sell the slave for his share, or the slave dies in the hand of its owner such that there is hopelessness of executing the will, then the will for the one hundred is completed because the validity of the will for the slave was established then voided, for we consider voidance upon hopelessness of execution. As for when the wills are all obligatory and are equal in guardianship (wakalah) and there is no will for a specific thing, such as bequeathing payment of Zakat, Hajj of Islam, and manumission of a slave for expiation of an oath, then according to al-Faqih Abu Bakr al-Balkhi, he starts with what the deceased started, unlike if he bequeathed manumission for expiation of Ramadan's fast-breaking, then he starts with expiation of fast-breaking or killing even if the deceased delayed it. And Abu Yusuf reported in al-Amali from Abu Hanifa and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa that he starts with Hajj, then Zakat, then manumission for expiation of oath, whether he started with Hajj or delayed. And in al-Kafi: It is reported from Abu Yusuf that he gives Zakat precedence in every case, then Hajj over expiations, and expiation of zihar, killing, and oath are given precedence over Sadaqat al-Fitr, and Sadaqat al-Fitr is given precedence over Udhiyah. Upon this analogy, some obligatory acts like a vow are given precedence over Udhiyah. And what is not obligatory, from it what the testator started with is given precedence. If he bequeathed manumission for expiation of killing or oath or zihar, he starts with expiation of killing even if the deceased delayed it, and if the expiation is for an oath, it equals expiation of killing in strength and guardianship, unlike if he bequeathed manumission for expiation of an oath and manumission for expiation of zihar and expiation of hunting compensation and expiation of swearing in harm, then he starts with what the deceased started. And the great judge in his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi narrated from our companions that he starts with Zakat, then Hajj, then manumission for expiation. All this if there is no voluntary act with the obligatory ones. If the voluntary is non-specific, such as bequeathing Hajj of Islam and manumission of a non-specific slave voluntarily, then the obligatory is better even if the deceased delayed it; this is istihsan, and by qiyas he would start with the voluntary if the deceased started with it. As for when the obligatory acts are specific, such as bequeathing Hajj of Islam and manumission of a specific slave, they share proportionally whether he started with manumission or delayed. This is the summary of what the Shaykh Imam known as Khawahirzadah presented. And the Shaykh Imam al-Zahid Ahmad al-Tawwaf mentioned in his commentary: and it is recommended that after the obligatory acts, expiation is given precedence over vows. And in al-Dhakhirah: expiation of killing is given precedence over other expiations and vows, and vows are given precedence over Udhiyah and Sadaqat al-Fitr, and Sadaqat al-Fitr is given precedence over Udhiyah because it is obligatory by consensus. And if there is with the obligatory a will of manumission and a non-specific voluntary, such as bequeathing to a man one hundred dirhams and bequeathing manumission of a non-specific slave, then distribution and proportional sharing are necessary to manifest the validity of the specific. When the validity of the specific appears from the third, the specific leaves the middle, and after that remains an obligatory and a voluntary that are not specific; so the obligatory is given precedence. If something remains after the obligatory and it does not take a slave, they said it is given to the specific legatee. And in Fatawa al-Khulasah: if there is with some of these wills a right of Allah, such as saying: one third of my wealth is for Hajj, Zakat, and expiation, and for Zayd a share into four parts. And in Fatawa Abi al-Layth: if he said: take out twenty thousand from my wealth and give so-and-so this, and so-and-so that, until he reached one ashrafi, then said: and the remaining was...
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This is a comprehensive passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq detailing the order of priority among bequests when the third of the estate is insufficient and heirs do not approve. It begins with a general principle: rights of Allah (obligatory acts like Hajj, Zakat, expiations) are given precedence over voluntary acts, because the obligatory is more important. The text then distinguishes cases: (1) Wills for people: the strongest are prioritized; if strength is equal, they share proportionally; manumission is given precedence. (2) Wills for Allah: if all are voluntary and specific ('ayn), they share proportionally regardless of order. If one specific voluntary becomes impossible, the other gets the full share. (3) When all wills are obligatory (like Zakat, Hajj, expiatory manumission), there is dispute: Abu Bakr al-Balkhi says follow the testator's order; Abu Hanifa (in one narration) puts Hajj first, then Zakat, then manumission; Abu Yusuf gives Zakat precedence always. The hierarchy among expiations and other acts is detailed: killing expiation > other expiations > vows > Sadaqat al-Fitr > Udhiyah. Non-obligatory bequests follow the testator's order. The passage also covers cases where obligatory and voluntary are mixed, and specific vs non-specific distinctions. It concludes with references to Fatawa al-Khulasah and Fatawa Abi al-Layth, though the latter is cut off.

Key Terms
الفرائض (al-fara'id): Obligatory acts of worship that a person owes to Allah, such as Hajj, Zakat, and expiations.
النفل (al-nafl): Voluntary acts of worship that are not obligatory, such as supererogatory charity or manumission.
المعين (al-mu‘ayyan): A specific item or person designated in the will, e.g., a specific slave or specific charity recipient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the narration from Abu Hanifa in al-Amali, what is the correct order of priority among these obligatory bequests: (1) Manumission for expiation of oath, (2) Zakat, (3) Hajj?
A) Hajj, then Zakat, then manumission.
B) Zakat, then Hajj, then manumission.
C) Manumission, then Hajj, then Zakat.
D) Follow the testator's order.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, obligatory bequests always override voluntary ones; among obligations, the mufta bihi order is Hajj, then Zakat, then expiation, though other views exist within the school.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Prioritizing Obligatory Bequests: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ordering obligatory bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that obligatory bequests take precedence over voluntary ones and identify the differing opinions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the order of Hajj and zakat in a will.

Core Idea
Obligations in a will always take precedence over voluntary acts, even if the testator ordered them later.

When a testator leaves a will that includes both obligatory acts (like missed zakat or Hajj) and voluntary acts, but the estate cannot cover all, the obligation is given priority. However, when all bequests are obligatory, Hanafi scholars differed on the order, with Abu Hanifa preferring Hajj first and Abu Yusuf preferring zakat first. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the underlying principle of istihsan.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on obligation vs. voluntary
Identify the general ruling: obligatory bequests (fard/wajib) take precedence over voluntary (nafl) even if the testator began with the voluntary. This is based on istihsan.
Keep in mind that the qiyas would suggest following the testator's order, but istihsan overrides.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf when only obligations exist
When all bequests are obligatory (e.g., zakat, Hajj, expiations) and the third is insufficient, scholars differ on the order. Abu Bakr al-Balkhi says follow the testator's order; Abu Hanifa says Hajj first, then zakat, then expiations; Abu Yusuf says zakat first.
The dispute is reported from Abu Hanifa via two narrations: one from Hasan ibn Ziyad and another from Abu Yusuf in al-Amali.
3
Follow Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa (according to one narration) gives priority to Hajj because it is the pillar of Islam and its obligation is original, while zakat is also original but Hajj is seen as more pressing for the deceased.
The reasoning is not explicitly given in the passage but inferred from the order.
4
Follow Abu Yusuf's reasoning
Abu Yusuf gives priority to zakat because it involves the rights of the poor and is more immediately owed, while Hajj can be performed by someone else or made up later.
This is the view reported in al-Kafi and later preferred by many scholars.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: If the third is insufficient, under Abu Hanifa's view, Hajj would be performed fully and zakat partially or not at all; under Abu Yusuf's view, zakat would be fulfilled first.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is Abu Yusuf's view: zakat first, then Hajj, then expiations.

Source Text

كتاب الوصايا باب العتق في المرض والوصية بالعتق

عن تنفيذ الوصية فإنه يكمل وصية الموصى له بالمائة لأن صحة الوصية للعبد صحت ثم بطلت لأنا نعتبر البطلان بوقوع اليأس عن تنفيذ الوصية للعبد، فأما إذا كانت الوصايا كلها فرائض وقد استوت في الوكالة وليس معها وصية للمعين بأن أوصى بأداء الزكاة وبحجة الإسلام وبأن يعتق عنه عبد عن كفارة يمين فإن على قول الفقيه أبي بكر البلخي يبدأ بما بدأ به الميت بخلاف ما لو أوصى بعتق في كفارة فطر فإنه يبدأ بكفارة الفطر أو القتل وإن أخرها الميت، وقد روى أبو يوسف في الأمالي عن أبي حنيفة والحسن بن زياد عن أبي حنيفة أنه يبدأ بالحج ثم بالزكاة ثم بالعتق عن كفارة اليمين سواء بدأ بالحج أو أخر. وفي الكافي : وروي عن أبي يوسف أنه يقدم عليه الزكاة بكل حال، ثم يقدم الحج على الكفارات، وكفارة الظهار والقتل واليمين مقدم على صدقة الفطر وصدقة الفطر مقدمة على الأضحية، وعلى هذا القياس يقدم بعض الواجبات كالنذر يقدم على الأضحية، وما ليس بواجب يقدم منه ما قدمه الموصي فإن أوصى بعتق في كفارة قتل أو كفارة يمين أو ظهار يبدأ بكفارة القتل وإن أخرها الميت وإن كانت الكفارة كفارة اليمين ساوت كفارة القتل في القوة والوكالة بخلاف ما إذا أوصى بالعتق في كفارة يمين وبالعتق في كفارة ظهار وبكفارة جزاء الصيد وبكفارة الحلف في الأذى فإنه يبدأ بما بدأ به الميت. وروى القاضي الإمام الجليل في شرح مختصر الطحاوي عن أصحابنا أنه يبدأ بالزكاة ثم بالحج ثم بالعتق عن الكفارة. هذا كله إذا لم يكن مع الفرائض نفل فإن كان النفل بغير العين بأن أوصى بأن يحج عنه حجة الإسلام ويعتق عنه نسمة لا بعينها تطوعاً فالفرض أولى وإن أخره الميت، وهذا استحسان والقياس أن يبدأ بالنفل إذا كان الميت بدأ بالنفل، فأما إذا الفرائض عين بأن أوصى بحجة الإسلام وبأن يعتق عنه معين يتحاصان سواء بدأ مع بالعتق أو أخر. هذه جملة ما أورده الشيخ الإمام المعروف بخواهر زاده. وذكر الشيخ الإمام الزاهد أحمد الطواف في شرحه ويسن أن بعد الفرائض تقدم الكفارة على النذور. وفي الذخيرة : تقدم كفارة القتل على غيرها من الكفارات وعلى النذور، وتقدم النذور على الأضحية وصدقة الفطو، وتقدم صدقة الفطر على الأضحية لأنها واجبة بالاتفاق. وإن كان مع الفرض وصية بعتق ونفل ليس بمعين بأن أوصى لرجل بمائة درهم وأوصى بعتق نسمة لا بعينها فإنه يجب التوزيع والمحاصة لتظهر صحة المعين، فإذا ظهر صحة المعين من الثلث خرج المعين عن الوسط بقي بعد هذا فرض ونفل وليس بعين فيقدم الفرض، فإن بقي بعد الفرض شيء ولا يأخذ بذلك نسمة قالوا يصرف إلى الموصى له بالعين. وفي فتاوى الخلاصة : فإن كان مع شيء من هذه الوصايا حق الله نحو أن يقول ثلث مالي في الحج والزكاة والكفارة ولزيد قسم على أربعة أسهم. وفي فتاوى أبي الليث : إذا قال أخرجوا من مالي عشرين ألفاً فأعطوا فلاناً كذا وفلاناً كذا حتى بلغ أحد عشر ألفاً ثم قال والباقي كان

فإذا ثلث ماله تسعة آلاف درهم والورثة لم يجيزوا فإنه ينفذ من وصية كل واحد منهم تسعة أجزاء من عشرين جزءاً ويبطل من وصية كل واحد منهم أحد عشر جزءاً من عشرين جزءاً أو يجعل قوله والباقي للفقراء بعدما سمى عشرين ألفاً وذلك لكل واحد ذلك نصيبهما حتى بلغ أحد عشر ألفاً فإنه قال أعطوا ثلث مالي لفلان كذا حتى بلغ أحد عشر ألفاً قال وأعطوا الباقي للفقراء، فإذا بلغ ماله تسعة آلاف أو أكثر إلى أحد شيء للفقراء ويعطى كل واحد من أصحاب الوصايا حصة كاملة إن كان الثلث أحد عشر ألفاً، ثم يعطى كل واحد منهم تسعة أجزاء أحد عشر جزءاً . من وصيته ويبطل سهمان من أحد عشر . وفي الواقعات للناطفي : الواجبات في الوصايا على أربع مراتب : ما أوجبه الله تعالى أبداً كالزكاة والحج والثاني ما أوجبه على العبد بسبب من جهته ككفارة اليمين وكفارة الظهار وكفارة القتل والثالث ما أوجبه على نفسه من غير ثبوته عليه بالنذر كقوله علي صدقة أو عتق وما أشبهه والرابع التطوع كقوله تصدقوا عني بعد وفاتي. وقد اختلفت الرواية في الحج مع الزكاة فعن أبي حنيفة في المجرد أنه حجة الإسلام وإن أخر الحج عن الزكاة في الوصية لفظاً وفي نوادر ابن رستم: إذا أوصى بالزكاة والحج والفرض يبدأ بما بدأ به الميت فعلى هذا الترتيب الذي بيناه يجب إبفاؤها مرتبة إذا لم يف ثلث ماله بذلك كله . تقدم
The Book of Wills, Chapter of Manumission in Illness and Bequest of Manumission. ... Regarding the execution of the bequest, he completes the bequest of the legatee of one hundred because the validity of the bequest for the slave was established then voided because we consider the voidance upon the occurrence of despair from executing the bequest for the slave. But if all the bequests are obligations and they are equal in agency and there is no bequest for a specific person, such as bequeathing the performance of zakat, Hajj al-Islam, and that a slave be freed for him as expiation for an oath, then according to Abu Bakr al-Balkhi, he begins with what the deceased began with, unlike if he bequeathed manumission as expiation for breaking fast, then he begins with expiation for breaking fast or killing even if the deceased delayed it. Abu Yusuf narrated in al-Amali from Abu Hanifa, and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa, that he begins with Hajj, then zakat, then manumission as expiation for an oath, whether he began with Hajj or delayed. In al-Kafi: it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he gives priority to zakat over it in every case, then he gives priority to Hajj over expiations, and expiation for zihar, killing, and oath is given priority over sadaqat al-fitr, and sadaqat al-fitr is given priority over the udhiya, and by this analogy some obligations are given priority, such as the nadhr is given priority over the udhiya, and what is not obligatory, from it he gives priority to what the testator gave priority. If he bequeaths manumission as expiation for killing or oath or zihar, he begins with expiation for killing even if the deceased delayed it, and if the expiation is for an oath, it equals expiation for killing in strength and agency, unlike if he bequeathed manumission as expiation for an oath and manumission as expiation for zihar and expiation for the penalty of hunting and expiation for swearing to harm, then he begins with what the deceased began with. The noble judge Imam narrated in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi from our companions that he begins with zakat, then Hajj, then manumission as expiation. This is all if there is no voluntary bequest with the obligations. If the voluntary bequest is not specific, such as bequeathing that Hajj al-Islam be performed for him and that a non-specific soul be freed for him voluntarily, then the obligatory is better even if the deceased delayed it, and this is istihsan, and the analogy is that he begins with the voluntary if the deceased began with the voluntary. But if the obligations are specific, such as bequeathing Hajj al-Islam and that a specific slave be freed for him, they share proportionally whether he began with manumission or delayed. This is the summary of what the Shaykh Imam known as Khawahir Zada mentioned. And the Shaykh Imam al-Zahid Ahmad al-Tawwaf mentioned in his commentary: It is recommended that after the obligations, expiations be given priority over nadhrs. In al-Dhakhira: Expiation for killing is given priority over other expiations and over nadhrs, and nadhrs are given priority over the udhiya and sadaqat al-fitr, and sadaqat al-fitr is given priority over the udhiya because it is obligatory by consensus. If there is with the obligatory a bequest of manumission and a non-specific voluntary bequest, such as bequeathing to a man one hundred dirhams and bequeathing the freeing of a non-specific soul, then distribution and sharing must be made to establish the validity of the specific. When the validity of the specific from the third is established, the specific leaves the middle, after that there remains an obligatory and a voluntary that is not specific, so the obligatory is given priority. If something remains after the obligatory and it does not take that soul, they said it is spent on the specific legatee. In Fatawa al-Khulasa: If there is with any of these bequests a right of Allah, such as he says 'one third of my wealth is for Hajj, zakat, and expiation' and for Zayd a share of four shares. In Fatawa Abi al-Layth: If he says 'take out twenty thousand from my wealth and give to so-and-so such and such and to so-and-so such and such until it reaches eleven thousand, then he said 'and the rest is...' Then if his third is nine thousand dirhams and the heirs did not approve, then nine-twentieths of each one's bequest is executed and eleven-twentieths is voided, or his saying 'and the rest is for the poor' after naming twenty thousand, and that for each one is their share until it reaches eleven thousand. If he said 'give one third of my wealth to so-and-so such and such until it reaches eleven thousand' he said 'and give the rest to the poor', then if his wealth is nine thousand or more up to something, for the poor, and each of the testators is given a full share if the third is eleven thousand, then each of them is given nine parts of eleven parts from his bequest and two parts out of eleven are voided. In al-Waqi'at al-Natifi: The obligations in bequests are of four ranks: what Allah Almighty has made obligatory absolutely, like zakat and Hajj; second, what He made obligatory upon the servant due to his own action, like expiation for oath, expiation for zihar, and expiation for killing; third, what he made obligatory upon himself without its being established on him by nadhr, like his saying 'upon me is charity or manumission' and the like; fourth, voluntary, like his saying 'give charity on my behalf after my death'. And the narration has differed regarding Hajj with zakat: from Abu Hanifa in al-Mujarrad that it is Hajj al-Islam even if he delayed Hajj after zakat in the wording of the will, and in Nawadir Ibn Rustam: if he bequeaths zakat and Hajj and the obligation, he begins with what the deceased began with. So according to this order we have mentioned, they must be fulfilled in order if his third does not suffice for all of that. The text said.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of Hanafi rulings on prioritizing bequests when the testator's estate is insufficient to fulfill all of them. The discussion covers both obligatory (fard/wajib) and voluntary (nafl) bequests, as well as the differences among Hanafi imams and later scholars. The author begins by citing the opinion of Abu Bakr al-Balkhi that when all bequests are obligations and no specific bequest is involved, one begins with what the testator started with. However, he then reports from Abu Yusuf and Hasan ibn Ziyad that Abu Hanifa gives priority to Hajj over zakat and then over expiation for an oath, regardless of the order in the will. Abu Yusuf's own view, as reported in al-Kafi, is that zakat is always given priority first, then Hajj, then expiations. The passage then ranks various expiations: kaffarat for killing, zihar, and oath take precedence over sadaqat al-fitr, which in turn takes precedence over udhiya. Nadhr (vows) are also prioritized over udhiya but after expiations? Actually, al-Dhakhira says expiation for killing takes precedence over all other expiations and over nadhr, and nadhr over udhiya and sadaqat al-fitr. The text emphasizes that when obligations and voluntary bequests are mixed, the obligation takes precedence even if the testator started with the voluntary, based on istihsan (juristic preference), although qiyas would suggest following the testator's order. The passage also discusses cases where specific versus non-specific bequests are involved, leading to proportional sharing (muhasah) to give effect to specific bequests first. A detailed calculation example is provided from Fatawa Abi al-Layth to illustrate the distribution when the third is insufficient. Finally, al-Waqi'at al-Natifi categorizes obligations into four ranks: 1) absolute obligations like zakat and Hajj, 2) obligations due to one's own action like various expiations, 3) self-imposed obligations like vows, and 4) voluntary acts. The passage records a disagreement among narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding the order of Hajj and zakat. Overall, the text serves as a practical guide for executors and judges when the estate cannot cover all bequests, with the underlying principle that obligations take priority over voluntary acts, and when all are equal in strength, the testator's own order is followed.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest or will directing that certain actions be performed or assets given after death.
الفرائض (al-fara'id): Obligatory acts that the testator was required to perform, such as zakat, Hajj, and expiations.
النفل (al-nafl): Voluntary or supererogatory acts, not obligatory, but commended.
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): Expiation for sins or missed obligations, such as breaking an oath, zihar, or unintentional killing.
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow made by the testator to perform a specific act of worship, now obligatory upon him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if a testator bequeaths both Hajj al-Islam (obligatory) and a voluntary charity, but the estate cannot cover both, which is given priority?
A) The voluntary charity, because the testator mentioned it first.
B) Both are given equal priority and distributed proportionally.
C) Hajj al-Islam, because it is obligatory.
D) The executor chooses based on which is more beneficial.

Key Takeaway
Obligatory bequests (fard/wajib) always take precedence over voluntary (nafl) in a will; when multiple obligations compete, the mufta bihi prioritizes zakat first, then Hajj, then expiations.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

8 min
Ruling on Equal Strength Bequests: Follow Testator's Order
Matn ruling with commentary on priority of bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for prioritizing bequests when they are equal in strength, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding zakat and Hajj, and apply the proof from Quranic warnings.

Core Idea
When bequests are equally strong, the testator's order prevails; zakat is prioritised over Hajj by Abu Hanifa due to the right of the slave.

This lesson unpacks a passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. You will learn the Hanafi procedure when multiple bequests compete for the limited third of the estate. The key principle: if bequests are equal in strength (e.g., both obligatory), the order mentioned by the testator is followed. The passage also presents an important intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa gives priority to zakat over Hajj, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad give priority to Hajj due to Quranic warnings. The underlying reasoning and proof texts are analysed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The matn states: if bequests are equal in strength, begin with what the testator began with. This establishes the primacy of the testator's order.
Strength (quwwah) refers to the degree of obligation and presence of Quranic warnings.
2
Understand the rationale
The commentator explains that the testator's apparent choice reflects what is most important to him, and this apparent evidence is treated like an explicit text.
This is a principle of takhrīj: the manifest action of the sick person is given weight.
3
Apply the ruling to the example of zakat vs Hajj
Abu Hanifa says zakat is given priority because it involves the right of the slave (haqq al-ʿabd). However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say Hajj is prioritised due to stern Quranic warnings.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school; both positions rely on different aspects of the Sharia.
4
Examine the proof from the Quran
The commentator cites verses on hoarding (9:34-35) and on Hajj (3:97) to show that both acts have explicit warnings, which elevate their strength over expiations.
The presence of waʿīd (threat of punishment) makes an act stronger than those without such warnings.
5
Generalise and note exceptions
When bequests are not equal in strength, the stronger is prioritised. Special rules apply to manumission and muḥābāh (preferential treatment).
If the testator did not specify an order, customs and apparent importance are used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن تساوت في القوة بدئ بما بدأ به لأن الظاهر من حال المريض يبدأ بما هو الأهم عنده والثابت بالظاهر كالثابت فصار كأنه نص على تقديمه باعتبار حاله فتقدم الزكاة على الحج لتعلق حق العبد بها. وعن أبي يوسف أن الحج يقدم وهو قول محمد، وهما يقدمان على الكفارة لرجحانهما عليها لأنه جاء الوعيد فيهما ما لم يأت في غيرهما قال الله تعالى والذين يكنزون الذهب والفضة ولا ينفقونها في سبيل الله فبشرهم بعذاب أليم الآية وقال تعالى فتكوى بها جباههم وجنوبهم ﴾ [التوبة: ٣٤، ٣٥] وقال تعالى ومن كفر فإن الله غني عن العالمين ﴾ [آل عمران ۹۷] مكان قوله ومن ترك الحج إلى غير ذلك من النصوص والأخبار الواردة فيهما. وكذا ما ورد نص بوعيد فيه يقدم وما ليس بواجب قدم منه ما قدمه الموصى لما بينا، وقد تقدم أن الوصايا إذا اجتمعت لا يقدم البعض على البعض إلا العتق والمحاباة على ما بينا من قبل، ولا معتبر بالتقديم ولا بالتأخير ما لم ينص عليه ولهذا لو أوصى الجماعة على التعاقب يستوون في الاستحقاق ولا يقدم أحد على أحد غير أن المستحق إذا اتحد ولم يف الثلث بالوصايا كلها يقدم الأهم فالأهم باعتبار أن يبدأ بالأهم عادة فيكون ذلك كالتنصيص عليه لأن من عليه قضاء من صلاة أو حج يشتغل بالنفل من ذلك الجنس ويترك القضاء عادة، لو فعل ذلك نسب إلى الحيف
He (the author of Kanz) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if they are equal in strength, one begins with what he began with, because the apparent from the state of the sick person is that he begins with what is more important to him, and what is established by apparent evidence is like what is established by explicit text, so it becomes as if he explicitly stated its priority considering his state. Thus, zakat is given priority over Hajj due to the attachment of the right of the slave to it. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that Hajj is given priority, and this is the saying of Muhammad, and they both give priority to these two over expiation because they outweigh it, since the warning has come regarding them that has not come regarding others. Allah Almighty said: 'And those who hoard gold and silver and do not spend them in the way of Allah, give them tidings of a painful punishment' the verse, and He said: 'So they will be branded on their foreheads and sides' [9:34-35], and He said: 'And whoever disbelieves, then indeed Allah is free from need of the worlds' [3:97] in place of His saying 'and whoever abandons Hajj' and other texts and reports narrated concerning them. Similarly, whatever text has come with a warning regarding it is given priority. And what is not obligatory, from it he gives priority to what the testator gave priority based on what we have explained. It has preceded that when bequests are combined, none is given priority over another except manumission and preference (muhabah) as we have explained before. And no consideration is given to priority or delay unless it is specified by the testator. For this reason, if he bequeaths to a group in sequence, they are equal in entitlement, and none is given priority over another. However, if the recipient is one and the third does not suffice for all the bequests, he gives priority to the most important, then the next most important, based on the consideration that he begins with the more important customarily, and that becomes like a specification. Because one who has a missed prayer or Hajj to make up does not usually occupy himself with voluntary acts of that type and leave the make-up, and if he were to do so, it would be attributed to injustice.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn ruling by the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The matn states: 'If bequests are equal in strength, one begins with what the testator began with.' The commentator explains the reasoning: the sick person's actions indicate what is most important to him, and this apparent evidence is treated like an explicit statement. Thus, if the testator started with zakat although Hajj is generally more important, zakat is given priority because it involves the right of a slave (the poor are considered 'slaves of Allah' in terms of rights). However, there is a difference of opinion: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani say Hajj is given priority because of the stern warnings in the Quran regarding hoarding wealth and abandoning Hajj. The commentator cites Quranic verses as proof: verses on hoarding (9:34-35) and on Hajj (3:97). These warnings indicate greater importance, so Hajj and zakat take precedence over expiations. The passage also clarifies that when bequests are of different types (obligatory vs voluntary), the obligatory is given priority based on custom, as one usually fulfills obligations before voluntary acts. For equally obligatory bequests, if the testator did not specify an order, they share proportionally, except for manumission and muhabah (preferential treatment) which have special rules. This lesson underscores the Hanafi principle of relying on the testator's apparent intention and the relative strength of obligations as indicated by Quranic warnings.

Key Terms
القوة (al-quwwah): Strength, meaning the degree of obligation or the severity of punishment for neglect, used to compare different bequests.
الأهم (al-ahamm): The more important (act), determined by the testator's custom and explicit warnings in the Quran.
حق العبد (haqq al-'abd): The right of the servant (i.e., human rights), such as the right of the poor in zakat, as opposed to the rights of Allah.
الوعيد (al-wa'id): The threat of punishment in the Quran for abandoning an obligation, indicating its high importance.
المحاباة (al-muhabah): Preferential treatment in a will, such as giving more to one heir or favoring a non-heir; has special rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary factor when bequests are equal in strength and the third is insufficient?
A) The amount of each bequest
B) The testator's order
C) The executor's choice
D) The number of witnesses

Key Takeaway
When bequests are equal in strength, the testator's order is binding; if there is an intra-Hanafi dispute on relative importance, follow the order mentioned.

Flexibility in Executing Bequests for Charity
Series of rulings on substituting charity bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a bequest for charity can be fulfilled by giving an equivalent value or substitute, and identify when substitution is not allowed.

Core Idea
A bequest for charity is binding, but the executor may substitute equivalent value unless the testator explicitly prohibits substitution.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a gap in the original matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) regarding bequests for charity. The commentator presents multiple scenarios showing that the Hanafi school generally allows the executor flexibility in fulfilling such bequests, especially when substituting equivalent value. However, there are some differences of opinion, particularly regarding specific items like garments. Understanding this flexibility is crucial for executors to act within the bounds of sharia while achieving the testator's charitable intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage establishes that a bequest for charity can often be fulfilled by giving an equivalent value or substitute, not necessarily the exact item mentioned.
This is based on a principle of fulfilling the testator's intention.
2
Recognize the ikhtilaf
There is a dispute between Khalaf and Muhammad ibn Salama regarding a bequest of a specific garment. Khalaf gives three options; Muhammad insists on the exact garment.
The author sides with Khalaf, indicating the preferred Hanafi position.
3
Apply to different scenarios
The passage applies this flexibility to various cases: substituting currency, changing the type of charity (e.g., from wheat to dirhams), and even changing the recipients (e.g., from poor of Hajj to other poor).
Each scenario is derived from different authorities.
4
Note the limits
If the testator explicitly specifies 'give charity with its price' (i.e., sale proceeds), the executor cannot keep the item and give value.
The testator's explicit wording may restrict flexibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يتعرض المؤلف للوصية بالصدقة ونحن نذكر ذلك تتميماً للفائدة، هذا يشتمل على أقسام : الأول إذا أوصى بالتصدق بشيء فيتصدق بغيره سأل ابن مقاتل عمن أوصى أن يتصدق عنه بألف درهم فتصدق عنه بالحنطة أو على عكسه قال : يجوز قال الفقيه : معناه أنه أوصى أن يتصدق عنه بألف درهم حنطة ولكن سقط ذلك عن السؤال فقيل له : إن كانت الحنطة موجودة فأعطى قيمته دراهم قال : أرجو أن يجوز . وفي النوازل وبه نأخذ وفي الظهيرية رجل قال تصدقوا بثلث مالي وورثته فقراء فإن كانوا كباراً كلهم فأجاز بعضهم لبعض جاز للموصي أن يعطيهم من شيئاً. وعن محمد : لو أوصى بصدقة ألف درهم بعينها فتصدق الوصي مكانها بألف من مال الميت جاز، وإن هلكت الأولى قبل أن يتصدق الوصي يضمنه الورثة مثلها وعنه أن تبطل الوصية. ولو أوصى بأن يتصدق بشيء من ماله على فقراء الحج هل يجوز أن يتصدق على غيرهم من الفقراء؟ قال الشيخ الإمام أبو نصر : أيجوز ذلك، وإن أوصى بالدراهم وأعطاهم حنطة لم يجز . قال الفقيه : وقد قيل إنه يجوز وبه نأخذ وسأل خلف عمن أوصى أن يتصدق بهذا الثوب قال : إن شاؤوا تصدقوا بعينه وإن شاؤوا باعوا وأعطوا ثمنه، وإن شاؤوا أعطوا قيمة الثوب وأمسكوا الثوب . وقال محمد بن سلمة : بل يتصدق بعينه كما وكذا اللقطة هو ولو نذر وقال الله علي أن أتصدق بهذا الثوب جاز أن يتصدق بقيمته. قال الفقيه أبو الليث رحمه الله : بقول خلف نأخذ فإنه ذكر في الزيادات فيمن أوصى أن يباع هذا العبد ويتصدق بثمنه على المساكين جاز لهم التصدق بعين العبد فثبت أن التصدق بالعين وبالثمن على السواء. وسأل أبو القاسم عمن أوصى إلى رجل وقال له بالفارسية فلان نعم راجام کر فأعطاه ثمن الكرباس قال : هذا يقع على المخيط. وفي الأجناس وفي نوادر ابن سماعة عن محمد: إذا أوصى أن يتصدق عنه بألف درهم فتصدق بقيمتها دنانير يجوز. وفي الخانية روى ابن سماعة عن محمد: إنه يجوز . ولو أوصى أن يتصدق بثمنه فليس له أن يمسك الثوب للورثة ويتصدق بقيمته، ولو قال اشتر عشرة أثواب وتصدق بها فاشترى الوصـ فله أن يبيعها ويتصدق
The author did not address the bequest for charity, and we mention it as a completion of benefit. This includes sections: First: If he bequeaths to give charity with something, then he gives charity with something else. Ibn Muqatil was asked about someone who bequeathed to give charity on his behalf with one thousand dirhams, but the executor gave charity on his behalf with wheat, or vice versa. He said: It is permissible. Al-Faqih said: Its meaning is that he bequeathed to give charity with one thousand dirhams of wheat, but that was omitted in the question? So it was said to him: If the wheat was present and he gave its value in dirhams, he said: I hope it is permissible. In al-Nawazil: And we take this. In al-Zahiriyya: A man said 'Give charity with my third to my poor heirs.' If they are all adults and some of them permit for others, it is permissible for the testator to give them something from it. From Muhammad: If he bequeaths a specific charity of one thousand dirhams, and the executor gives charity in its place with one thousand from the deceased's wealth, it is permissible. If the original one perishes before the executor gives charity, the heirs guarantee its like; and from him also that the bequest becomes void. And if he bequeaths to give charity with something from his wealth to the poor of Hajj, is it permissible to give charity to other poor? Sheikh Imam Abu Nasr said: Yes, it is permissible. And if he bequeaths dirhams and they gave wheat, it is not permissible. Al-Faqih said: It has been said that it is permissible and we take that. Khalaf asked about someone who bequeaths to give charity with this garment: He said: If they wish, they can give charity with its exact self; if they wish, they can sell and give its price; if they wish, they can give its value and keep the garment. Muhammad ibn Salama said: Rather, they must give charity with its exact self. Similarly, a found item (luqata) and if he made a vow saying 'Upon me to give charity with this garment' it is permissible to give its value. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: We take the saying of Khalaf, because it is mentioned in al-Ziyadat that a person bequeathed that this slave be sold and its price be given in charity to the poor, and it was permissible for them to give charity with the slave itself. So it is established that giving charity with the exact thing and with its price are equal. Abu al-Qasim asked about someone who bequeathed to a man and said in Persian 'so-and-so, be a good man' and then he gave him the price of a cloth (karbas). He said: This applies to sewn goods. In al-Ajnas and in Nawadir Ibn Sam'ah from Muhammad: If he bequeaths to give charity on his behalf with one thousand dirhams, then he gives charity with its value in dinars, it is permissible. In al-Khaniyya, Ibn Sam'ah narrated from Muhammad that it is permissible. And if he bequeaths to give charity with its price, he is not allowed to keep the garment for the heirs and give its value. And if he said 'Buy ten garments and give them in charity' and the executor bought them, then he may sell them and give charity (with the proceeds).
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an addendum by the commentator, as the original matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) did not explicitly cover bequests for charity (sadaqah). The commentator presents a series of rulings derived from various sources. The key points include: (1) If the testator bequeaths a specific item for charity, it is generally permissible for the executor to substitute its equivalent value, such as giving wheat instead of dirhams, as long as the value is met. (2) There is a question of whether a bequest to give charity to the poor of Hajj can be diverted to other poor; different opinions exist, and the author's preferred view is that it is permissible. (3) Regarding a bequest of a specific garment for charity, there is ikhtilaf: Khalaf says the executor has options to either give the garment itself, sell it and give the price, or give the value and keep the garment; Muhammad ibn Salama insists on giving the garment itself. The commentator sides with Khalaf because a similar case in al-Ziyadat allows selling a slave and giving its price, showing the equivalence. (4) If the testator bequeaths a specific sum of money for charity, giving the value in another currency (e.g., dinars instead of dirhams) is permissible. (5) If the testator says to buy garments and give them in charity, the executor may instead sell them and give the proceeds. The passage treats these rulings as practical guidance for executors, showing the Hanafi school's flexibility in fulfilling charitable bequests.

Key Terms
صدقة (sadaqah): Charity given voluntarily or by bequest.
وصي (wasiyy): The executor of the will, appointed to carry out the testator's instructions.
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform a good deed, which becomes obligatory if the condition is fulfilled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only give the garment itself
B) Only sell and give the price
C) Give the garment, sell it, or give its value
D) Give the garment to the heirs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows flexibility in fulfilling charitable bequests, permitting substitution of equivalent value unless the testator explicitly restricts it.

Executor's Authority to Sell Property for a General Charity Bequest
Ruling on sale of property for general charity bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that an executor may sell houses, lands, and slaves to fulfill a general charity bequest and identify the condition that triggers this authority.

Core Idea
A general charity bequest permits the executor to sell and convert property to cash.

When a testator leaves a general charity bequest, such as 'give a third of my wealth in charity', the executor must determine how to fulfill it. This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling that the executor has the authority to sell houses, lands, and even slaves to raise cash for the bequest, provided the testator did not specify particular items. Understanding this authority is crucial for correct estate administration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of bequest
Read the testator's words: is the bequest general (e.g., 'a third of my wealth') or specific (e.g., 'this house')? This lesson deals with general bequests.
2
State the executor's authority
According to the text, the executor may sell property (houses, lands, slaves) and give the price in charity.
The underlying principle: the bequest is for value, not the specific item.
3
Apply to different assets
The text gives examples: houses, lands, and slaves. The same ruling applies to any property the testator owned.
4
Contrast with specific bequest
Note that if the testator specified a particular item (e.g., 'this slave'), the executor must give that item itself, not its price.
This distinction is important for the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فتصدق الوصي تلك الدور يبيع بثمنها، وكذلك لو قال تصدقوا بثلث مالي وله دور وأرضون فللوصي أن يبيع الدور والأرضين ويتصدق بالثمن، وكذلك قال تصدقوا بثلث مالي وبهذا العبد فللوصي أن يبيع ذلك العبد ويتصدق بالثمن. وعن محمد إذا أوصى أن يتصدق عنه بألف درهم بعينها بألف أخرى مكانها من مال الميت جاز والحاصل أن الحي إذا نذر بالتصدق بمال نفسه فتصدق بمثله أو قيمته ففيه روايتان فإن هلكت الألف التي عينها الوصي قبل أن يتصدق الوصي ضمن الوارث مثلها. وعنه أيضاً : لو أوصى بألف درهم بعينها تصدق عنه فهلكت الألف بطلت الوصية. وفي النوازل : إذا أوصى لرجل بهذه البقرة لم يكن للورثة أن يتصدقوا بثمنها.
The charity executor sells those houses for their price. Similarly, if he said 'Give charity with a third of my wealth' and he has houses and lands, the executor may sell the houses and lands and give charity with the price. Similarly, if he said 'Give charity with a third of my wealth and with this slave', the executor may sell that slave and give charity with the price. From Muhammad: If he bequeathed that charity be given from him with a specific thousand dirhams, then [the executor may] take another thousand in its place from the wealth of the deceased, it is permissible. In summary, if a living person vows to give charity from his own wealth and then gives the like or its value, there are two narrations. If the thousand that the executor designated perishes before the executor gives charity, the heir guarantees its like. Also from him: If he bequeathed a specific thousand dirhams to give charity from him and the thousand perished, the bequest is void. In al-Nawazil: If he bequeathed this cow to a man, the heirs may not give charity with its price.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings (ruling_statement) from the chapter on bequests (kitab al-wasaya) concerning the executor's authority to sell property to fulfill a charity bequest. The primary ruling: when a testator says 'give charity with a third of my wealth', the executor may sell any property (houses, land, slaves) to convert it into cash and give that cash as charity. This is because the bequest is for the value, not the specific item. However, if the testator specifies a particular item, like 'this cow' or 'these thousand dirhams', then the executor must give that specific item; if it perishes, the bequest is void, and the heirs cannot substitute it with something else. The Hanafi madhhab permits the executor to sell generic property to realize the bequest, but strict adherence to explicit specifications is required. The passage also notes a transmission from Muhammad that if the testator specified a sum of dirhams, the executor may replace them with another sum from the estate, indicating flexibility when the original amount is lost. However, if the loss occurs before the executor acts, the heir is liable for the like. The final ruling from al-Nawazil clarifies that if a specific cow is bequeathed to a person, the heirs cannot sell it and give the price; the cow itself must be given.

Key Terms
الوصي (al-wasi): The executor appointed in the will to carry out the testator's wishes.
الصدقة (al-sadaqa): Charitable giving, in this context a bequest to give in charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Give the house itself as charity
B) Sell the house and give the price as charity
C) Keep the house and give nothing
D) Ask the heirs for permission

Key Takeaway
A general charity bequest empowers the executor to sell any property and donate the cash proceeds.

Ruling When a Charity Bequest Specifies a Particular Item
Rulings on specific charity bequests and perishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that a specific charity bequest (e.g., 'this slave' or 'these dirhams') must be fulfilled with the exact item, and that if it perishes, the bequest is void.

Core Idea
A specific bequest requires the exact item; loss voids the bequest.

When a testator explicitly names a particular item for charity, the executor must give that very item, not its equivalent or price. This lesson examines the rulings on specific bequests, including what happens if the item perishes before delivery. The Hanafi school distinguishes strict adherence to specific instructions, while also noting an exception from Imam Muhammad regarding replacement under certain conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify specific bequest scenarios
The passage discusses three specific cases: (1) bequest of a specific thousand dirhams, (2) bequest of a specific cow, (3) implication that a specific slave must be given as is.
2
State the general ruling for specific items
If the testator specifies a particular item (e.g., 'this cow'), the heirs cannot give its price instead; they must give the item itself.
This is based on the final ruling from al-Nawazil.
3
Analyze the perishment scenario
If the specified item perishes before the executor acts, the bequest is void (batalat al-wasiyya). The executor cannot substitute another item.
There is a nuance from Muhammad: if the testator said 'with a specific thousand dirhams', the executor may take another thousand from the estate as a replacement.
4
Reconcile the apparent contradiction
Muhammad's narration allows replacement when the testator's wording implies the value (e.g., 'a thousand dirhams' without specifying 'these coins'), whereas other specific items like 'this cow' require the exact cow.
The distinction lies in whether the description is of a genus or a specific physical object.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Executor's Liability for Misdirected Charity: Specific vs General Bequests
Rulings on executor's liability when giving charity to wrong recipients

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which an executor is liable for deviating from a specified charity bequest and apply the Hanafi fatwa permissibility rule to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Deviation from a specified bequest incurs liability unless the fatwa permits general charity intent.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq collects numerous rulings on the executor's liability when he gives charity to someone other than the testator's specified recipient. The key distinction is between a specific individual (e.g., 'this poor person') and a class (e.g., 'the poor of Makkah'). While strict liability applies in the first case, the later fatwa allows deviation when the testator's intention is general charity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Type of Specification
Read each hypothetical in the passage: does the testator name a specific person, a specific group (e.g., poor of Makkah), or a general category (e.g., the poor)? This determines the initial ruling.
Specific person → strict liability; specific class → liability unless excused; general → no liability.
2
Distinguish Self-Action from Agency
Note where the passage compares the person acting himself vs. appointing an agent. In vows, acting oneself may be permissible, but an agent is liable for deviation.
The ruling changes based on who performs the act.
3
Recognize the Fatwa's Broadening Effect
The passage states 'الفتوى على الجواز' — the operative ruling is permissibility across these issues. Understand that this fatwa relaxes the strict liability for executors.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Apply to Subsidiary Cases
The passage also covers quantity and timing conditions (e.g., giving to ten vs. one, or within ten days). Analyze how the fatwa applies to these scenarios.
Conditions about number or time are not binding unless explicitly emphasized.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الفقيه : وبهذا نأخذ القسم الثاني من النوع إذا أوصى أن يتصدق على مسكين بعينه فتصدق على غيره ضمن. وفي نوادره إذا أوصى أن يتصدق على مساكين مكة أو مساكين الري فتصدق الوصي على غير هذا الصنف ضمن إن كان الآخر حياً، وكذلك لو أوصى أن يتصدق على المرضى من الفقراء أو الشيوخ من الفقراء فتصدق على الشباب من الفقراء ضمن في ذلك كله، ولم يقيد هذه المسألة بحياة الآمر. وفي الخانية : ولو قال الله علي أن أتصدق على فلان فتصدق على غيره لو فعل ذلك بنفسه جاز، ولو أمر غيره بالتصدق ففعل المأمور ذلك ضمن المأمور. ولو قال الله علي أن أتصدق على مساكين مكة فله أن يتصدق على غيرهم، وعن أبي يوسف رواية أخرى فيمن أوصى أن يتصدق عنه على فقراء مكة فتصدق على فقراء غيرها أنه يجوز وسأل أبو نصر عمن أوصى أن يتصدق عنه لهم فتصدق على غيرهم من الفقراء قال : يجوز على ما تقدم عنه وفي أمالي الحسن : قول أبي حنيفة كقول محمد والمذكور في الأمالي : إذا أوصى لمساكين الكوفة فقسم الوصي في غير مساكين الكوفة ضمن ولم يفرق بين حياة الآمر وبين وفاته والفتوى على الجواز في هذه المسائل. وفي نوادر أبي يوسف إذا قال لعبده تصدق بهذه العشرة الدراهم على عشرة مساكين فتصدق بها على مسكين واحد دفعة واحدة جاز قال : وهذا على أن الأمر في ليس على عدد المساكين، لو قال تصدق بها على عشرة لا يجوز وفي الظهيرية ولو قال تصدق بها على مسكين واحد فأعطاها عشرة مساكين جاز، ولو قال في عشرة أيام فتصدق في يوم واحد جاز، وكذا في الخانية. وفي الفتاوى: سأل إبراهيم بن يوسف عمن أوصى لفقراء أهل بلخ فالأفضل أن لا يتجاوز بلخ ولو أعطى فقراء مكة وكورة أخرى جاز.
The jurist said: With this we take the second type of the category: if he bequeathed to give charity to a specific poor person and he gave charity to someone else, he is liable. And in his Nawadir: if he bequeathed to give charity to the poor of Makkah or the poor of Rey, and the executor gave charity to other than this group, he is liable as long as the other was alive. Similarly, if he bequeathed to give charity to the sick among the poor or the elderly among the poor, and he gave charity to the young among the poor, he is liable in all that, and he did not restrict this issue to the life of the testator. In al-Khaniya: And if he said 'I have an obligation to give charity to so-and-so' and he gave charity to someone else, if he did that himself it is permissible, and if he ordered another to give charity and the agent did that, the agent is liable. And if he said 'I have an obligation to give charity to the poor of Makkah', he may give charity to others. And from Abu Yusuf another narration about one who bequeathed to give charity from him to the poor of Makkah, and he gave charity to the poor of other than it: that it is permissible. And Abu Nasr asked about one who bequeathed to give charity from him to them, and he gave charity to other poor people: he said it is permissible, according to what preceded from him. In Amali al-Hasan: The saying of Abu Hanifa is like the saying of Muhammad, and what is mentioned in al-Amali: If he bequeathed to the poor of Kufa, and the executor distributed to other than the poor of Kufa, he is liable, and he did not differentiate between the life of the testator and his death. And the fatwa is on permissibility in these issues. In Nawadir Abu Yusuf: If he said to his slave 'Give charity with these ten dirhams to ten poor persons' and he gave charity with them to one poor person in one go, it is permissible. He said: This is because the command is not on the number of poor persons; if he said 'Give charity with them to ten', it is not permissible. In al-Zahiriyya: And if he said 'Give charity with them to one poor person' and he gave them to ten poor persons, it is permissible. And if he said 'in ten days' and he gave charity in one day, it is permissible. Similarly in al-Khaniya. In al-Fatawa: Ibrahim ibn Yusuf asked about one who bequeathed to the poor of the people of Balkh: the best is that he does not exceed Balkh, but if he gave to the poor of Makkah and another town, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is a detailed collection of rulings (ruling_statement) on the executor's liability when he deviates from the testator's specification of charity recipients. The second type (al-qism al-thani) deals with cases where the testator specifies a particular individual or group. The key principle: if the testator names a specific person (e.g., 'this poor person'), the executor must give to that person; giving to another makes him liable for compensation. If the testator names a specific class (e.g., 'the poor of Makkah'), the executor is generally bound to that class, unless the specific individuals within that class are unavailable or the testator's intention is broad. However, there is a difference between a vow (nadhr) and a bequest (wasiyya): in a vow, the person himself may give to another, but if he appoints an agent, the agent is liable for deviation. In bequests, the executor is usually liable if he deviates, but some narrations from Abu Yusuf allow deviation for broader charity. The fatwa (operative ruling) in these issues is permissibility (jawaz) for the executor to deviate to other poor, as long as the general objective of charity is achieved. The passage also addresses subsidiary issues: if the testator says 'give to ten poor persons', giving to one is not permissible; but if he says 'give to one', giving to ten is permissible. Timing conditions like 'in ten days' are not strict; giving all at once is acceptable. The final fatwa indicates that for a bequest to the poor of Balkh, it is better to restrict to Balkh, but giving to other poor (like Makkah) is also permissible.

Key Terms
ضمن (damina): He is liable, i.e., must compensate the estate for the misdirected charity.
الفتوى (al-fatwa): The formally adopted ruling for practice, here indicating permissibility.
مساكين (masakin): Poor people; the category of recipients for charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the fatwa (operative ruling) regarding an executor who gives charity to the poor of Makkah instead of the specified poor of Kufa?
A) He is definitely liable
B) It is permissible
C) It is invalid
D) He must ask the heirs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa allows the executor flexibility to give charity to other poor if the testator's specification was not strictly personal.

Defining 'Neighbors' in a Bequest: Adjacent vs. All Local Residents
Definition of 'jiran' in bequests with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'neighbors' in a bequest and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
In bequests, 'neighbors' means only those physically adjacent to the testator's wall (Abu Hanifa).

When someone bequeaths to 'my neighbors', who exactly is included? The word 'neighbor' can be ambiguous, but Hanafi law provides a precise definition grounded in linguistic derivation and prior rulings on preemption. This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions on the scope of the term, and why the restriction to adjacent neighbors is the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal context
Recognise that this passage comes from the chapter on bequests (wasiyyah) and specifically addresses the interpretation of a general term ('jiran') in a bequest. The ruling determines who is entitled to the bequest.
The same definition affects other areas like preemption (shuf'a).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that 'neighbors' refers only to those whose property directly adjoins the testator's wall (mulāṣiqūn). Understand the linguistic basis: the word 'jār' is derived from 'mujāwara' meaning adjacency.
This is presented as qiyas (analogical reasoning).
3
Identify the supporting dalil
The passage cites the hadith 'al-jār aḥaqqu bi-shuf'atihi' (the neighbor is more entitled to his preemption). According to Hanafi interpretation, this hadith establishes preemption only for adjacent neighbors, and the same principle applies to bequests.
The hadith is used to restrict the general meaning.
4
Contrast the Sahibayn's view
The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) define 'neighbors' more broadly to include all residents of the locality. Their view is based on istihsan (juristic preference), though the text cuts off before giving their full reasoning.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both views are within the school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Although the passage does not explicitly resolve the ikhtilaf, later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Hidayah) adopt Abu Hanifa's view as the relied-upon position. Understand that the mufta bihi is the adjacent-neighbor definition.
This affects both bequest distribution and preemption claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوصية للأقارب وغيرهم قال في العناية : إنما أخر هذا الباب عما تقدم لأن في هذا الباب ذكر أحكام الوصية لقوم مخصوصين وفيما تقدم ذكر أحكامها على وجه العموم والخصوص أبداً يتلو العموم. وقوله «جيرانه كان حق الكلام أن يقدم ذكر الوصية للأقارب نظراً إلى ما في الترجمة، ويجوز قال رحمه الله : أن يقال الواو لا تدل على الترتيب وأن يقال قدم ذكر الجيران للاهتمام بهم . (جيرانه ملاصقوه) يعني لو أوصى إلى جيرانه يصرف ذلك للملاصقين لجداره، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وهو القياس لأنه مأخوذ من المجاورة وهي الملاصقة ولهذا حمل قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «الجار أحق بشفعته حتى لا يستحق الشفعة غير الملاصق بالجوار، ولأنه لما تعذر صرفه إلى الجميع صرف إليه ألا ترى أنه يدخل فيه جار المحلة وجار الأرض وجار القرية فوجب صرفه إلى أخص الخصوص وهو الملاصق في الاستحسان وفي قولهما جار الرجل
Chapter: Bequest to Relatives and Others. He said in al-Inaya: This chapter is delayed after what preceded because in this chapter are mentioned rulings of bequest to specific people, while in the preceding were its rulings in general, and the specific always follows the general. And his saying 'his neighbors' — the correct speech would be to mention the bequest to relatives first in view of the chapter heading, but it is permissible — he (may Allah have mercy on him) said — that the 'waw' does not indicate order, and it is said that mentioning neighbors first is to emphasize them. (His neighbors are those adjacent to him) meaning: if he bequeathed to his neighbors, it is given to those adjacent to his wall. This is according to Abu Hanifa, and it is the qiyas because it is derived from 'mujawara' which is adjacency. For this reason, the Prophet's saying 'The neighbor is more entitled to his preemption' was interpreted such that the preemption right is not established for non-adjacent neighbors due to mere neighborliness. And because when it is impossible to give to all, it is given to the nearest. Do you not see that it includes the neighbor of the quarter, the neighbor of the land, and the neighbor of the village? So it is necessary to give to the most specific, which is the adjacent, in istihsan. According to the two, the neighbor of a man is...
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage opens a new chapter (bāb) on bequests to relatives and others. The author first explains the chapter ordering: specific follows general. The first ruling defined 'neighbors' (jīrān) in a bequest. Abu Hanifa's position: 'neighbors' refers only to those whose property directly adjoins the testator's wall (mulāṣiqūn). This is derived from the root meaning of 'mujāwara' (adjacency) and is supported by the hadith 'The neighbor is more entitled to his preemption' which Hanafis interpret as referring only to adjacent neighbors for the right of preemption (shuf'a). Since it is impossible to distribute to all possible neighbors (neighbor of the quarter, land, village), the term must be restricted to the closest type. This is qiyas. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) define 'neighbors' more broadly to include all residents of the locality. The passage does not provide their full reasoning here, but the difference affects who is entitled to the bequest. The text mentions that their view is based on istihsan, though the passage cuts off before completing their argument.

Key Terms
الجار (al-jār): Neighbor; in the context of bequest, Abu Hanifa limits it to the one whose property directly adjoins the testator's wall.
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): Right of preemption: the right of an adjacent neighbor to purchase a shared property before an outsider.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, who is entitled to a bequest made to 'my neighbors'?
A) All residents of the same street
B) Those whose property directly adjoins the testator's wall
C) All members of the local mosque
D) Relatives living nearby

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, bequests to 'neighbors' are restricted to those with physically adjoining walls, based on linguistic derivation and the hadith on preemption.

Defining 'Neighbors' in Bequests: A Hanafi Internal Dispute
Commentary on the interpretation of 'neighbors' in bequests with Hanafi internal dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi definitions of 'neighbors' in bequests and explain the proofs for each position.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'neighbors' only includes adjacent property owners according to Abu Hanifa, but includes all local mosque-goers according to the Sahibayn.

In bequests, precise wording matters. When a testator bequeaths to 'my neighbors', who is included? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. This lesson examines the linguistic and hadith-based arguments each side uses, and the practical implications for distributing the bequest.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the legal question: When a testator says 'to my neighbors', to whom does the bequest go? The word 'neighbor' (جار) is ambiguous.
2
Present Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that only adjacent property owners (ملاصقون) are included. His proof: linguistic derivation from 'mujawarah' meaning adjacency, and the hadith on preemption.
The hadith 'الجار أحق بشفعته' supports adjacency.
3
Present the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that neighbors are those living in the same locality and sharing a mosque. Their proof: custom ('urf) and the hadith 'لا صلاة لجار المسجد إلا في المسجد' interpreted as all who hear the call.
They argue the purpose of the bequest is benevolence, which applies to a wider group.
4
Identify the practical difference
Under Abu Hanifa, only those with adjoining property share; under Sahibayn, a larger group (locality + mosque) shares. This affects distribution.
Also note the cross-madhhab contrast: Shafi'i extends to 40 houses.
5
Consider the cross-madhhab comparison
Imam al-Shafi'i defines neighbor as within 40 houses each side, but the commentator declares that hadith weak. The Hanafi internal dispute remains the primary framework.
This shows the importance of hadith criticism in usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوصية للأقارب وغيرهم قال في العناية : إنما أخر هذا الباب عما تقدم لأن في هذا الباب ذكر أحكام الوصية لقوم مخصوصين وفيما تقدم ذكر أحكامها على وجه العموم والخصوص أبداً يتلو العموم. وقوله «جيرانه كان حق الكلام أن يقدم ذكر الوصية للأقارب نظراً إلى ما في الترجمة، ويجوز قال رحمه الله : أن يقال الواو لا تدل على الترتيب وأن يقال قدم ذكر الجيران للاهتمام بهم . (جيرانه ملاصقوه) يعني لو أوصى إلى جيرانه يصرف ذلك للملاصقين لجداره، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وهو القياس لأنه مأخوذ من المجاورة وهي الملاصقة ولهذا حمل قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «الجار أحق بشفعته حتى لا يستحق الشفعة غير الملاصق بالجوار، ولأنه لما تعذر صرفه إلى الجميع صرف إليه ألا ترى أنه يدخل فيه جار المحلة وجار الأرض وجار القرية فوجب صرفه إلى أخص الخصوص وهو الملاصق في الاستحسان وفي قولهما جار الرجل هو من يسكن محلته ويجمعهم مسجد المحلة لأن الكل يسمون جاراً عرفاً وشرعاً. قال عليه الصلاة والسلام لا صلاة لجار المسجد إلا في المسجد» ففسر بكل من سمع النداء، ولأن المقصود بالوصية للجيران برهم والإحسان إليهم،
