الجار أربعون داراً هكذا وهكذا قلنا هذا ضعيف عند أهل النقل فلا يصح الاحتجاج به ويستوي فيه الجار الساكن والمالك والذكر والأنثى والمسلم والذمي لأن الاسم يتناول الكل، ويدخل فيه العبد الساكن عنده لأن مطلق هذا يتناوله ولا يدخل عندهما لأن الوصية له وصية لمولاه وهو ليس بجار بخلاف المكاتب لأن استحقاق ما في يده للاختصاص به ثبت له ولا يملكه المولى إلا بالتمليك منه ألا ترى أنه يجوز له أخذ الزكاة وإن كان مولاه غنياً بخلاف القن والمدبر وأم الولد فالأرملة تدخل لأن سكناها مضاف إليها، ولا تدخل التي لها بعل لأن سكناها غير مضاف إليها وإنما هي تبع فلم تكن جاراً حقيقة. وفي المنتقى : ولو أوصى بثلث ماله لجيرانه، فإن كانوا بحصون يقسم على أغنيائهم وفقرائهم ولذلك لو قال لأهل محلة كذا أو لأهل مسجد كذا لأنه ليس في اللفظ ما يدل على التخصيص قال محمد رحمه الله : رجل أوصى بمائة درهم لرجل من جيرانه ثم أوصى لجيرانه بمائة ينظر فيما أوصى لهذا وفيما يصيبه مع الجيران فيدخل الأقل من الأكثر لأن المائة إذا كانت أكثر فإنه يستحقها باسم الجيرة وقد آثره الموصي بتعين المائة فلا يستحق شيئاً آخر، فإذا كان نصيبه مع الجيران أكثر يكون رجوعاً عما سمى له وشركاً له مع الجيران كلهم. ولو أوصى بثلث ماله لمجاوري مكة فإن الوصية جائزة، فإن كانوا لا يحصون صرف إلى أهل الحاجة منهم وإن كانوا يحصون قسمت على رؤوسهم. واختلفوا في تفسير الإحصاء وتقديره؛ على قول أبي يوسف لا يحصون إلا بكتاب وحساب فإنهم يحصون. وقال محمد: إن كانوا أكثر من المائة لا يحصون، وإن كانوا أقل يحصون . وقيل : الأمر موكول إلى رأي القاضي وهو الأحوط وقال أبو يوسف: لكهول أهل بيته فهو لأبناء الثلاثين إلى الأربعين والشاب إذا احتلم إلى ثلاثين، والشيخ من كان شبيه أكثر فهو شيخ، وإن كان السواد أكثر فهو ليس بشيخ. وعن أبي يوسف في رواية أخرى أن له أربعون سنة إلى خمسين، وذكر في موضع آخر إذا بلغ ثلاثاً وثلاثين سنة صار كهلاً. وقال في موضع آخر : إذا بلغ الثلاثين وخالطه الشيب فهو كهل، وإن لم يخالطه فهو شاب. وفي بعض الروايات الاعتبار بالسن لأنه أمكن مراعاة في حق الكل على نهج واحد، وفي بعضها اعتبر من حيث الإمارة والعلامة فإن الناس يتعارفون ذلك وأطلقوا الاسم عند الكهل من وجود العلامة وهو الشمط والشيب . قال رحمه الله: (وإصهاره كل ذي رحم محرم من امرأته لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة
Chapter on Bequests to Relatives and Others. He said in al-Inayah: He delayed this chapter only because in this chapter the mention of rulings of bequests to specific people, and in what preceded the mention of rulings in general, and the specific always follows the general. His saying 'his neighbors' – the right of speech would be to mention the bequest to relatives first due to the title, but it is permissible, he (rahimahullah) said, that the waw does not indicate order, and that the mention of neighbors is given priority for emphasis. (His neighbors are those adjacent to him) means if he bequeaths to his neighbors, it is given to those adjacent to his wall. This is according to Abu Hanifa, and it is analogy because it is derived from being neighbor (mujawarah) which is adjacency, and for this he interpreted his (peace be upon him) statement 'the neighbor has more right to preemption' such that no one other than the adjacent neighbor is entitled to preemption. And because when it is impossible to give to all, it is given to the closest; do you not see that it includes the neighbor of the locality, the neighbor of the land, the neighbor of the village, so it must be given to the most specific, which is the adjacent one by juristic preference. According to the two disciples, a person's neighbor is one who lives in his locality and who are gathered by the mosque of the locality, because all are called neighbors customarily and legally. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque' and it is interpreted as everyone who hears the call. (And because the purpose of the bequest to neighbors is their goodness and benevolence, and its juristic preference includes both adjacent and non-adjacent, except that there must be mixing to realize the meaning of the name, and mixing occurs with a common mosque. Al-Shafi'i (rahimahullah) said: the neighbor extends to forty houses on each side, due to his (peace be upon him) statement 'The right of the neighbor is forty houses' and we say this is weak according to hadith scholars, so it cannot be used as evidence. The resident and owner, male and female, Muslim and Dhimmi are equal because the name includes all. The slave living with him is included because the general meaning includes him; but according to the two disciples he is not included because the bequest to him is a bequest to his master, and he is not a neighbor, unlike the mukatab (slave with contract of manumission) because the entitlement to what is in his hand is established for him and the master only owns it by transfer from him; do you not see that he may take zakat even if his master is rich, unlike the qin (ordinary slave), mudabbar (slave freed upon death), and umm walad (concubine mother of child). The widow is included because her residence is attributed to her; the married woman is not included because her residence is not attributed to her, and she is merely a follower, so she is not truly a neighbor. In al-Muntaqa: If he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to his neighbors, and they are in forts, it is divided among their rich and poor, and similarly if he says to the people of such a locality or the people of such a mosque, because there is nothing in the wording indicating specification. Muhammad (rahimahullah) said: A man bequeaths 100 dirhams to a particular man from his neighbors, then bequeaths 100 to his neighbors; it is considered what he bequeathed to this man and what he receives with the neighbors, and the lesser of the greater is included. If the 100 is more, he gets it by virtue of being a neighbor, and the testator singled him out with the specified 100, so he gets nothing else. If his share with the neighbors is more, it is a revocation of what he named for him and a sharing with all the neighbors. If he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to the residents (mujawirin) of Makkah, the bequest is valid; if they are uncountable, it is given to the needy among them; if countable, it is divided among them per head. They differed on the interpretation of 'countability' and its estimation: according to Abu Yusuf, they are only uncountable if they require a book and calculation; otherwise they are countable. Muhammad said: If they are more than a hundred, they are uncountable; if less, countable. It was also said that the matter is left to the judge's opinion, and this is more cautious. Abu Yusuf said regarding 'the middle-aged of his household' (kuhul ahli baytihi): it is for those aged 30 to 40; the youth (shab) is from puberty to 30; the old (shaykh) is one whose white hair is more; if black hair is more, he is not old. In another narration from Abu Yusuf, he said 40 to 50. In another place, he said when he reaches 33 he becomes middle-aged. In another place: when he reaches 30 and his hair is mixed with white, he is middle-aged; if not mixed, he is young. In some narrations, consideration is by age because it is more observable for all in a uniform manner; in others, consideration is by signs and marks because people know each other by that, and they apply the name to the middle-aged when the sign exists, which is dappling and grey hair. He (rahimahullah) said: (And his in-laws are every prohibited relative from his wife) because it is related that he (peace be upon him)...
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq begins the commentary on the chapter of bequests to relatives and others. The author first explains why this chapter was delayed, then addresses the interpretation of 'neighbors' (جيران) in a bequest. He presents the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. Abu Hanifa holds that only those whose property adjoins the testator's property are included, because the word neighbor linguistically denotes adjacency, and since it is impossible to give to all, the closest should be preferred. He supports this with the hadith on preemption. The two disciples define neighbors as those living in the same locality and sharing a mosque, relying on custom and a hadith about the neighbor of the mosque. The commentary also discusses the inclusion of various individuals: slaves, free persons, Muslims, Dhimmis, widows, married women, etc. It then addresses cases of bequests to neighbors and to residents of Makkah, including how to distribute when the number is countable or uncountable. Finally, it defines the terms 'kahl' (middle-aged), 'shab' (youth), and 'shaykh' (old) with multiple views from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and begins to define 'in-laws' (أصهار) but the text cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
الجيران (al-jiran): Neighbors entitled to a bequest; defined by Abu Hanifa as adjacent property owners, and by Sahibayn as those living in the same locality and sharing a mosque.
الملاصق (al-mulasiq): One whose property adjoins that of another; the literal interpretation of neighbor in Abu Hanifa's view.
الكهل (al-kahl): Middle-aged person; defined variably between 30-40 or 40-50 years old, or by presence of grey hair.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), who is included in a bequest to 'neighbors'?
A) Only those whose property is adjacent
B) Those who live in the same locality and gather at the same mosque
C) All residents within 40 houses
D) Only male neighbors

Key Takeaway
The term 'neighbors' in a bequest is subject to a valid Hanafi internal dispute: Abu Hanifa restricts to adjacent properties, while the Sahibayn include the mosque community.

Interpreting 'Family' (أهله) and 'Lineage' (آله) in Wills
Explains legal meaning of terms like wife, family, lineage, and relatives in wills.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of أهله and آله in the context of wills and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding أهله.

Core Idea
In a will, 'أهله' is his wife (Abu Hanifa) or all dependents (Sahibayn); 'آله' is his paternal lineage.

When a testator uses terms like 'family' or 'lineage', the law must define who qualifies. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi positions on the scope of such terms, focusing on the dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions over the meaning of أهله, and the agreed definition of آله as the paternal tribe.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term used in the will
Determine whether the testator used أهله (his family) or آله (his lineage). Each term has a distinct legal meaning.
The text also covers examples like 'my son's wife' to illustrate determining the recipient at death.
2
For أهله, note the ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa restricts it to the wife; the Sahibayn extend it to all dependents (excluding slaves). Understand their respective proofs.
Abu Hanifa relies on literal meaning and Quranic usage; Sahibayn rely on customary usage in Quranic verses.
3
Examine the dalil of each
Abu Hanifa: 'وسار بأهله' (Quran 28:29) where أهله refers to his wife. Sahibayn: 'وأتوني بأهلكم أجمعين' (12:93) and 'فانجيناه وأهله' (7:83) where أهله includes household.
The dispute hinges on whether the term is حقيقة (literal) or عرفي (customary).
4
Derive the practical outcome
Under Abu Hanifa, only the wife receives the bequest for أهله. Under the Sahibayn, all dependents (spouse, children, etc.) share.
For آله, there is consensus that it means paternal lineage, excluding maternal relatives and children of daughters.

امرأته [الاعراف: ۸۳] والمراد من كان في عياله ولأبي حنيفة أن الاسم حقيقة للزوجة يشهد بذلك النص والعرف قال الله تعالى : وسار بأهله ﴾ [القصص : ۲۹] والمطلق ينصرف إلى الحقيقة المستعملة. قال رحمه الله : ( وآله أهل بيته وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام : «من تأهل ببلدة فهو منها» لأن الآل القبيلة التي ينسب إليها فيدخل فيه كل من ينسب إليه من قبل آبائه إلى أقصى أب له في الإسلام الأقرب والأبعد، والذكر والانثى والمسلم والكافر، والصغير والكبير فيه سواء، ولا يدخل فيه أولاد البنات وأولاد الأخوات ولا أحد من قرابة أمه لأنهم لا ينسبون إلى أبيه وإنما ينسبون إلى آبائهم فكانوا من جنس آخر لأن النسب يعتبر من الآباء وفي المبسوط ولو أوصى بماله لقربته فالقرابه من قبل الأب لأن القرب يثبت بالاتصال من الجانبين، فإن أوصى لذوي قرابته أو لذوي أرحامه فعند أبي حنيفة هو لكل ذي رحم محرم منه اثنان فصاعداً الأقرب وعندهما يستحقه الواحد ويستوي فيه المحرم وغير المحرم والبعيد والقريب وهو قول الشافعي . لهما القرابة اسم عام يعم الكل ويشملهم بدليل أنه لما نزل قوله تعالى : وانذر عشيرتك الأقربين ﴾ [الشعراء : ٢١٤] دعا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قبائل قريش وأنذرهم فأكثر بني هاشم ليس بمحرم منه وبعيد عنه في القرابة، ولأن إطلاق القريب في استعمال الكلام في الأباعد من الأقارب أكثر من إطلاقه على الأقرب من الأقارب فإنه يقال لمن بعد منه هذا قريب مني ولا يقال لمن قرب منه كالعم هذا قريبي والقرابة اسم جنس فيتناول الواحد فصاعداً كاسم الرجل. وأبو حنيفة اعتبر في استحقاق أربعة شرائط : أحدها أن يكون المستحق اثنين فصاعداً إذا كانت الوصية باسم الجمع وهو قوله قرابتي من القرب ومعنى الإجماع فيه وهو مقابلة الفرد بالفرد والجمع من وجه ملحق بالجمع من كل وجه في الميراث فكذا في الوصية لأنها أخت الميراث. والثاني أنه يعتبر الأقرب فالأقرب لأنه علق استحقاق المال باسم القرابة وفي الميراث يقدم الأقرب فالأقرب ويكون الأبعد محجوباً بالأقرب فكذا في الوصية لأنهما أخوان لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام الوصية أخت الميراث والأختية تقتضي الاستواء والمشاركة في أصل الاستحقاق والثالث أن يكون ذو رحم محرم من الموصي حتى إن أولاد العم لا تستحقه بهذه الوصية لأن المقصود من الوصية صلة القرابة فيختص بها من يستحق الصلة بالقرابة وهو القرابة المحرمة للنكاح الموجبة للصلة لأنه يتعلق بها صلة استحقاق النفقة والعتق عند دخوله في ملكه . والرابع أن يكون ممن يرث من الموصي لأن قصد الموصي صحة الوصية ولا تصح الوصية للوارث ويستوي فيه الرجال والنساء لأن اسم القرابة يتناولهما لصفة واحدة، وليس في لفظ الموصي ما يدل على تفضيل الذكر على الأنثى ولا يدخل فيه الوالدان والولد لأنهما لا ينطبق عليهما اسم القرابة لقوله تعالى للوالدين والأقربين [البقرة: ١٨٠] فقد عطف الأقربين على الوالدين والمعطوف غير المعطوف عليه، ولأن الجزئية والبعضية بينهما ثابتة واسم القرابة لا يطلق مع وجود الجزئية والبعضية في عرف الاستعمال. والجد والجدة وولد الولد من ذكر وأنثى يدخلون في هذه الوصية لأنهم ينسبون إليه بواسطة القريب، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أن الجد لا يدخل بمنزلة الأب لأن اسم الأب يتناوله ولا يتناول اسم القريب عند أبي حنيفة، فلو كان واحداً يستحق نصف الوصية لأن ما زاد على الواحد ليس له نهاية معلومة فلا يعتبر للمزاحم أكثر من الواحد كما في الميراث . قال رحمه الله : (وجنسه أهل بيت أبيه) لأن الانسان بأبيه فصار كأنه يتجنس قرابته حيث يدخل فيه جهة الأب والأم لأن الكل يسمون قرابته فلا يختص بشيء منهم، وكذا أهل نسبته وأهل نسبه فيكون حكمه حكم جميع ما ذكرنا ويدخل فيه الأب والجد لأن الأب أصل النسب والجد أصل نسب أبيه. وقال في الكافي : لو كان الأب الأكبر حياً لا يدخل تحت الوصية لأن الوصية للمضاف لا للمضاف إليه، ولو أوصت المرأة لجنسها أو لأهل بيتها لا يدخل ولدها لأن ولدها ينسب إلى أبيه لا إليها إلا أن يكون أبوه من قوم أبيها وقرابته. قال رحمه الله : ( وإن أوصى لأقاربه أو لذوي قرابته أو لأرحامه أو لأنسابه) فهي للأقرب فالأقرب . رب من كل ذي رحم محرم منه ولا يدخل الوالدان والولد والوارث ويكون للاثنين فصاعداً. وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : الوصية لكل من ينسب إلى أقصى أب له في الاسلام وإن لم يسلم بعد أن أدرك الاسلام أو أسلم على ما اختلف فيه المشايخ، وفائدة الاختلاف تظهر في مثل أبي طالب وعلي رضي الله عنه إذا وقعت الوصية لأقرباء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يدخل فيه أولاد أبي طالب وعلى لأن لفظة القريب حقيقة للكل إذ هي مشتقة من القرابة فيكون اسماً لكل من قامت به . فيتناول مواضع الخلاف ضرورة. ولأبي حنيفة أن الوصية أخت الميراث وفي الميراث يعتبر
Chapter of wills, section on will for relatives and others. ... [full literal translation would be very long; here summarized for brevity]. The text covers: if one says 'I bequeath to my son's wife' it applies to the wife at death; if to 'daughters' husbands' etc. 'His family' (أهله): according to Abu Hanifa is his wife; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) includes all dependents except slaves, based on custom and Quranic verses. 'His lineage' (آله): means his household/tribe, including all paternal relatives to the furthest ancestor in Islam, excluding children of daughters and maternal relatives. If one bequeaths to 'his relatives' or 'his kin': according to Abu Hanifa, conditions: at least two, the closest, mahram (unmarriageable), and not an heir; according to the two, one suffices and no mahram condition, and Shafi'i agrees with them. Abu Hanifa's four conditions are detailed. Then 'his kind/people of his father's house' includes paternal and maternal sides. Finally, if bequeathing to 'his relatives' etc., the ruling is for the closest mahram relative, at least two, excluding parents, children, and heirs, per Abu Hanifa; the two say for all relatives to the furthest ancestor who reached Islam, with a dispue about the Islam condition exemplified by Abu Talib and Ali.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the legal interpretation of various terms used in wills for family and relatives. It opens with practical examples: if someone bequeaths to 'my son's wife', it specifically means the wife at the time of the testator's death, not any subsequent wife. If there are multiple possible recipients, the heirs choose. Then it discusses the word أهله (family): Abu Hanifa restricts it to the wife because the word is literally used for wife in Quran and custom, while the two imams (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) extend it to all dependents (excluding slaves) based on the customary usage in Quranic verses where أهله includes household. For آله (lineage/people), the author explains it means the paternal tribe, including all relatives through the father's line to the furthest ancestor in Islam, excluding children of daughters and maternal relatives. The hadith 'من تأهل ببلدة فهو منها' supports this. Then the passage tackles the most detailed ikhtilaf: a will to أقاربه (his relatives) or ذوي قرابته (his kin). Abu Hanifa imposes four conditions: (1) at least two beneficiaries, because the plural form implies plurality, analogous to inheritance; (2) the closest relatives have priority, again by analogy with inheritance; (3) the beneficiary must be a mahram (unmarriageable relative), because the purpose is maintaining kinship ties which are strongest with mahram; (4) the beneficiary must not be an heir, because a will to an heir is invalid. Parents and children are excluded because the word قرابة does not apply to them in common usage (Quran separates الوالدين والأقربين). Grandparents and grandchildren are included. The two imams disagree: they consider the term general, covering even one person and non-mahram, citing Quranic call to 'عشيرتك الأقربين' which included non-mahram. They also argue custom uses 'qarib' for distant relatives. Abu Hanifa's view relies on the principle that the will is 'sister of inheritance' (الوصية أخت الميراث), so rules of inheritance apply. The later part discusses 'جنسه أهل بيت أبيه' (his kind/people of his father's house) which includes all relatives from both father and mother, but excludes the child of a testatrix because the child is attributed to the father. Finally, if the will is to أقاربه or similar, the same conditions apply per Abu Hanifa, while the two imams include all relatives up to the furthest ancestor who reached Islam, with a practical difference in cases like the relatives of the Prophet (ﷺ) regarding the inclusion of Abu Talib's children. The passage thus provides a comprehensive treatment of how different kinship terms are interpreted in Hanafi will law.

Key Terms
أهله (ahluhu): In the context of a will, according to Abu Hanifa it means his wife; according to the two imams it includes all dependents (except slaves) whom he supports.
آله (alihi): Refers to the paternal tribe/lineage, including all descendants through males back to the furthest ancestor in Islam, excluding descendants through females.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only the wife
B) All dependents including slaves
C) All dependents except slaves
D) All relatives

Key Takeaway
The meaning of family terms in wills is disputed within the Hanafi school, with implications for who receives the bequest: Abu Hanifa restricts أهله to the wife, while the Sahibayn include all dependents except slaves.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Conditions for Beneficiaries under a Will to 'Relatives' (أقاربه)
Explains legal meaning of terms like wife, family, lineage, and relatives in wills.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's four conditions for beneficiaries under a will to relatives, explain the opposing view of the Sahibayn, and apply the differences to practical cases.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa requires at least two, closest, mahram, and not heir; the Sahibayn and Shafi'i allow even one distant non-mahram.

When a testator bequeaths to 'my relatives', who qualifies? Abu Hanifa draws an analogy to inheritance, imposing strict conditions. This lesson examines his four conditions, the counterarguments from his companions, and the practical consequences of each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the will phrase
Determine whether the testator used أقاربي (my relatives), ذوي قرابتي (my kin), or similar. The ruling applies to all such phrases.
The text also covers terms like أرحامي (my womb relatives) and أنسابي (my lineages).
2
State Abu Hanifa's four conditions
List: (1) at least two beneficiaries, (2) the closest relatives have priority, (3) must be mahram (unmarriageable), (4) must not be an heir.
These conditions are based on the hadith 'الوصية أخت الميراث' (the will is the sister of inheritance).
3
State the Sahibayn's view and their dalil
The Sahibayn (and Shafi'i) allow even one beneficiary, with no mahram condition. They argue that the term قرابة is a general noun covering one or more, and that custom includes non-mahram.
They cite the Quranic verse 'وأنذر عشيرتك الأقربين' which included non-mahram like Abu Lahab.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa maintains that the plural form implies at least two, and the sisterhood with inheritance requires proximity and mahram. He also argues that the Quranic usage of 'الوالدين والأقربين' shows that الأقربين excludes parents, so the term is not fully general.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, a will to a single non-mahram invalidates that bequest; under the Sahibayn, it is valid.
5
Apply to a case
For example, a testator bequeaths to 'my relatives' and has only one distant cousin who is not mahram. Under Abu Hanifa, the bequest is invalid for that cousin; under the Sahibayn, the cousin takes all.
If there are two mahram relatives, both take under Abu Hanifa; under Sahibayn, the single non-mahram would take, etc.

Source Text

أوصيت لزوجه ابني بكذا فهو على زوجها يوم مات الموصي، ولو قال لأزواج ابنتي ولابنته أزواج قد طلقوا وزوج حال الموت لم يطلقها فالوصية للكل . ولو أوصى لامرأة ابنه فهذا على امرأة ابنه يوم موت الموصى وإنما يدخل تحت الوصية امرأة واحدة حتى لو كان لابنه امرأة يوم الوصية وتزوج بامرأة أخرى ثم مات الموصي فالخيار إلى الورثة يعطون أيتهما شاؤوا ويجبرون على أن يبينوا في أحدهما . قال رحمه الله وأهله زوجته وهذا عند امرأته [الاعراف: ۸۳] والمراد من كان في عياله ولأبي حنيفة أن الاسم حقيقة للزوجة يشهد بذلك النص والعرف قال الله تعالى : وسار بأهله ﴾ [القصص : ۲۹] والمطلق ينصرف إلى الحقيقة المستعملة. قال رحمه الله : ( وآله أهل بيته وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام : «من تأهل ببلدة فهو منها» لأن الآل القبيلة التي ينسب إليها فيدخل فيه كل من ينسب إليه من قبل آبائه إلى أقصى أب له في الإسلام الأقرب والأبعد، والذكر والانثى والمسلم والكافر، والصغير والكبير فيه سواء، ولا يدخل فيه أولاد البنات وأولاد الأخوات ولا أحد من قرابة أمه لأنهم لا ينسبون إلى أبيه وإنما ينسبون إلى آبائهم فكانوا من جنس آخر لأن النسب يعتبر من الآباء وفي المبسوط ولو أوصى بماله لقربته فالقرابه من قبل الأب لأن القرب يثبت بالاتصال من الجانبين، فإن أوصى لذوي قرابته أو لذوي أرحامه فعند أبي حنيفة هو لكل ذي رحم محرم منه اثنان فصاعداً الأقرب وعندهما يستحقه الواحد ويستوي فيه المحرم وغير المحرم والبعيد والقريب وهو قول الشافعي . لهما القرابة اسم عام يعم الكل ويشملهم بدليل أنه لما نزل قوله تعالى : وانذر عشيرتك الأقربين ﴾ [الشعراء : ٢١٤] دعا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قبائل قريش وأنذرهم فأكثر بني هاشم ليس بمحرم منه وبعيد عنه في القرابة، ولأن إطلاق القريب في استعمال الكلام في الأباعد من الأقارب أكثر من إطلاقه على الأقرب من الأقارب فإنه يقال لمن بعد منه هذا قريب مني ولا يقال لمن قرب منه كالعم هذا قريبي والقرابة اسم جنس فيتناول الواحد فصاعداً كاسم الرجل. وأبو حنيفة اعتبر في استحقاق أربعة شرائط : أحدها أن يكون المستحق اثنين فصاعداً إذا كانت الوصية باسم الجمع وهو قوله قرابتي من القرب ومعنى الإجماع فيه وهو مقابلة الفرد بالفرد والجمع من وجه ملحق بالجمع من كل وجه في الميراث فكذا في الوصية لأنها أخت الميراث. والثاني أنه يعتبر الأقرب فالأقرب لأنه علق استحقاق المال باسم القرابة وفي الميراث يقدم الأقرب فالأقرب ويكون الأبعد محجوباً بالأقرب فكذا في الوصية لأنهما أخوان لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام الوصية أخت الميراث والأختية تقتضي الاستواء والمشاركة في أصل الاستحقاق والثالث أن يكون ذو رحم محرم من الموصي حتى إن أولاد العم لا تستحقه بهذه الوصية لأن المقصود من الوصية صلة القرابة فيختص بها من يستحق الصلة بالقرابة وهو القرابة المحرمة للنكاح الموجبة للصلة لأنه يتعلق بها صلة استحقاق النفقة والعتق عند دخوله في ملكه . والرابع أن يكون ممن يرث من الموصي لأن قصد الموصي صحة الوصية ولا تصح الوصية للوارث ويستوي فيه الرجال والنساء لأن اسم القرابة يتناولهما لصفة واحدة، وليس في لفظ الموصي ما يدل على تفضيل الذكر على الأنثى ولا يدخل فيه الوالدان والولد لأنهما لا ينطبق عليهما اسم القرابة لقوله تعالى للوالدين والأقربين [البقرة: ١٨٠] فقد عطف الأقربين على الوالدين والمعطوف غير المعطوف عليه، ولأن الجزئية والبعضية بينهما ثابتة واسم القرابة لا يطلق مع وجود الجزئية والبعضية في عرف الاستعمال. والجد والجدة وولد الولد من ذكر وأنثى يدخلون في هذه الوصية لأنهم ينسبون إليه بواسطة القريب، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أن الجد لا يدخل بمنزلة الأب لأن اسم الأب يتناوله ولا يتناول اسم القريب عند أبي حنيفة، فلو كان واحداً يستحق نصف الوصية لأن ما زاد على الواحد ليس له نهاية معلومة فلا يعتبر للمزاحم أكثر من الواحد كما في الميراث . قال رحمه الله : (وجنسه أهل بيت أبيه) لأن الانسان بأبيه فصار كأنه يتجنس قرابته حيث يدخل فيه جهة الأب والأم لأن الكل يسمون قرابته فلا يختص بشيء منهم، وكذا أهل نسبته وأهل نسبه فيكون حكمه حكم جميع ما ذكرنا ويدخل فيه الأب والجد لأن الأب أصل النسب والجد أصل نسب أبيه. وقال في الكافي : لو كان الأب الأكبر حياً لا يدخل تحت الوصية لأن الوصية للمضاف لا للمضاف إليه، ولو أوصت المرأة لجنسها أو لأهل بيتها لا يدخل ولدها لأن ولدها ينسب إلى أبيه لا إليها إلا أن يكون أبوه من قوم أبيها وقرابته. قال رحمه الله : ( وإن أوصى لأقاربه أو لذوي قرابته أو لأرحامه أو لأنسابه) فهي للأقرب فالأقرب . رب من كل ذي رحم محرم منه ولا يدخل الوالدان والولد والوارث ويكون للاثنين فصاعداً. وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : الوصية لكل من ينسب إلى أقصى أب له في الاسلام وإن لم يسلم بعد أن أدرك الاسلام أو أسلم على ما اختلف فيه المشايخ، وفائدة الاختلاف تظهر في مثل أبي طالب وعلي رضي الله عنه إذا وقعت الوصية لأقرباء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يدخل فيه أولاد أبي طالب وعلى هذا وقعت الوصية على قول من شرط الاسلام ويدخلون على قول من شرط أدراك الاسلام ومن شرط إسلامه صرفه إلى أولاد علي لا غير، ولا يدخل أولاد عبد المطلب بالإجماع لأنه لم يدرك الاسلام. لهما أن الاسم يتناول الكل لأن لفظة القريب حقيقة للكل إذ هي مشتقة من القرابة فيكون اسماً لكل من قامت به . فيتناول مواضع الخلاف ضرورة. ولأبي حنيفة أن الوصية أخت الميراث وفي الميراث يعتبر
Chapter of wills, section on will for relatives and others. ... [full literal translation would be very long; here summarized for brevity]. The text covers: if one says 'I bequeath to my son's wife' it applies to the wife at death; if to 'daughters' husbands' etc. 'His family' (أهله): according to Abu Hanifa is his wife; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) includes all dependents except slaves, based on custom and Quranic verses. 'His lineage' (آله): means his household/tribe, including all paternal relatives to the furthest ancestor in Islam, excluding children of daughters and maternal relatives. If one bequeaths to 'his relatives' or 'his kin': according to Abu Hanifa, conditions: at least two, the closest, mahram (unmarriageable), and not an heir; according to the two, one suffices and no mahram condition, and Shafi'i agrees with them. Abu Hanifa's four conditions are detailed. Then 'his kind/people of his father's house' includes paternal and maternal sides. Finally, if bequeathing to 'his relatives' etc., the ruling is for the closest mahram relative, at least two, excluding parents, children, and heirs, per Abu Hanifa; the two say for all relatives to the furthest ancestor who reached Islam, with a dispue about the Islam condition exemplified by Abu Talib and Ali.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the legal interpretation of various terms used in wills for family and relatives. It opens with practical examples: if someone bequeaths to 'my son's wife', it specifically means the wife at the time of the testator's death, not any subsequent wife. If there are multiple possible recipients, the heirs choose. Then it discusses the word أهله (family): Abu Hanifa restricts it to the wife because the word is literally used for wife in Quran and custom, while the two imams (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) extend it to all dependents (excluding slaves) based on the customary usage in Quranic verses where أهله includes household. For آله (lineage/people), the author explains it means the paternal tribe, including all relatives through the father's line to the furthest ancestor in Islam, excluding children of daughters and maternal relatives. The hadith 'من تأهل ببلدة فهو منها' supports this. Then the passage tackles the most detailed ikhtilaf: a will to أقاربه (his relatives) or ذوي قرابته (his kin). Abu Hanifa imposes four conditions: (1) at least two beneficiaries, because the plural form implies plurality, analogous to inheritance; (2) the closest relatives have priority, again by analogy with inheritance; (3) the beneficiary must be a mahram (unmarriageable relative), because the purpose is maintaining kinship ties which are strongest with mahram; (4) the beneficiary must not be an heir, because a will to an heir is invalid. Parents and children are excluded because the word قرابة does not apply to them in common usage (Quran separates الوالدين والأقربين). Grandparents and grandchildren are included. The two imams disagree: they consider the term general, covering even one person and non-mahram, citing Quranic call to 'عشيرتك الأقربين' which included non-mahram. They also argue custom uses 'qarib' for distant relatives. Abu Hanifa's view relies on the principle that the will is 'sister of inheritance' (الوصية أخت الميراث), so rules of inheritance apply. The later part discusses 'جنسه أهل بيت أبيه' (his kind/people of his father's house) which includes all relatives from both father and mother, but excludes the child of a testatrix because the child is attributed to the father. Finally, if the will is to أقاربه or similar, the same conditions apply per Abu Hanifa, while the two imams include all relatives up to the furthest ancestor who reached Islam, with a practical difference in cases like the relatives of the Prophet (ﷺ) regarding the inclusion of Abu Talib's children. The passage thus provides a comprehensive treatment of how different kinship terms are interpreted in Hanafi will law.

Key Terms
قرابته (qarabatuhu): Relatives, specifically blood relatives from the father's side. In the will context, subject to ikhtilaf regarding mahram, number, and proximity.
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahim muhrim): A relative who is mahram (unmarriageable) due to blood relationship (e.g., father, brother, uncle). One of Abu Hanifa's conditions for eligibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is one of Abu Hanifa's conditions for a will to relatives?
A) The beneficiary must be a child
B) There must be at least two beneficiaries
C) The beneficiary must be wealthy
D) The bequest must be in multiples of 10

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's four conditions for a will to relatives—plurality, proximity, mahram, and non-heir—derive from the principle that the will is the sister of inheritance.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

6 min
Conditions for Bequest to Relatives: Who Qualifies?
Defines who qualifies as a relative for a bequest and the conditions of inclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which relatives are included in a bequest to 'relatives' under Hanafi law and apply the conditions of mahram and heirship.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'relatives' covers only mahram blood relatives who are potential heirs, excluding parents and children.

When a testator uses the phrase 'to my relatives' (qarabah), the Hanafi school imposes specific conditions to interpret the testator's intent. This passage clarifies that the term does not include everyone with a blood tie; rather, it targets those who are both mahram (unmarriageable kin) and potential heirs. We will examine the four conditions, the exclusion of parents and children, and the inclusion of grandparents, along with an internal Hanafi dispute about the grandfather.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four conditions
List the four conditions that a relative must satisfy to be included in a bequest: mahram, potential heir, not a parent or child, and the specific relation is one that obligates maintenance and inheritance.
The source text mentions the third and fourth conditions explicitly; the first two are implied by the opening.
2
Apply the mahram condition
Determine which relatives are mahram: brothers, uncles, aunts, nieces, nephews, etc. Exclude non-mahram relatives like cousins (children of paternal uncle). Use the principle that mahram ties obligate maintenance and create inheritance rights.
This excludes many distant relatives.
3
Apply the heir condition
The beneficiary must be a potential heir at the time of death (i.e., not already excluded as an heir). A bequest to an heir is invalid unless other heirs consent; thus, only those who would not inherit automatically are valid recipients. However, the condition here means the relative must be of a category that can inherit (e.g., not a non-Muslim relative excluded by religion) – note the source says 'mimman yarith' which may be a textual error; the expected meaning is 'mimman la yarith' (those who do not inherit). We follow the commentary's interpretation.
The source text seems to say 'mimman yarith' (from those who inherit) but the context suggests it means 'from those who can be potential heirs' i.e., not already an heir by default.
4
Exclude parents and children
Using Quran 2:180, the conjunction of 'aqarib' with 'parents' shows they are different categories. Also, parents and children are not called 'relatives' in common usage because they are considered partial of the testator. Thus, they are automatically excluded.
This is a linguistic argument (urf) supported by the Quran.
5
Resolve the intra-Hanafi dispute on grandfather
Al-Hasan narrated that Abu Hanifa excluded the grandfather, considering him a 'father'. The dominant opinion (zahir al-riwayah) includes him because he is related through an intermediate. This difference affects distribution when only a grandfather exists.
The mufta bihi is inclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قرابته أو لأرحامه أو لأنسابه فإن كان له عمان وخالان ولو كان له عم وخالان كان له في أصل الاستحقاق والثالث أن يكون ذو رحم محرم من الموصي حتى إن أولاد العم لا تستحقه بهذه الوصية لأن المقصود من الوصية صلة القرابة فيختص بها من يستحق الصلة بالقرابة وهو القرابة المحرمة للنكاح الموجبة للصلة لأنه يتعلق بها صلة استحقاق النفقة والعتق عند دخوله في ملكه . والرابع أن يكون ممن يرث من الموصي لأن قصد الموصي صحة الوصية ولا تصح الوصية للوارث ويستوي فيه الرجال والنساء لأن اسم القرابة يتناولهما لصفة واحدة، وليس في لفظ الموصي ما يدل على تفضيل الذكر على الأنثى ولا يدخل فيه الوالدان والولد لأنهما لا ينطبق عليهما اسم القرابة لقوله تعالى للوالدين والأقربين [البقرة: ١٨٠] فقد عطف الأقربين على الوالدين والمعطوف غير المعطوف عليه، ولأن الجزئية والبعضية بينهما ثابتة واسم القرابة لا يطلق مع وجود الجزئية والبعضية في عرف الاستعمال. والجد والجدة وولد الولد من ذكر وأنثى يدخلون في هذه الوصية لأنهم ينسبون إليه بواسطة القريب، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أن الجد لا يدخل بمنزلة الأب لأن اسم الأب يتناوله ولا يتناول اسم القريب عند أبي حنيفة، فلو كان واحداً يستحق نصف الوصية لأن ما زاد على الواحد ليس له نهاية معلومة فلا يعتبر للمزاحم أكثر من الواحد كما في الميراث .
His relatives or his kinsfolk or his relations: If he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, even if he has one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles... The third [condition] is that [the person] be a close relative who is a mahram of the testator, so that the children of a paternal uncle do not deserve [the bequest] by this bequest, because the purpose of the bequest is maintaining ties of kinship, so it is restricted to one who deserves maintaining ties through kinship, which is kinship that prohibits marriage and necessitates maintenance, because maintenance and manumission are attached to it when he enters into his ownership. The fourth [condition] is that he be among those who inherit from the testator because the testator intends the validity of the bequest, and a bequest to an heir is not valid. And men and women are equal in it because the term 'kinship' includes them with one attribute, and there is nothing in the testator's wording to indicate preference of male over female. And parents and children are not included because the term 'kinship' does not apply to them, due to His statement, may He be exalted: 'to parents and near relatives' [2:180], for He has joined 'near relatives' to 'parents', and the conjoined is different from the conjoined. And because partiality and part-whole relationship are established between them, and the term 'kinship' is not applied when there is partiality and part-whole relationship in common usage. And the grandfather, grandmother, and grandchild, male and female, are included in this bequest because they are related to him through a near relative. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that the grandfather is not included by virtue of the father because the term 'father' applies to him, and the term 'relative' does not apply to him according to Abu Hanifa. So if there is one [such relative], he deserves half the bequest because what is more than one has no known limit, so more than one is not considered as a competitor, as in inheritance.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the conditions for a bequest made to relatives using phrases like 'to my relatives', 'to my kinsfolk', or 'to my relations'. The commentary explains that according to Abu Hanifa, such a bequest is only for relatives who are mahram (blood relatives who are unmarriageable, such as siblings, uncles, aunts, etc.). Therefore, children of a paternal uncle are not included because they are not mahram; they are cousins. A key condition is that the beneficiary must be a potential heir at the time of death (i.e., not already excluded as an heir), because a bequest to an heir is invalid unless other heirs consent. Men and women are equal; there is no preference for males. Parents and children are excluded because in common usage the word 'relatives' does not apply to them; the Quranic verse (2:180) distinguishes 'parents' from 'near relatives'. Grandparents and grandchildren, however, are included because they are related through an intermediate. There is a difference within the Hanafi school: Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa that the grandfather is not included, because he is considered a father in terms of terminology. If only one such relative exists, that person takes half the bequest; if more than one, they share equally but the maximum number of shares is not predetermined.

Key Terms
قرابة (qarabah): Blood relationship; specifically, relatives who are mahram (unmarriageable).
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahm mahram): A relative through blood who is permanently prohibited for marriage (e.g., sister, aunt, niece, uncle, etc.).
وارث (warith): An heir at the time of death; a bequest to an heir is invalid unless consent is given by other heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, which of the following is a condition for a relative to be included in a bequest to 'relatives'?
A) The relative must be male
B) The relative must be mahram
C) The relative must be a parent or child
D) The relative must be a cousin

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest to 'relatives' only includes mahram blood relatives who are potential heirs, automatically excluding parents and children, and including grandparents per the relied-upon opinion.

Distribution of Bequest to Relatives: The Nearest-Relative Rule vs. Equal Shares
Applies the earlier rules to concrete cases with differing numbers of paternal and maternal uncles and aunts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on distribution of a bequest to relatives when both paternal and maternal uncles/aunts exist, and identify the difference between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).

Core Idea
In bequests to relatives, Abu Hanifa applies the nearest-relative rule (paternal over maternal); the disciples distribute equally.

This lesson applies the principle of 'al-aqrab fa al-aqrab' to concrete scenarios involving different combinations of paternal and maternal uncles and aunts. You will see how Abu Hanifa's preference for paternal relatives differs from the equal distribution approach of the two disciples, and learn an important condition about the timing of relationship assessment and a later fatwa on uncountable relatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
The passage presents three main scenarios: (1) two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, (2) one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, and (3) a paternal uncle, paternal aunt, maternal uncle, and maternal aunt. Each scenario has a specific distribution rule.
2
Apply Abu Hanifa's rule
For each scenario, determine the distribution according to Abu Hanifa. He prioritizes paternal relatives (closer in lineage) over maternal ones. When there are only paternal relatives, they take all; when mixed, paternal relatives take half or more.
Abu Hanifa's rule is based on analogy to inheritance: the nearest relative (in terms of lineage) is preferred.
3
Apply the disciples' rule
For the same scenarios, determine the distribution according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. They treat all relatives equally, dividing the bequest equally among all named categories.
The disciples consider the term 'relative' (qarib) to include all equally, regardless of paternal/maternal distinction.
4
Note additional rules
Identify two key points: (1) the relationship is considered at the time of the testator's death, not when the bequest is made; (2) if there is no mahram relative at death, the bequest is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. Also note the later fatwa that a bequest to uncountable relatives is valid (Muhammad ibn Salamah's view).
The uncountable relatives fatwa is an exception to the general rule; it is based on the act being a qurba (devotion).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في الأصل: ولو ترك الموصي ولداً يحوز ميراثه وترك عمين وخالين فالوصية عند أبي حنيفة للعمين، وإنما شرط قيام الولد كيلا يكون العمان وارثين وعند أبي يوسف ومحمد الوصية بين العمين والخالين أرباعاً لاستوائهم في تناول اسم القريب، ولو كان عماً وخالين فللعم النصف والباقي للخالين عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما الوصية بينهم بالسوية. وإن ترك عماً وعمة وخالاً وخالة فالوصية للعم والعمة عند أبي حنيفة. وفي الكافي : ولو أوصى لأقاربه وله عمان وخالان فالوصية لعميه عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يقسم بينهم أرباعاً، وكذا في قوله لأرحامه ولذوي أرحامه ولأنسابه ولذوي أنسابه ولو قال لذوي قرابته أو لذي نسبته أو لقرابته فالجواب ما ذكرنا إذ هنا لا يعتبر الجمع عند أبي حنيفة فإنه يدخل تحت الوصية الأقرب فالأقرب والواحد فصاعداً بلا خلاف. وفي الكافي ولو أوصى لذوي قرابته لا يشترط فيه الجمع لاستحقاق الكل حتى لو كان له وخالان فكله للعم عنده . قال : ويعتبر في هذه المسائل قرابة الموصى له وقت موت الموصي لا وقت الإيصاء. قال في الأصل: وإن لم يكن ذو رحم في هذه المسائل فالوصية باطلة عند أبي حنيفة. وفي النوازل وفي الظهيرية : الوصية إذا كانوا إلا يحصون اختلف المشايخ في جوازها قال بعضهم : إنها باطلة . وقال محمد بن سلمة : إنها جائزة وعليه الفتوى لأنها قرية لكونها صلة. ولو أوصى بثلث ماله للموص وصي عم
It is said in al-Asl: If the testator leaves a child who takes his inheritance and leaves two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then the bequest according to Abu Hanifa is for the two paternal uncles. The condition of the child's existence is only to ensure that the two paternal uncles are not heirs. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the bequest is divided between the two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles in fourths [each] because they are equal in receiving the name 'relative'. And if there is one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then for the paternal uncle is half and the rest for the two maternal uncles according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two [disciples] the bequest is divided among them equally. And if he leaves a paternal uncle and a paternal aunt and a maternal uncle and a maternal aunt, the bequest is for the paternal uncle and paternal aunt according to Abu Hanifa. And in al-Kafi: If he makes a bequest to his relatives and he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, the bequest is for his two paternal uncles according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two it is divided among them in fourths. And similarly in his saying 'to his kinsmen' or 'to his nearest kin' or 'to his relations' or 'to his next of kin', and if he says 'to his kin' or 'to his lineage' or 'to his relatives', the answer is what we mentioned, because here the plural is not considered according to Abu Hanifa, for the nearest and nearer enters under the bequest, and one or more without dispute. And in al-Kafi: If he makes a bequest to his kin [dhawi qarabatihi], plurality is not required because every one of them deserves, so even if he has one [maternal uncle] and two maternal uncles, all goes to the paternal uncle according to him. He said: In these matters, the relationship of the legatee is considered at the time of the testator's death, not at the time of the bequest. It is said in al-Asl: If there is no mahram relative in these matters, the bequest is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. In al-Nawazil and al-Zahiriyyah: If the bequest is made to relatives who cannot be counted, the masters differed on its validity. Some said it is invalid. Muhammad ibn Salamah said: It is valid, and the fatwa is upon it, because it is an act of kinship devotion due to being a connection. And if he makes a bequest of one-third of his wealth to ...
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage applies the previous rules to concrete scenarios with specific numbers of uncles and aunts. The core principle for Abu Hanifa is 'the nearest relative, then the next nearest' (al-aqrab fa al-aqrab). Therefore, when there is both a paternal uncle and a maternal uncle, the paternal uncle is considered closer (since he shares the same lineage) and takes priority. In the first scenario: testator leaves a child (so that the uncles are not heirs, i.e., they are prevented from inheriting by the child) and leaves two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles. Abu Hanifa gives all to the two paternal uncles. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) give equal shares to all four uncles (each gets one quarter). If there is one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, Abu Hanifa gives the paternal uncle half and the two maternal uncles the other half (so paternal uncle gets 1/2, each maternal uncle gets 1/4). The disciples give equal thirds to all three (each gets 1/3). In the scenario with a paternal uncle, a paternal aunt, a maternal uncle, and a maternal aunt, Abu Hanifa restricts to the paternal uncle and aunt only. The passage also clarifies that the same rules apply whether the testator uses 'aqarib', 'arham', 'ansab', etc. However, if the phrase is 'dhawi qarabatihi' (his kin), even Abu Hanifa does not require plurality; even one relative can take the whole bequest. An important procedural rule: the relationship is considered at the time of the testator's death, not when the bequest was made. If there is no mahram relative at death, the bequest is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. The passage ends with a fatwa issue: if the number of relatives is so vast that they cannot be counted (e.g., distant relatives), there is a difference among later scholars: some say the bequest is invalid (since it cannot be executed), but Muhammad ibn Salamah says it is valid, and this is the fatwa upon which practice relies, because it is an act of devotion (qurba) to maintain ties. The text cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
الأقرب فالأقرب (al-aqrab fa al-aqrab): The rule of distributing to the nearest relative first, then the next nearest, as in inheritance.
قربة (qurba): An act of devotion or piety; here it refers to the bequest itself as a way of maintaining family ties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a testator has one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, how should the bequest be distributed?
A) All to the paternal uncle
B) Paternal uncle gets half, maternal uncles get the other half equally
C) Divided equally among all three
D) Paternal uncle gets two-thirds, maternal uncles one-third

Key Takeaway
When a bequest is to relatives without specification, Abu Hanifa applies the nearest-relative rule, prioritizing paternal over maternal; the Sahibayn distribute equally; and a later fatwa validates bequests to uncountable relatives as an act of devotion.

Bequest to One's Household and Kin
Explaining who is included in a bequest to household, kin, and family

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who is included in a bequest made to 'ahl baytih' or 'jinsih' according to the Hanafi school and explain the role of istihsan in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
A bequest to family includes all paternal dependents, not just the wife, because Hanafi istihsan overrides strict analogy.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the scope of bequests made to one's household, kin, or family. Understanding these definitions is crucial for correctly executing a testator's wishes. The Hanafi school employs istihsan to expand the bequest beyond mere analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms
Recognize the terms 'ahl baytih', 'jinsih', 'ahlih', and 'aaliyhi' and their legal significance.
These terms are often used interchangeably in the passage.
2
Define 'ahl baytih'
According to the text, 'ahl baytih' includes every paternal relative up to the farthest forefather in Islam, regardless of religion, gender, or proximity.
Excluded are children of daughters, sisters' children, and maternal relatives unless the daughter's husband is from paternal uncles.
3
Recognize the qiyas argument
For a bequest to 'ahlih', qiyas (analogy to the wife being part of the family) would restrict it to the wife alone.
This is the baseline ruling before istihsan.
4
Apply the istihsan override
Istihsan (juristic preference) overrides qiyas to include all dependents whom the testator is obliged to support and who live in his house, excluding slaves.
The ruling extends to dependents in multiple locations due to the general wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النصف ولهما النصف ولو له عم وعمة استويا ولولد فلان للذكر والأنثى سواء ولورثة لأهل بيته دخل في الوصية كل من يتصل به من قبل آبائه إلى اقصى أب له في الاسلام يستوي فيه المسلم والكافر والذكر والأنثى، والمحرم والقريب والبعيد. ونسب الإنسان من قبل أبيه وكل من يتصل به من قبل آبائه إلى أقصى أب في الإسلام فهو من أهل بيت نسبته فيدخل تحت الوصية ولا يدخل تحت الوصية أولاد البنات قال : إلا إذا كان أزواجهن من بني أعمام الوصي وعشيرته، ولا يدخل فيه أولاد الأخوات ولا أحد من قرابة أم الموصي . وإذا أوصى الجنسه فهذا وما لو أوصى لأهل بيته سواء لأن الانسان من جنس قوام ابيه ألا ترى أن إبراهيم ولد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان قريشاً وكذلك أولاد الخلفاء يصلحون للخلافة وإن كان أكثرهم من الإماء واعتبروا من جنس قوم آبائهم فصار قوله وجنسه وقوله لأهل بيته سواء وكل من يتصل به إلى اقصى أب في الاسلام يدخل تحت الوصية إن أوصى لآله فهذا وما لو أوصى لأهل بيته سواء لأنهم يستعملون استعمالاً واحداً يقال آل محمد وأهل بيت محمد وآل عباس وأهل بيت عباس. إذا اوصى بثلث ماله لأهله أو لأهل فلان فالوصية للزوجة خاصة دون من سواها قياساً إلا أنا استحسنا وجعلنا الوصية لكل من يكون عياله وتلزمه نفقتهم ويضمهم بيته ولا يدخل تحت الوصية مماليكه فلو كان أهل في بلدتين أو في بيتين دخلوا تحت الوصية لعموم اللفظ .
The half and for them the half. And if he has a paternal uncle and a maternal aunt they are equal. And for the children of so-and-so, male and female are equal. And for the heirs of his household: everyone who is connected to him through his forefathers up to the farthest forefather in Islam enters into the bequest, and it is equal for Muslim and disbeliever, male and female, non-marriageable relative and distant relative. A person's lineage is from his father, and everyone connected to him through his forefathers up to the farthest forefather in Islam is of his household lineage and enters under the bequest. Children of daughters do not enter under the bequest unless their husbands are from the sons of the testator's paternal uncles and his tribe. Children of sisters and no one from the mother's relatives enter. If he bequeathed to his kin (jinsih), this is the same as bequeathing to his household because a person is from the kin of his father's people. Do you not see that Ibrahim, the son of the Messenger of Allah, was Qurayshi, and likewise the children of the caliphs are suitable for the caliphate even if most of them are from slave women, and they are considered from the kin of their fathers' people. So his saying 'his kin' and his saying 'his household' are the same. And everyone connected to him up to the farthest forefather in Islam enters under the bequest. If he bequeathed to his family (aaliyhi), this is the same as bequeathing to his household because they are used interchangeably. It is said 'Aal Muhammad' and 'Ahl Bayt Muhammad', and 'Aal Abbas' and 'Ahl Bayt Abbas'. If he bequeaths a third of his property to his family (ahlihi) or to the family of so-and-so, the bequest is for the wife specifically, excluding others, by qiyas, except that we apply istihsan and make the bequest for everyone who is his dependent and whose maintenance is obligatory upon him and who are gathered in his house. His slaves do not enter under the bequest. If the family is in two towns or two houses, they enter under the bequest due to the generality of the wording.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the scope of a bequest made to the testator's 'household' (ahl baytih) or 'kin' (jinsih) or 'family' (ahlih). It is a commentary expanding on a matn. The author first defines 'ahl baytih' as all paternal relatives up to the farthest forefather who embraced Islam, including Muslims and non-Muslims, males and females, close and distant. This is based on lineage through the father. Excluded are children of daughters, children of sisters, and maternal relatives, unless the daughters' husbands are from the testator's paternal cousins (bani a'mam). The terms 'jinsih' and 'ahl baytih' are treated as synonymous because a person's 'jins' (kin) is determined by the father's lineage, as illustrated by Ibrahim the son of the Prophet being considered Qurayshi. Similarly, 'aaliyhi' (his family) is equivalent to 'ahl baytih'. The passage then discusses a bequest to 'ahlih' (his family) applying qiyas first: by analogy to the wife being part of the family, only she would receive. But istihsan overrides this, granting the bequest to all dependents (those he is obligated to support), but excluding slaves. If the family resides in multiple locations, the bequest applies to all due to the general wording.

Key Terms
أهل بيت (ahl bayt): In this passage, all paternal relatives of the testator up to the farthest forefather in Islam.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference overriding qiyas to give the bequest to all dependents, not just the wife.
جنس (jins): Kin, here synonymous with 'ahl bayt' because a person's lineage is from his father's people.
قياس (qiyas): Analogy that would restrict bequest to wife alone based on her being the prototypical family member.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, who is included in a bequest to 'ahl baytih'?
A) All relatives including maternal and daughters' children
B) Only the testator's wife and children
C) All paternal relatives up to the farthest forefather in Islam
D) Only Muslim relatives

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school interprets a bequest to 'family' broadly through istihsan, including all paternal dependents, unlike strict qiyas which restricts it to the wife.

Bequest to 'Children of So-and-So': Tribal Scope and Gender Inclusion
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bequest to named children with tribal scope issues

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi dispute on gender inclusion in bequests to 'children of so-and-so' and apply the tribal hierarchy to determine the scope of a bequest.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'children of so-and-so' includes males only or both? It depends on whether so-and-so is a tribe or a specific person.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a common scenario: a testator bequeaths to 'children of so-and-so'. The ruling is not straightforward—it hinges on whether the named person is a tribal ancestor or a specific individual, and whether the bequest includes females. We will explore the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and also learn the tribal hierarchy (sha'b, qabila, imara, etc.) used to interpret such bequests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main scenarios
The passage distinguishes between two cases: when 'so-and-so' is a tribal ancestor (e.g., Tamim for Banu Tamim) and when 'so-and-so' is a specific individual (a particular father). The ruling differs in each scenario.
If the named is a tribe, the bequest includes all descendants within that tribal level. If a specific father, gender inclusion becomes disputed.
2
Apply the tribal hierarchy for tribal bequests
The hierarchy is: sha'b, qabila, imara, batn, fakhdh, fasila. When a bequest is made to a tribe name (e.g., 'Bani Qushayr'), it includes all subdivisions below that level but excludes higher levels. For example, if bequest is to 'Bani Quraysh' (an imara), it includes imara and below (batn, fakhdh, fasila) but excludes qabila and sha'b (Kinana, Mudar).
Memorize the hierarchy: شعب → قبيلة → عمارة → بطن → فخذ → فصيلة.
3
Determine gender inclusion for a specific father
If the named is a specific individual with children, there is a clear intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that only male children receive the bequest; female children receive nothing. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that males and females share equally.
There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa supporting Muhammad's view, making the school's position nuanced.
4
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf, a father with three sons and two daughters would give the entire bequest to the three sons. Under Muhammad, all five children share equally.
The text does not give a mufta bihi; both views are recorded for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولولد فلان للذكر والأنثى سواء) يعني لو أوصى لأولاد فلان للذكر والأنثى سواء لأن اسم الولد يشمل الكل وليس في اللفظ شيء يقتضي التفضيل فتكون الوصية بينهم على السواء. قال في العيني على الهداية قال الفقيه أبو الليث : ولو أوصى لولد فلان ولفلان ولد الصلب وله ولد ولد فالوصية كلها له وليس لولد الولد شيء. وقال شمس الأئمة في شرح الكافي : لو كان له ولد واحد ذكراً أو أنثى فجميع الوصية له. وذكر الكرخي بخلاف ذلك فقال : إذا أوصى الأئمة بثلث ماله فلان وله ولد الصلب ذكر أو أنثى كان الثلث لهم بعد أن يكون اثنين فصاعداً، ولم يكن لولد ولده شيء ولو كان لصلبه واحد أو له ولد ولد كان للذي لصلبه نصف الثلث ذكراً كان أو أنثى، وكان ما يبقى لولد ولده بالسوية الذكر والأنثى وهذا كله قول أبي حنيفة .اهـ. ولو أوصى لولد فلان أو لابن فلان فهذا على وجهين : إما إن كان فلان أبا قبيلة يعني أبا جماعة كثيرة كتميم لبني تميم وأسد لبني أسد أو كان فلان أبا خاص ليس باب الجماعة كثيرة. واعلم بأن أولى الأسامي في هذا الباب الشعب - بفتح الشين شعباً لتشعب القبائل منها ولهذا بدأ الله تعالى بذكره فقال يا أيها الناس إنا خلقناكم من ذكر وأنثى وجعلناكم شعوباً وقبائل لتعارفوا [الحجرات : ١٣ ]ثم القبيلة ثم العمارة ثم البطن ثم الفخذ ثم الفصيلة، فمضر شعب، وكنانة قبيلة، وقريش عمارة، وقصي بطن وهاشم أبو جد النبي له فخذ، وعبد المطلب فصيلة. وإذا أوصى لبني قريش وقريش عمارة فإنه لا يدخل تحت الوصية أولاد مضر وكنانة وتدخل أولاد قريش وأولاده قصي وهاشم وأولاده والعباس وأولاده. وإذا أوصى لبني قصي وهم بطنه فإنه لا يدخل تحت الوصية أولاد مضر وكنانة وأولاد قريش ويدخل من دونهم وإذا أوصى لبني هاشم الذي . هو فخذ فإنه لا يدخل تحت الوصية من فوقهم ويدخل من دونهم من أولاد الفصيلة. ولو أوصى لبني الفصيلة فإنه لا يدخل تحت الوصية أولاد العباس وأولاد أبي طالب وأولاد علي ولا يدخل من فوقهم قال الشيخ الزاهد أحمد الطواويسي: مثال الفخذ مضر، ومثال البطن بنو هاشم ومثال القبيلة قريش ومثال الشعب العرب. وفي الذخيرة: وإذا أوصى لولد على وهم فخذ لا يدخل تحته من فوقهم وهم أولاد قريش لأنهم فوقهم فإذا عرفنا هذه الجملة جئنا إلى المسألة التي ذكرناها وهو ما إذا أوصى بثلث ماله لبني فلان وفلان القبيلة وله أولاد ذكور وإناث فإن ثلث ماله يكون بين الذكور والإناث من أولاده بالسوية إذا كانوا يحصون بالإجماع، وإن كن نساء كلهن ولم يذكر هذا في الكتاب قلوا : ينبغي أن يكون الثلث لهن. وإن كانوا ذكوراً كلهم يستحقون كله فأما إذا كان فلان أباً واحداً أولاد ذكور كلهم فإن ثلث ماله ،لهم وإن كان أولاد اناثاً كلهن لا شيء لهن وإن كان فلان أباً خاصاً وأولاد فلان ذكوراً أو أناثاً اختلفوا فيه ؛ قال أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف الوصية للذكور منهم دون للإناث. وقال محمد بأن الوصية للذكور والإناث بينهم بالسوية إذا كانوا يحصون، وقد روى أبو يوسف بن خالد السمتي عن أبي حنيفة مثل قول محمد. حكى الكرخي أنه كان
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And for the children of so-and-so, male and female are equal). That is, if he bequeaths to the children of so-and-so, male and female are equal because the word 'child' includes all, and there is nothing in the wording that necessitates preference, so the bequest is equal among them. Al-Ayni said in his commentary on Al-Hidayah that Abu al-Layth said: If he bequeaths to the child of so-and-so and so-and-so has a direct child and also a grandchild, the entire bequest is for the direct child, and nothing for the grandchild. Shams al-A'imma said in Sharh al-Kafi: If he has one child, male or female, the entire bequest is for him/her. Al-Karkhi mentioned contrary: If the imams bequeath one third of their property to so-and-so, and he has a direct child male or female, the third goes to them if they are two or more, and nothing to grandchildren. If he has only one direct child or has grandchildren, then the direct child gets half of the third, male or female, and the remainder goes to the grandchildren equally, male and female. All this is the saying of Abu Hanifa. End. If he bequeaths to the children of so-and-so or to the son of so-and-so, this has two aspects: either so-and-so is the father of a tribe, meaning the father of a large group, like Tamim for Banu Tamim and Asad for Banu Asad, or so-and-so is a specific father, not a group. Know that the first of the names in this chapter is al-sha'b (with fatha on shin) for the branches of tribes from it, and for this reason Allah began with it, saying: 'O mankind, indeed We have created you from male and female and made you peoples and tribes that you may know one another' (49:13). Then al-qabila, then al-imara, then al-batn, then al-fakhdh, then al-fasila. Thus Mudar is a sha'b, Kinana is a qabila, Quraysh is an imara, Qusay is a batn, Hashim is the father of the prophet's grandfather, so he is a fakhdh, and Abd al-Muttalib is a fasila. If he bequeaths to Banu Quraysh and Quraysh is an imara, then the children of Mudar and Kinana do not enter under the bequest, but the children of Quraysh, his children, Qusay, Hashim, his children, al-Abbas and his children do enter. If he bequeaths to Banu Qusay, who are his batn, then the children of Mudar, Kinana, and Quraysh do not enter, but those below them enter. If he bequeaths to Banu Hashim, who is a fakhdh, then those above do not enter, but those below him from the children of the fasila enter. If he bequeaths to Banu al-Fasila, then the children of al-Abbas, Abu Talib, and Ali do not enter, and those above them do not enter. Al-Shaykh al-Zahid Ahmad al-Ta'awisi said: Example of fakhdh is Mudar, example of batn is Banu Hashim, example of qabila is Quraysh, example of sha'b is Arabs. And in al-Dhakhira: If he bequeaths to the child of Ali and they are a fakhdh, then those above them, who are the children of Quraysh, do not enter because they are above them. Now that we know this summary, we come to the issue we mentioned: if he bequeaths one third of his property to Banu so-and-so, and so-and-so is a tribe, and he has sons and daughters, then the third is divided equally among his sons and daughters by consensus if they are countable. If they are all women, and this is not mentioned in the book, they said: it should be for them. If they are all men, they deserve all. But if so-and-so is a single father, and all his children are males, then the third is for them; if all are females, nothing for them. If so-and-so is a specific father and his children are males or females, they differed in it: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf said the bequest is for the males only, not the females. Muhammad said the bequest is for males and females equally if they are countable. Abu Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti narrated from Abu Hanifa like Muhammad's saying. Al-Karkhi narrated that he was...
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses bequests to 'children of so-and-so' (walad fulan). The matn states that males and females are equal because 'walad' includes both. The commentary then reports several opinions. According to Abu al-Layth, if the testator bequeaths to 'walad fulan' and the named person has both direct children and grandchildren, the bequest goes entirely to the direct child. Shams al-A'imma states that if there is only one child, that child takes all. Al-Karkhi reports Abu Hanifa's view: if there are two or more direct children, they take the entire bequest; if only one direct child, that child gets half and grandchildren get the other half, equally. The passage then shifts to when the bequest is to 'bani fulan' (sons of so-and-so) and distinguishes two cases: (1) fulan is a tribal ancestor (e.g., Tamim for Banu Tamim) — then the bequest includes all descendants within that tribal level (sha'b, qabila, etc.) defined by a hierarchy (sha'b, qabila, imara, batn, fakhdh, fasila). Examples are given: Mudar is a sha'b, etc. If the bequest is to Banu Quraysh (an imara), it excludes higher levels like Mudar and includes lower ones. (2) Fulan is a specific individual (a particular father). Then the ruling depends on the gender of the children: if all are males, they take; if all are females, they get nothing (according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad says males and females share equally if they are countable. There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa supporting Muhammad's view. The text cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
شعب (shu'b): The broadest tribal division; e.g., Mudar is a shu'b of Arabs.
قبيلة (qabila): Tribe; e.g., Kinana is a qabila under the shu'b of Mudar.
عمارة (imara): Sub-tribe; e.g., Quraysh is an imara under Kinana.
بطن (batn): Clan; e.g., Qusay is a batn of Quraysh.
فخذ (fakhdh): Sub-clan; e.g., Hashim is a fakhdh of Qusay.
فصيلة (fasila): Family; e.g., Abd al-Muttalib is a fasila of Hashim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if someone bequeaths to 'children of Zayd' and Zayd is a specific father with sons and daughters, who receives the bequest?
A) Both sons and daughters equally
B) Only the sons
C) Only the daughters
D) The bequest is invalid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest to 'children of so-and-so' requires determining whether the named is a tribal ancestor (applying hierarchy) or a specific person (where Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf limit to males, Muhammad includes females).

Bequest to 'Child of So-and-So': Who is Included?
States the ruling on bequest to 'ولد فلان' and intra-Hanafi differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the differing Hanafi positions on whether a grandchild is included in a bequest to 'walad fulan' when the testator has a direct child.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'child of so-and-so' normally excludes grandchildren if there is a direct child, but a minority view gives them half.

When a testator bequeaths to 'the child of so-and-so' (ولد فلان), and that person has both a direct child and a grandchild, who gets the bequest? The term 'walad' can be ambiguous. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement among early authorities, led by Abu al-Layth, Shams al-A'imma, and al-Karkhi who reports a divergent opinion from Abu Hanifa himself. Understanding these nuances is crucial for drafting valid bequests and interpreting the testator's intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting rulings
Read the three opinions reported: Abu al-Layth gives all to the direct child; Shams al-A'imma agrees; al-Karkhi reports that if there is one direct child, that child gets half and the grandchild gets half, but if two or more direct children, they take all.
Focus on who gets what and under what conditions.
2
Note the authority behind each view
Abu al-Layth and Shams al-A'imma are later Hanafi authorities. Al-Karkhi attributes his view to Abu Hanifa himself. Determine the strength of each transmission.
The passage does not indicate the mufta bihi, so we evaluate the basis.
3
Analyze the underlying reason for the dispute
The dispute centers on whether the term 'walad' in a bequest includes grandchildren (walad al-walad) when there is a direct child. Some say it strictly means direct children; others give a share to grandchildren when there is only one direct child.
Consider if there is a qiyas to inheritance rules or a textual interpretation.
4
Apply to a simple scenario
Test your understanding: A bequest to 'walad Zaid'. Zaid has one son and one grandson. Apply each opinion and state the outcome.
This step consolidates the legal operation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سمى كتاب الوصايا/ باب الوصية للأقارب وغيرهم والأنثى سواء لأن اسم الولد يشمل الكل وليس في اللفظ شيء يقتضي التفضيل فتكون الوصية بينهم على السواء. قال في العيني على الهداية قال الفقيه أبو الليث : ولو أوصى لولد فلان ولفلان ولد الصلب وله ولد ولد فالوصية كلها له وليس لولد الولد شيء. وقال شمس الأئمة في شرح الكافي : لو كان له ولد واحد ذكراً أو أنثى فجميع الوصية له. وذكر الكرخي بخلاف ذلك فقال : إذا أوصى [؟] بثلث ماله فلان وله ولد الصلب ذكر أو أنثى كان الثلث لهم بعد أن يكون اثنين فصاعداً، ولم يكن لولد ولده شيء ولو كان لصلبه واحد أو له ولد ولد كان للذي لصلبه نصف الثلث ذكراً كان أو أنثى، وكان ما يبقى لولد ولده بالسوية الذكر والأنثى وهذا كله قول أبي حنيفة .اهـ.
It is called the Book of Bequests / Chapter of Bequest to Relatives and Others. And the female is the same because the term 'child' includes all, and there is nothing in the wording that necessitates preference, so the bequest is divided equally among them. He said in al-‘Ayni on al-Hidayah: Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: If someone makes a bequest to the child of so-and-so, and so-and-so has a direct child and also a grandchild, the entire bequest goes to the direct child, and the grandchild gets nothing. And Shams al-A'imma said in Sharh al-Kafi: If he has only one child, male or female, the entire bequest goes to that child. And al-Karkhi mentioned contrary to that: He said: If the testator [?] bequeaths one-third of his wealth to so-and-so, and so-and-so has a direct child, male or female, the third is for them if they are two or more, and his grandchild gets nothing; but if he has only one direct child or he has a grandchild, then the direct child gets half of the third, male or female, and the remaining goes to his grandchild equally between male and female. All of this is the saying of Abu Hanifa. End quote.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the ruling on a bequest made to 'the child of so-and-so' (ولد فلان) when the named person (فلان) is a specific individual (أب خاص). The basic rule is that the term 'ولد' includes both male and female children equally unless there is an indication otherwise. The author first cites al-‘Ayni's commentary on al-Hidayah, quoting Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi: if the testator bequests to the child of someone who has a direct child (ولد الصلب) and also a grandchild (ولد الولد), the bequest goes entirely to the direct child, excluding the grandchild. Then Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi is quoted: if the person has only one child, that child gets the whole bequest. Then al-Karkhi reports a contrary opinion from Abu Hanifa: if the testator bequeaths one-third of his wealth to so-and-so, and so-and-so has two or more direct children, the third is divided among them; if there is only one direct child, that child gets half of the third, and the remaining half goes to the grandchild; but if there are no direct children, the grandchild gets nothing. Al-Karkhi attributes this to Abu Hanifa. The passage highlights an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether a grandchild can be included under the term 'ولد' when the testator has a direct child. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not stated here, but the author presents the different views.

Key Terms
ولد الصلب (walad al-sulb): Direct child (son or daughter) of a person, as opposed to a grandchild.
ولد الولد (walad al-walad): Grandchild (child of one's child).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when a testator bequeaths to 'walad fulan' and fulan has one direct child and one grandchild, what does Abu al-Layth rule?
A) The bequest is split equally between the direct child and grandchild.
B) The bequest goes entirely to the direct child.
C) The bequest goes entirely to the grandchild.
D) The bequest is void.

Key Takeaway
In a bequest to 'walad fulan', the Hanafi school predominantly excludes grandchildren if there is a direct child, but a minority view (from Abu Hanifa) gives the grandchild half when only one direct child exists.

The Six Levels of Arab Tribes and Bequests to Tribal Groups
Defines tribal hierarchy and inclusion rule for bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six levels of Arab tribal classification (sha'b, qabilah, 'imarah, batn, fakhdh, fasilah) and apply the rule that a bequest to a group at a given level includes all lower levels but excludes higher levels.

Core Idea
A bequest to a tribe reaches only those at the named level and below; higher ancestors are excluded.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a systematic classification of Arab tribal levels, derived from the Quranic verse in al-Hujurat. Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for interpreting bequests to tribal groups, because the Hanafi jurists have detailed rules about who is included depending on which level the testator named. In this lesson, we will explore the six levels and see how they determine the distribution of a bequest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the tribal levels
List the six levels from highest to lowest: sha'b, qabilah, 'imarah, batn, fakhdh, fasilah.
2
Memorize the examples
Note the classic examples given: Mudar (sha'b), Kinanah (qabilah), Quraysh ('imarah), Qusayy (batn), Hashim (fakhdh), 'Abd al-Muttalib (fasilah).
These examples are traditional and help anchor the levels.
3
Understand the inclusion rule
When a bequest is made to a group at a certain level, only those at that level and below are included; those above are excluded.
For example, a bequest to a qabilah includes its 'imarah, batn, etc., but not a higher sha'b.
4
Apply the rule to the example of Quraysh
Bequest to Banu Quraysh ('imarah) includes children of Quraysh and below (Qusayy, Hashim, etc.) but excludes Mudar and Kinanah.
The passage explicitly lists these inclusions and exclusions.
5
Apply the rule to the testator's own children
If the testator bequeaths to Banu Fulān (where Fulān is a tribe) and he has his own children, they share equally by consensus.
This is a separate ruling when the testator is himself a member of the named tribe.

وإناثاً لا غير وإن كان أولاد البنات اناثاً كلهن فلا شك أنه لهن، وفي الذخيرة سأل عن هذه المسألة فقال : أولاد البنات لا يدخلون تحت الوصية ثم أنشد :، بنونا بنو أبنائنا وبناتنا أبناء الرجال الأباعد بنوهن فإذا كان هو أباً فخذاً فأولاد الأولاد يدخلون تحت الوصية حال قيام ولد الصلب، وإن لم يكن له ولد إلا ولداً واحداً كان الثلث له بخلاف ما لو أوصى الأولاد فلان وله ولد واحد فإنه يستحق النصف، وإذا أوصى
