الله العلوية والشيعية والفقهاء والعلماء وأصحاب الحديث صحت الوصية.
If he makes a bequest to the child of so-and-so or to the son of so-and-so, then this is of two types: either so-and-so is a tribal ancestor, meaning the ancestor of a large group, like Tamim for Banu Tamim and Asad for Banu Asad, or so-and-so is a specific individual, not the ancestor of a large group. Know that the highest of the names in this chapter is al-sha‘b (plural: shu‘ūb), from which tribes branch out. For this reason, Allah the Exalted began with it, saying, 'O mankind, indeed We have created you from male and female and made you peoples (shu‘ūb) and tribes (qabā’il) that you may know one another' (al-Hujurat 13). Then al-qabīlah, then al-‘imārah, then al-batn, then al-fakhdh, then al-fasīlah. Mudar is a sha‘b, Kinānah is a qabīlah, Quraysh is an ‘imārah, Qusayy is a batn, Hāshim (the great-grandfather of the Prophet) is a fakhdh, and ‘Abd al-Muttalib is a fasīlah. If he makes a bequest to Banī Quraysh, and Quraysh is an ‘imārah, then the children of Mudar and Kinānah are not included under the bequest, but the children of Quraysh, and his children Qusayy and Hāshim and his children, and al-‘Abbās and his children are included. If he makes a bequest to Banī Qusayy, and they are his batn, then the children of Mudar and Kinānah and the children of Quraysh are not included, but those below them are included. If he makes a bequest to Banī Hāshim, who is a fakhdh, then those above them are not included, but those below them from the children of the fasīlah are included. If he makes a bequest to Banī al-fasīlah, then the children of al-‘Abbās, the children of Abī Tālib, and the children of ‘Alī are not included, nor those above them. Al-Shaykh al-Zāhid Ahmad al-Ṭawāwīsī said: An example of a fakhdh is Mudar, an example of a batn is Banū Hāshim, an example of a qabīlah is Quraysh, and an example of a sha‘b is the Arabs. In al-Dhakhīrah: If he makes a bequest to the child of ‘Alī, and they are a fakhdh, then those above them are not included – they are the children of Quraysh because they are above them. So when we know this summary, we come to the issue we mentioned: that if he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to Banī Fulān, and Fulān is a tribe, and he (the testator) has male and female children, then his one-third wealth is divided equally among his male and female children if they are countable according to consensus. If they are all females and this is not mentioned in the book, they said: the third should be for them. If they are all males, they deserve all of it. But if so-and-so is a specific individual (abā wāḥid) and his children are all males, then his one-third wealth is for them; if his children are all females, then nothing is for them. If so-and-so is a specific ancestor and the children of so-and-so are males or females, they differed: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf said the bequest is for the males among them, not for the females. And Muhammad said the bequest is for the males and females equally among them if they are countable. And Abu Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti narrated from Abu Hanifa similar to Muhammad’s saying. Al-Karkhi narrated that he used to say: what was mentioned in this narration is Abu Hanifa’s latter opinion, and what Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti narrates is his first opinion. And he used to attribute to Abu Hanifa an opinion that was first and last in this issue, saying: his first opinion is qiyas (analogical reasoning) and his latter opinion is istihsan (juristic preference). If so-and-so has no direct children (awlād sulbiyyah) and he has children (awlād) – do they enter under the bequest? They all enter. And if he has daughters (awlād banāt), they do not enter under the bequest. If they are all males, or males and females only, and if the children of the daughters are all females, then there is no doubt that it is for them. In al-Dhakhīrah: He asked about this issue and said: The children of daughters do not enter under the bequest. Then he recited: 'Our sons are the sons of our sons, and our daughters are the sons of distant men.' Something: Fulān. This is if he made a bequest to Banī Fulān. But if he made a bequest to the child of Fulān, and Fulān has only daughters, they enter under the bequest, unlike if he made a bequest to Banī Fulān, and Fulān has only daughters – nothing is for them. If Fulān has sons and daughters, then the third is among them all, and his one-third wealth is divided equally among them, no preference of males over females. He said: If he has a pregnant wife, what is in her womb also enters the bequest. And grandchildren do not enter under this bequest, like 'child of Fulān' and 'child of Fulān' etc. In reality, the one who is born to Fulān and the one from whom his son and his direct daughter are born. As for the child of his son or his daughter, that is born from his son or his daughter and is not generated from – and the reality of this name is for the direct child. So as long as Fulān has a direct child, his grandson does not enter. This is if Fulān is a specific individual (abā khāṣṣan). If he is a fakhdh ancestor, then grandchildren enter under the bequest even in the presence of a direct child. If he has no child except one, the third is for him, unlike if he made a bequest to the children of Fulān and he has one child – then he takes half. If he makes a bequest to the children of Fulān and Fulān has no direct children, then the children of sons enter under the bequest. And do the children of daughters enter? There are two narrations regarding the entry of sons of daughters. As for daughters of daughters, they do not enter the bequest, in one narration. If he makes a bequest to the children of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, the ‘Alawīs, the Shī‘īs, the jurists, the scholars, and the hadith narrators, the bequest is valid.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into the classification of Arab tribal levels (شعب, قبيلة, عمارة, بطن, فخذ, فصيلة) and applies these distinctions to the interpretation of bequests. It begins by distinguishing between a bequest to 'ولد فلان' when فلان is a tribal ancestor (أب قبيلة) versus a specific individual (أب خاص). For tribal ancestors, the passage provides a detailed hierarchy: the highest level is الشعب (e.g., Mudar), followed by القبيلة (e.g., Kinanah), then العمارة (e.g., Quraysh), then البطن (e.g., Qusayy), then الفخذ (e.g., Hashim), then الفصيلة (e.g., 'Abd al-Muttalib). When a bequest is made to a group at a certain level, only those belonging to that level and lower levels are included; higher levels are excluded. For example, a bequest to Banu Quraysh (an 'imarah) includes the children of Quraysh and those below (Qusayy, Hashim, etc.) but not those above (Mudar, Kinanah). The text then applies this to the original case: if a testator bequeaths one-third of his wealth to 'Banu Fulān' and Fulān is a tribe (qabīlah), and the testator has children, the third is divided equally among his male and female children if they are countable (yuhsawun) by consensus; if all are females, they get the third; if all are males, they take all. If Fulān is a specific individual (abā wāḥid) and his children are all males, they take the third; if females, they get nothing. If Fulān is a specific ancestor (abā khāṣṣan) and his children are mixed, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf give the bequest to males only, while Muhammad gives equally. A narration from Abu Hanifa via Abu Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti supports Muhammad, and al-Karkhi reconciles this as Abu Hanifa having two opinions: first qiyas (males only), second istihsan (equal). Then the passage discusses grandchildren: if the named person has no direct children, his grandchildren enter; but if he has direct children, grandchildren are excluded unless the named person is a fakhdh, in which case grandchildren enter even in presence of direct children. The poem 'بنونا بنو أبنائنا...' is cited to emphasize that grandchildren through daughters are not considered direct descendants for this purpose. Finally, the passage distinguishes between bequests to 'بني فلان' and 'ولد فلان': in the former, if فلان has only daughters, they get nothing; in the latter, they get everything. This is a complex passage requiring careful parsing of the tribal hierarchy and its legal implications.

Key Terms
شعب (sha‘b (pl. shu‘ūb)): The highest level of Arab tribal classification; e.g., Mudar is a sha‘b.
قبيلة (qabīlah): A tribe; second level below sha‘b; e.g., Kinanah is a qabīlah.
عمارة (‘imārah): A sub-tribe; third level; e.g., Quraysh is an ‘imārah.
بطن (batn): A clan; fourth level; e.g., Qusayy is a batn.
فخذ (fakhdh): A sub-clan; fifth level; e.g., Hashim is a fakhdh.
فصيلة (fasīlah): The smallest tribal unit; sixth level; e.g., ‘Abd al-Muttalib is a fasīlah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths one-third of his wealth to 'Banī Qusayy' and Qusayy is a batn, who is included in the bequest according to the passage?
A) All descendants of Mudar.
B) All descendants of Quraysh.
C) Only descendants of Qusayy and those below (e.g., Hashim, ‘Abd al-Muttalib).
D) Only the direct children of Qusayy.

Key Takeaway
The six-level tribal hierarchy (sha'b to fasilah) determines inclusion in bequests: a named group includes itself and all lower levels, but excludes higher ancestors.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
advanced
12 min
Intra-Hanafi Disputes on Bequests to the Descendants of a Specific Individual
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bequest distribution and grandchild entry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two opinions of Abu Hanifa (qiyas and istihsan) regarding distribution of a bequest to the children of a specific individual, and explain the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and apply the rule for including grandchildren.

Core Idea
When a bequest names a specific individual's descendants, the Hanafi school splits on whether females are included — Abu Hanifa's istihsan and Muhammad say yes, while his qiyas and Abu Yusuf say no.

This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi disputes arising from bequests to the children of a specific person (not a tribe). The passage records two opinions from Abu Hanifa, and a disagreement between his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. We will also see how grandchildren are treated, and the difference between the phrases 'Bani Fulān' and 'Walid Fulān'. Mastering these nuances is essential for correctly applying Hanafi law in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between two types of testator's children
When the named is a specific individual (ab khass), the testator's own male children take the bequest; females take nothing according to Abu Hanifa's first opinion and Abu Yusuf.
This is the qiyas-based opinion.
2
Identify the second opinion of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa later adopted istihsan, giving equally to males and females. Muhammad also holds this view.
Al-Karkhi reconciles these as qiyas vs istihsan.
3
Reconcile the two opinions
Al-Karkhi explains that the first is qiyas (analogical reasoning), the second is istihsan (juristic preference).
Both are attributed to Abu Hanifa.
4
Determine inclusion of grandchildren
If the named has no direct children, grandchildren enter. If he has direct children, grandchildren are excluded unless the named is a fakhdh (where they enter even with direct children).
The poem 'بنونا بنو أبنائنا...' is cited to support excluding grandchildren through daughters.
5
Distinguish between Bani and Walad
A bequest to 'Bani Fulān' when Fulān has only daughters gives nothing to them, but a bequest to 'Walid Fulān' includes daughters.
This distinction is crucial for drafting wills.

الباب الشعب - بفتح الشين شعباً لتشعب القبائل منها ولهذا بدأ الله تعالى بذكره فقال يا أيها الناس إنا خلقناكم من ذكر وأنثى وجعلناكم شعوباً وقبائل لتعارفوا [الحجرات : ١٣ ]ثم القبيلة ثم العمارة ثم البطن مضر، ومثال البطن بنو هاشم ومثال القبيلة قريش ومثال الشعب العرب. وفي الذخيرة: وإذا أوصى لولد على وهم فخذ لا يدخل تحته من فوقهم وهم أولاد قريش لأنهم فوقهم فإذا عرفنا هذه الجملة جئنا إلى المسألة التي ذكرناها وهو ما إذا أوصى بثلث ماله لبني فلان وفلان القبيلة وله أولاد ذكور وإناث فإن ثلث ماله يكون بين الذكور والإناث من أولاده بالسوية إذا كانوا يحصون بالإجماع، وإن كن نساء كلهن ولم يذكر هذا في الكتاب قلوا : ينبغي أن يكون الثلث لهن. وإن كانوا ذكوراً كلهم يستحقون كله فأما إذا كان فلان أباً واحداً أولاد ذكور كلهم فإن ثلث ماله ،لهم وإن كان أولاد اناثاً كلهن لا شيء لهن وإن كان فلان أباً خاصاً وأولاد فلان ذكوراً أو أناثاً اختلفوا فيه ؛ قال أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف الوصية للذكور منهم دون للإناث. وقال محمد بأن الوصية للذكور والإناث بينهم بالسوية إذا كانوا يحصون، وقد روى أبو يوسف بن خالد السمتي عن أبي وإناثاً لا غير وإن كان أولاد البنات اناثاً كلهن فلا شك أنه لهن، وفي الذخيرة سأل عن هذه المسألة فقال : أولاد البنات لا يدخلون تحت الوصية ثم أنشد :، بنونا بنو أبنائنا وبناتنا أبناء الرجال الأباعد بنوهن : شيء فلان هذا إذا أوصى لبني فلان فأما إذا أوصى لولد فلان ولفلان بنات لا غير دخلن تحت الوصية بخلاف ما لو أوصى لبني فلان ولفلان بنات لا شيء لهن، فإن كان لفلان بنون وبنات فالثلث بينهم عندهم جميعاً ويكون ثلث ماله بينهم بالسوية لا يفضل الذكور على الاناث قال : فإن كانت له امرأة حامل دخل. ما في بطنها في الوصية أيضاً ولا تدخل أولاد الأولاد تحت هذه الوصيه كولد فلان وولد فلان وولد فلان في الحقيقة من يولد لفلان وللذي يولد منه ابنه وابنته الصلبه فأما ولد ابنه أو ابنته يولد من ابنه أو ابنته ولم يتولد من وكان حقيقة هذا الاسم لولد الصلب فما دام لفلان ولد صلبه لا يدخل ولد ابنه. وهذا إذا كان فلان أباً خاصاً، فإذا كان هو أباً فخذاً فأولاد الأولاد يدخلون تحت الوصية حال قيام ولد الصلب، وإن لم يكن له ولد إلا ولداً واحداً كان الثلث له بخلاف ما لو أوصى الأولاد فلان وله ولد واحد فإنه يستحق النصف، وإذا أوصى لأولاد فلان وليس لفلان أولاد لصلبه يدخل تحت الوصية أولاد البنين وهل يدخل فيه أولاد البنات؟ ففيه روايتان في دخول بني البنات، وأما بنات البنات لا يدخلون في الوصية رواية واحدة ولو أوصى لأولاد رسول الله الله العلوية والشيعية والفقهاء والعلماء وأصحاب الحديث صحت الوصية.
If he makes a bequest to the child of so-and-so or to the son of so-and-so, then this is of two types: either so-and-so is a tribal ancestor, meaning the ancestor of a large group, like Tamim for Banu Tamim and Asad for Banu Asad, or so-and-so is a specific individual, not the ancestor of a large group. Know that the highest of the names in this chapter is al-sha‘b (plural: shu‘ūb), from which tribes branch out. For this reason, Allah the Exalted began with it, saying, 'O mankind, indeed We have created you from male and female and made you peoples (shu‘ūb) and tribes (qabā’il) that you may know one another' (al-Hujurat 13). Then al-qabīlah, then al-‘imārah, then al-batn, then al-fakhdh, then al-fasīlah. Mudar is a sha‘b, Kinānah is a qabīlah, Quraysh is an ‘imārah, Qusayy is a batn, Hāshim (the great-grandfather of the Prophet) is a fakhdh, and ‘Abd al-Muttalib is a fasīlah. If he makes a bequest to Banī Quraysh, and Quraysh is an ‘imārah, then the children of Mudar and Kinānah are not included under the bequest, but the children of Quraysh, and his children Qusayy and Hāshim and his children, and al-‘Abbās and his children are included. If he makes a bequest to Banī Qusayy, and they are his batn, then the children of Mudar and Kinānah and the children of Quraysh are not included, but those below them are included. If he makes a bequest to Banī Hāshim, who is a fakhdh, then those above them are not included, but those below them from the children of the fasīlah are included. If he makes a bequest to Banī al-fasīlah, then the children of al-‘Abbās, the children of Abī Tālib, and the children of ‘Alī are not included, nor those above them. Al-Shaykh al-Zāhid Ahmad al-Ṭawāwīsī said: An example of a fakhdh is Mudar, an example of a batn is Banū Hāshim, an example of a qabīlah is Quraysh, and an example of a sha‘b is the Arabs. In al-Dhakhīrah: If he makes a bequest to the child of ‘Alī, and they are a fakhdh, then those above them are not included – they are the children of Quraysh because they are above them. So when we know this summary, we come to the issue we mentioned: that if he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to Banī Fulān, and Fulān is a tribe, and he (the testator) has male and female children, then his one-third wealth is divided equally among his male and female children if they are countable according to consensus. If they are all females and this is not mentioned in the book, they said: the third should be for them. If they are all males, they deserve all of it. But if so-and-so is a specific individual (abā wāḥid) and his children are all males, then his one-third wealth is for them; if his children are all females, then nothing is for them. If so-and-so is a specific ancestor and the children of so-and-so are males or females, they differed: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf said the bequest is for the males among them, not for the females. And Muhammad said the bequest is for the males and females equally among them if they are countable. And Abu Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti narrated from Abu Hanifa similar to Muhammad’s saying. Al-Karkhi narrated that he used to say: what was mentioned in this narration is Abu Hanifa’s latter opinion, and what Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti narrates is his first opinion. And he used to attribute to Abu Hanifa an opinion that was first and last in this issue, saying: his first opinion is qiyas (analogical reasoning) and his latter opinion is istihsan (juristic preference). If so-and-so has no direct children (awlād sulbiyyah) and he has children (awlād) – do they enter under the bequest? They all enter. And if he has daughters (awlād banāt), they do not enter under the bequest. If they are all males, or males and females only, and if the children of the daughters are all females, then there is no doubt that it is for them. In al-Dhakhīrah: He asked about this issue and said: The children of daughters do not enter under the bequest. Then he recited: 'Our sons are the sons of our sons, and our daughters are the sons of distant men.' Something: Fulān. This is if he made a bequest to Banī Fulān. But if he made a bequest to the child of Fulān, and Fulān has only daughters, they enter under the bequest, unlike if he made a bequest to Banī Fulān, and Fulān has only daughters – nothing is for them. If Fulān has sons and daughters, then the third is among them all, and his one-third wealth is divided equally among them, no preference of males over females. He said: If he has a pregnant wife, what is in her womb also enters the bequest. And grandchildren do not enter under this bequest, like 'child of Fulān' and 'child of Fulān' etc. In reality, the one who is born to Fulān and the one from whom his son and his direct daughter are born. As for the child of his son or his daughter, that is born from his son or his daughter and is not generated from – and the reality of this name is for the direct child. So as long as Fulān has a direct child, his grandson does not enter. This is if Fulān is a specific individual (abā khāṣṣan). If he is a fakhdh ancestor, then grandchildren enter under the bequest even in the presence of a direct child. If he has no child except one, the third is for him, unlike if he made a bequest to the children of Fulān and he has one child – then he takes half. If he makes a bequest to the children of Fulān and Fulān has no direct children, then the children of sons enter under the bequest. And do the children of daughters enter? There are two narrations regarding the entry of sons of daughters. As for daughters of daughters, they do not enter the bequest, in one narration. If he makes a bequest to the children of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, the ‘Alawīs, the Shī‘īs, the jurists, the scholars, and the hadith narrators, the bequest is valid.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into the classification of Arab tribal levels (شعب, قبيلة, عمارة, بطن, فخذ, فصيلة) and applies these distinctions to the interpretation of bequests. It begins by distinguishing between a bequest to 'ولد فلان' when فلان is a tribal ancestor (أب قبيلة) versus a specific individual (أب خاص). For tribal ancestors, the passage provides a detailed hierarchy: the highest level is الشعب (e.g., Mudar), followed by القبيلة (e.g., Kinanah), then العمارة (e.g., Quraysh), then البطن (e.g., Qusayy), then الفخذ (e.g., Hashim), then الفصيلة (e.g., 'Abd al-Muttalib). When a bequest is made to a group at a certain level, only those belonging to that level and lower levels are included; higher levels are excluded. For example, a bequest to Banu Quraysh (an 'imarah) includes the children of Quraysh and those below (Qusayy, Hashim, etc.) but not those above (Mudar, Kinanah). The text then applies this to the original case: if a testator bequeaths one-third of his wealth to 'Banu Fulān' and Fulān is a tribe (qabīlah), and the testator has children, the third is divided equally among his male and female children if they are countable (yuhsawun) by consensus; if all are females, they get the third; if all are males, they take all. If Fulān is a specific individual (abā wāḥid) and his children are all males, they take the third; if females, they get nothing. If Fulān is a specific ancestor (abā khāṣṣan) and his children are mixed, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf give the bequest to males only, while Muhammad gives equally. A narration from Abu Hanifa via Abu Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti supports Muhammad, and al-Karkhi reconciles this as Abu Hanifa having two opinions: first qiyas (males only), second istihsan (equal). Then the passage discusses grandchildren: if the named person has no direct children, his grandchildren enter; but if he has direct children, grandchildren are excluded unless the named person is a fakhdh, in which case grandchildren enter even in presence of direct children. The poem 'بنونا بنو أبنائنا...' is cited to emphasize that grandchildren through daughters are not considered direct descendants for this purpose. Finally, the passage distinguishes between bequests to 'بني فلان' and 'ولد فلان': in the former, if فلان has only daughters, they get nothing; in the latter, they get everything. This is a complex passage requiring careful parsing of the tribal hierarchy and its legal implications.

Key Terms
أب خاص (ab khāṣṣ): A specific individual ancestor, not a tribal ancestor (e.g., a named person like Zaid).
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; here, Abu Hanifa's first opinion applied qiyas to limit the bequest to males.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; Abu Hanifa's second opinion used istihsan to include females equally.
ولد الصلب (walad al-ṣulb): Direct child of a person, as opposed to grandchildren.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, when a bequest is made to 'Bani Fulān' and Fulān has only daughters, what is the ruling?
A) The daughters receive the bequest.
B) Nothing is given to the daughters.
C) The bequest is invalid.
D) The bequest goes to the testator's own children.

Key Takeaway
When a bequest names a specific individual's descendants, the Hanafi school splits on whether females are included; Abu Hanifa's istihsan and Muhammad say yes, while his qiyas and Abu Yusuf say no.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Bequests to Religious and Professional Groups
Ruling on bequests to groups

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequests to unspecified groups and apply the condition that makes such bequests valid.

Core Idea
A bequest to a non-countable group is invalid unless it specifies the poor among them.

In Hanafi law, a bequest must be made to a specific beneficiary or a countable group. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq addresses bequests to groups like the descendants of the Prophet, the ‘Alawīs, and the fuqahā’. The key principle is that if the group is too large to be enumerated (لا يحصون) and the term does not indicate poverty, the bequest is invalid. However, if the bequest is specifically to the poor among them, it becomes valid. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and application of this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the groups mentioned
List the groups: 'children of the Prophet' (أولاد رسول الله), 'Alawīs (العلوية), fuqahā’ (الفقهاء), and teachers of children (معلمي الصبيان).
2
Note the ruling for each group
For children of the Prophet: restricted to the children of al-Hasan and al-Husayn. For ‘Alawīs and fuqahā’: general bequest invalid; only valid if to their poor. For teachers: waqf valid because most are poor.
The rationale for invalidity: the group is not countable (لا يحصون) and the term does not indicate need.
3
Recognize the decisive condition
The condition that transforms an invalid bequest into a valid one is specification of poverty (فقر). When the bequest is to 'the poor' of that group, it becomes valid.
This is based on the prevalence of poverty among some groups (e.g., teachers).
4
Understand the underlying principle
A bequest to a general, non-countable group is invalid because the beneficiaries are unknown and the bequest cannot be executed. Specifying poverty makes them identifiable as a category of needy recipients.
The same principle applies to waqf; if poverty is prevalent, it is as if explicitly stipulated.
5
Apply the rule to a new case
Consider a bequest 'to the scholars of this city.' It is invalid because scholars are not a countable group and the term does not indicate poverty. But 'to the poor scholars' would be valid.
This demonstrates the practical operation of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسأل الفقيه أبو جعفر عن رجل أوصى لأولاد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فذكر أن ابا نصر بن يحيى كان يقول : الوصية لأولاد الحسن والحسين ولا تكون لغيرهما وأما العمرية فهل يدخلون في الوصية؟ قال : ينظر كل من كان ينسب إلى الحسن والحسين ولا يكون لغيرهما، فأما العمرية فهل يدخلون في هذه الوصية ويتصل بما في هذه الوصية لأنه كان رضي الله عنه زوج ابنتيه من ولد عمر رضي الله عنه . وأذا أوصى للعلوية فقد حكى عن الفقيه أبي جعفر أنه لا يجوز لأنهم لا يحصون وليس في هذا الاسم ما ينبيء عن الفقر أو ذي الحاجة. ولو أوصى لفقراء العلوية يجوز وعلى هذا الوصية للفقهاء لا تجوز ولو أوصى لفقرائهم يجوز، وقد حكي بعض مشايخنا أن الوقف على معلمي الصبيان في المساجد يجوز لأن عامتهم فقراء والفقر فيهم الغالب فصار حكم غلبة الفقر كالمشروط . قال الشيخ الإمام شمس الأمة الحلواني : كان البحر الرائق/ ج ۹/ م ١٩ هو هذه عن
Al-Faqih Abu Ja‘far was asked about a man who made a bequest to the children of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. He mentioned that Abu Nasr ibn Yahya used to say: The bequest is for the children of al-Hasan and al-Husayn, and not for others. As for the ‘Umarīs (descendants of ‘Umar), do they enter the bequest? He said: It is considered that everyone who is attributed to al-Hasan and al-Husayn, and it is not for others. As for the ‘Umarīs, do they enter into this bequest and connect to what is in this bequest because he (رضي الله عنه) married his two daughters to the children of ‘Umar (رضي الله عنه)? And if he makes a bequest to the ‘Alawīs, it has been reported from al-Faqih Abu Ja‘far that it is not valid because they are not countable (lā yuhsawun), and there is nothing in this name that indicates poverty or need. If he makes a bequest to the poor among the ‘Alawīs, it is valid. And on this, a bequest to the jurists (fuqahā’) is not valid, but if he makes a bequest to their poor, it is valid. And some of our shaykhs reported that a waqf for the teachers of children (mu‘allimī al-ṣibyān) in the mosques is valid because most of them are poor, and poverty is prevalent among them, so the ruling of the prevalence of poverty is like a condition. Al-Shaykh al-Imam Shams al-Ummah al-Halwanī said: 'al-Bahr al-Ra’iq, volume 9, part 19, this... about'.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This concluding passage of the chapter deals with bequests to specific religious and professional groups. Al-Faqih Abu Ja‘far is asked about a bequest to 'the children of the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ)'. Abu Nasr ibn Yahya restricts this to the children of al-Hasan and al-Husayn, excluding others. The 'Umarīs (descendants of ‘Umar ibn al-Khattab) are not included in such a bequest because they are not descendants of the Prophet. Next, a bequest to the 'Alawīs (descendants of ‘Ali) is invalid because the group is too large to be enumerated (لا يحصون) and the term does not indicate poverty or need. However, if the bequest is specifically to the poor among the ‘Alawīs, it is valid. The same ruling applies to bequests to the fuqahā’ (jurists): a general bequest to them is invalid due to lack of specification and countable nature, but a bequest to their poor is valid. The passage notes that a similar principle applies to waqf for teachers of children in mosques: since poverty is prevalent among them, it is as if poverty is explicitly stipulated, making the waqf valid. This section highlights the Hanafi rule that a bequest to an unspecified group that is too large to be counted or does not indicate need is invalid, but if it is to the poor among them, it becomes valid.

Key Terms
العلوية (al-‘Alawiyyah): Descendants of ‘Ali ibn Abi Talib (رضي الله عنه).
العمرية (al-‘Umariyyah): Descendants of ‘Umar ibn al-Khattab (رضي الله عنه) through marriage with the Prophet's family.
الفقهاء (al-fuqahā’): Jurists; a general group that is not countable for bequest purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a bequest to the 'Alawis (descendants of ‘Ali) valid?
A) Always valid regardless of specification.
B) Valid only if they are scholars.
C) Valid if it is for the poor among them.
D) Never valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest to a general, non-countable group is invalid unless it specifies the poor among them, and this rule applies consistently across groups like 'Alawis, fuqaha', and even waqf for teachers.

Conditions for Valid Bequests to General Groups
Rulings on bequests to specific groups

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid bequest to a general group and distinguish between a faqih and a student of fiqh.

Core Idea
A bequest to a general group is valid only if they are poor and countable; students are not Fuqaha.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the rules of bequests (wasiyyah) to various religious groups. The Hanafi school requires that such bequests be directed to a determinate group or to the poor of that group. Understanding these conditions prevents invalid bequests that executors cannot fulfill.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest object
Determine which group the testator named (e.g., Alawiyya, Fuqaha, students).
2
Check countability and poverty
If the group is not countable or poverty is not indicated, the bequest is invalid unless restricted to the poor.
Examples: 'Alawiyya' is not countable; 'poor Fuqaha' is valid.
3
Distinguish true Faqih from student
Only a true faqih (master jurist) is included; a mutafaqqih (student) is not considered a faqih.
The passage quotes Faqih Abu Ja'far: the student has no share.
4
Apply the ruling on distribution
If the bequest is to a poor countable group, the executor may give to one poor person (Abu Yusuf) or must give to at least two (Muhammad).
The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أوصى لأولاد رسول الله العلوية والشيعية والفقهاء والعلماء وأصحاب الحديث صحت الوصية. وسأل الفقيه أبو جعفر عن رجل أوصى لأولاد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فذكر أن ابا نصر بن يحيى كان يقول : الوصية لأولاد الحسن والحسين ولا تكون لغيرهما وأما العمرية فهل يدخلون في الوصية؟ قال : ينظر كل من كان ينسب إلى الحسن والحسين ولا يكون لغيرهما، فأما العمرية فهل يدخلون في هذه الوصية ويتصل بما في هذه الوصية لأنه كان رضي الله عنه زوج ابنتيه من ولد عمر رضي الله عنه . وأذا أوصى للعلوية فقد حكى عن الفقيه أبي جعفر أنه لا يجوز لأنهم لا يحصون وليس في هذا الاسم ما ينبيء عن الفقر أو ذي الحاجة. ولو أوصى لفقراء العلوية يجوز وعلى هذا الوصية للفقهاء لا تجوز ولو أوصى لفقرائهم يجوز، وقد حكي بعض مشايخنا أن الوقف على معلمي الصبيان في المساجد يجوز لأن عامتهم فقراء والفقر فيهم الغالب فصار حكم غلبة الفقر كالمشروط . قال الشيخ الإمام شمس الأمة الحلواني : كان الإمام القاضي يقول على هذا القياس : إذا أوصى لطلبه علم كورة كذا أو لطلبة علم كذا يجوز، ولو أعطى الوصي واحداً من فقراء الطلبة أو من فقراء العلوية جاز عند أبي يوسف، وعند محمد لا يجوز إلا إذا صرف إلى اثنين منهم وإذا أوصى للشيعة ومحبيه قال محمد: اعلم بأن كل مسلم شيعة ومحب لآل رسول له ، وأما ما وقع عليهم الوهم من أنهم الذين يعرفون بالميل إليهم وصاروا موسومين بذلك دون غيرهم فقد قيل الوصية باطلة قياساً إذا كانوا لا يحصون، وإذا أوصى لفقراء الفقهاء حكي عن الفقيه أبي جعفر أنه قال : الفقيه عندنا من بلغ من الفقه الغاية وليس المتفقة بفقيه. وليس له من الوصية بنصيب قال الفقيه أبو جعفر : إنه لم يكن في بلدنا أحد يسمى فقيهاً غير أبي بكر الأعمش شيخنا وقد أهدى أبو بكر الفارسي مالاً كثيراً لطلبة العلم حين نادوه في مجلس أيها الفقيه. وإذا أوصى لأهل العلم ببلدة كذا فإنه يدخل فيه أهل الفقه وأهل الحديث ولا يدخل من يتعلم الحكمة. وفي الخانية : ولا يدخل من يتعلم الحكمة مثل كلام الفلسفة وغيره لأن هؤلاء يسمون المتفلسفة لا طلبة علم وهل يدخل فيه المتكلمون؟ فلا ذكر لهذه المسألة أيضاً في الكتب وعن أبي القاسم أن كتب الكلام ليست كتب علم يعني في العرف ولا يسبق إلى الفهم فلا يدخل تحت كتب العلم، فعلى قياس هذه المسألة لا يدخل في الوصية المتكلمون . وإذا أوصى بثلث ماله على فقراء طلبة العلم من أصحاب الحديث الذين يختلفون إلى مدرسة منسوبة في كورة كذا فالمتعلم للفقه إذا لم يكونوا من جملة أصحاب الحديث لا يتناول شفعوي المذهب ويتناول من يقرأ الأحاديث ويسمع ويكون في طلب ذلك، سواء كان شفعوي المذهب أو حنفي المذهب أو غير ذلك، كان شفعوي المذهب إلا أنه لا يقرأ الأحاديث ولا يسمع ولا يكون في طلب ذلك لا يتناوله اسم أصحاب الأحاديث
If he bequeaths to the children of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, the Alawiyya, Shia, Fuqaha, scholars, and hadith scholars, the bequest is valid. Faqih Abu Ja'far was asked about a man who bequeathed to the children of the Messenger of Allah, and he mentioned that Abu Nasr ibn Yahya used to say: The bequest is for the children of Hasan and Husayn, and not for others. As for the Umariyya, do they enter? He said: Look at whoever is attributed to Hasan and Husayn, not to others. As for the Umariyya, do they enter this bequest and connect to it because he (may Allah be pleased with him) married his two daughters to the children of Umar? If he bequeaths to the Alawiyya, it is reported from Faqih Abu Ja'far that it is not valid because they are not countable, and this name does not indicate poverty or need. If he bequeaths to the poor of the Alawiyya, it is valid. Similarly, a bequest to the Fuqaha is not valid, but to their poor is valid. Some of our teachers have said that an endowment for teachers of boys in mosques is valid because most of them are poor, and poverty is predominant, so the ruling of predominant poverty is like a condition. Sheikh Imam Shams al-Umma al-Halwani said: The Imam Qadi says on this analogy: If he bequeaths to the students of a certain region or to the students of a certain knowledge, it is valid. If the executor gives to one poor student or to one poor Alawi, it is permitted according to Abu Yusuf, but according to Muhammad, it is not permitted unless he gives to two of them. If he bequeaths to the Shia and their lovers, Muhammad said: Know that every Muslim is a Shia and lover of the family of the Messenger. But as for the misconception that they are known by inclination to them and have become distinguished thereby, it has been said the bequest is invalid by analogy if they are not countable. If he bequeaths to the poor of the Fuqaha, it is narrated from Faqih Abu Ja'far that he said: The Faqih in our view is one who has reached the utmost in fiqh; the mutafaqqih (student) is not a faqih. He has no share of the bequest. Faqih Abu Ja'far said: There was no one in our town called faqih except Abu Bakr al-A'mash, our teacher. Abu Bakr al-Farsi gave a lot of money to students when they called him in a gathering, 'O faqih!' If he bequeaths to the people of knowledge of a certain town, it includes the people of fiqh and hadith, and does not include those who learn philosophy (hikma). In al-Khaniyya: It does not include those who learn philosophy like philosophical discourse and other things, because these are called mutafalsifa, not students of knowledge. Are the mutakallimun (theologians) included? There is no mention of this issue in the books. From Abu al-Qasim, that books of kalam are not considered books of knowledge (in custom), and do not come to mind, so they do not fall under books of knowledge. Therefore, by analogy, the mutakallimun do not enter the bequest. If he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to the poor students of knowledge from the hadith scholars who attend a particular school in a certain region, then the one learning fiqh, if they are not among the hadith scholars, does not receive it, even if he is Shafi'i. And it reaches the one who recites hadith, listens, and seeks it, whether he is Shafi'i, Hanafi, or otherwise. If he is Shafi'i but does not recite or listen to hadith and does not seek it, the name 'hadith scholars' does not include him.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of bequests to various religious groups. The Hanafi position is that a bequest to a general group like 'Alawiyya' (descendants of the Prophet) is not valid unless they are poor and countable. Similarly, bequests to 'Fuqaha' (jurists) are not valid because the term is ambiguous and not all are poor; but to their poor it is valid. The text distinguishes between a full faqih and a student (mutafaqqih). Abu Yusuf allows the executor to give to one poor recipient, while Muhammad requires at least two unless the bequest is to a countable group. The author also excludes those who study philosophy or theology (mutakallimun) from bequests to 'people of knowledge', reserving it for hadith and fiqh scholars. The key principle is that the bequest must be to a determinate or needy group to be validly executed.

Key Terms
العلوية (al-Alawiyya): Descendants of Ali (and Fatima), i.e., the Prophet's family.
الفقهاء (al-Fuqaha): Jurists; in this context, those who have reached the highest level of fiqh, not students.
المتفقهة (al-mutafaqqiha): Students of fiqh who have not yet mastered the science.
المتكلمون (al-mutakallimun): Theologians engaged in kalam (speculative theology).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, a bequest to 'the Fuqaha' is:
A) Valid if all fuqaha are rich
B) Not valid because they are not countable and not necessarily poor
C) Valid only if they are all poor
D) Valid regardless of condition

Key Takeaway
A bequest to a general group is valid only if the group is poor and countable; the true faqih is distinguished from the student.

Bequest to an Uncountable Group: Conditions of Validity
Ruling on bequests to a group that is countable vs. not countable

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest to a group that is not countable (like a large tribe) and apply the condition of poverty to determine validity.

Core Idea
A bequest to an uncountable tribe is invalid; valid only if all are poor and the bequest is considered to Allah.

This passage from al-Muhit clarifies a key condition for bequests to specific groups like Bani Fulan. The Hanafi school requires that the group be countable (mahsur) for the bequest to be executed. If not, the bequest fails unless the group consists exclusively of the poor, in which case it is treated as a charitable bequest to the poor. This lesson walks through the reasoning and the intra-Hanafi difference on disbursement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the group and countability
Determine whether the group (e.g., Bani Fulan) is countable or not. The passage states if they are not countable, the bequest is invalid due to impossibility of execution.
2
Apply the exception for the poor
If the group is not countable but all are poor, the bequest is valid because it is considered a bequest to the poor (for Allah). The poor are recipients for Allah's sake, so execution is possible even if uncountable.
3
Contrast with bequest to a specific individual
Note the analogy: a bequest to 'one of the public' is invalid due to uncertainty. Similarly, a bequest to an uncountable group is invalid. But a bequest to a known poor person is valid.
4
Consider the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Yusuf permits giving to one poor person from the group, while Muhammad requires distribution to at least two. The text favors Abu Yusuf's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في المحيط : ولو أوصى لبني فلان فإن كانوا يحصون فالوصية باطلة لأنا عجزنا عن تنفيذ هذه الوصية لأنه لا يمكنه تنفيذها للكل لأنهم لا يحصون فبطلت الوصية كما لو أوصى لواحد من عرض الناس بخلاف ما لو أوصى للفقراء لأن الوصية للفقراء وقعت الله تعالى والفقراء مصارف ولهذا لا يرتد بردهم وجاز صرفها إلى الواحد منهم عند أبي يوسف لأنه واحد معلوم فوقعت الوصية له بخلاف الوصية لبني فلان لأنها تناولت الأغنياء كما تناولت الفقراء فيقع للغني لا لله تعالى حتى ترتد برده ولو أوصى يحصون، فإن كانوا فقراء جازت الوصية لأنها وقعت لله تعالى، وإن كانوا أغنياء لا يجوز لأنها وقعت للعباد وقد تعذر تنفيذها، ثم لا يخلو إما إن كان فلان أبا قبيلة أو فلان أب أو جد فإن كان فلان أبا قبيلة وهم ذكور وإناث فالثلث بينهم بالسوية إن كانوا يحصون لأن النساء إذا اختلطن بالرجال يدخلن في خطاب الرجال قال الله تعالى أقيموا الصلاة وآتوا الزكاة [البقرة : ٤٣] وقد تناول ذلك الرجال والنساء جميعاً وقوله تعالى فإن كان له أخوة فلامه السدس ﴾ [النساء : ١١] وقد تناول الذكور والإناث. فإن كن إناثاً خلصاً لم يذكره في
He said in al-Muhit: If he bequeaths to Bani Fulan, and they are countable, the bequest is invalid because we are unable to execute this bequest; it cannot be executed for all because they are not countable, so the bequest is invalid, just as if he bequeathed to one of the general public. Unlike if he bequeaths to the poor, because the bequest to the poor is for Allah Almighty, and the poor are recipients. Therefore, it is not voided by their refusal, and it is permitted to disburse it to one of them according to Abu Yusuf, because he is a known individual, so the bequest was made for him. This is unlike the bequest to Bani Fulan because it includes the rich as it includes the poor, so it falls to the rich, not for Allah, so it is voided by their refusal. If he bequeaths to them and they are countable, then if they are poor, the bequest is valid because it is for Allah Almighty. If they are rich, it is not valid because it is for the servants and its execution is impossible. Then it is either that Fulan is a tribal father, or a father, or a grandfather. If Fulan is a tribal father, and they are males and females, the third is among them equally if they are countable, because women when mixed with men enter the address of men. Allah said: 'Establish prayer and give zakah' (2:43), and it addressed both men and women. And His saying: 'If he has brothers, then for his mother the sixth' (4:11) includes both males and females. If they are only females, he did not mention it.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage clarifies the condition of countability (ihsa) for bequests to Bani Fulan. The key ruling: if the group is not countable (e.g., a large tribe), the bequest is invalid because execution is impossible. However, if the group is poor, it is considered a bequest to the poor (for Allah) and is valid even if not countable, as the poor are recipients for Allah. The distinction is that a bequest to a specific group like Bani Fulan includes the rich, so it cannot be executed for all. If the group is countable and poor, it's valid. Abu Yusuf allows giving to one poor person; the bequest is not void by refusal. The author also discusses when the testator is a tribal father (abu qabila), then both males and females share equally if countable, citing Qur'anic verses where women are included in general addresses. The text ends abruptly discussing a case of only females.

Key Terms
يُحصون (yuhsawn): They are countable; i.e., the group is limited and known in number.
أبا قبيلة (aba qabila): Tribal father; the testator is a tribal ancestor, so the bequest covers the entire tribe.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man bequeaths one-third to 'Bani Zaid', a tribe of 1000 members (some rich). The bequest is:
A) Valid because it is to a known group
B) Invalid because they are not countable
C) Valid only if all are poor
D) Invalid because bequest to a tribe is never allowed

Key Takeaway
The validity of a bequest to a named group depends on countability; if uncountable, it is invalid unless all are poor (then it's for Allah).

Inclusion of Women in Bequest to a Tribal Father (Abu Qabila)
Ruling on inclusion of women when testator is a tribal father

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain that when a testator is a tribal father (abu qabila), the bequest to Bani Fulan includes both males and females equally if the group is countable, citing Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
When the testator is a tribal ancestor, women are included in the bequest just like men.

The passage also addresses a specific scenario: if the testator is a tribal father (abu qabila), the bequest to 'Bani Fulan' includes both sons and daughters. This is because in Arabic, the term 'Bani' (children of) in the context of a tribal ancestor includes females when mixed with males. The author cites Quranic verses to support this inclusion. This lesson clarifies the gender inclusion rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the testator's relation
Determine whether the testator is 'abu qabila' (tribal father) or just a father/grandfather. If tribal father, the bequest covers the entire tribe including men and women.
2
Apply the rule of mixed groups
When males and females are mixed, the address to 'Bani' (sons) includes daughters. This is derived from Quranic usage where a general address to men includes women when context allows.
3
Cite the Quranic evidence
The passage quotes 2:43 (Establish prayer and give zakah) and 4:11 (inheritance verse) to show that women are included in general commands for men when mixed.
4
Consider the distribution
If countable, the third is divided equally among all males and females. The text does not mention a case of only females (it breaks off).

Bequest to Students: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad on Minimum Recipients
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bequest distribution minimum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the distribution of a bequest to students of knowledge and identify the practical difference in rulings.

Core Idea
One poor student may suffice (Abu Yusuf); Muhammad demands at least two.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a bequest to students of knowledge. While the bequest itself is valid, a dispute arises between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani about the minimum number of recipients. Understanding their reasoning illuminates how Hanafi scholars interpret the collective intent of a bequest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
The bequest to students of knowledge (talabat 'ilm) is ruled valid by the chief judge on the basis of analogy.
The bequest itself is not contested; the dispute is about distribution.
2
Recognize the dispute
The dispute is between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding whether giving the entire bequest to a single poor student is permissible.
Abu Yusuf says yes; Muhammad says no, must give to at least two.
3
Analyze each imam's reasoning
Abu Yusuf considers giving to one sufficient to fulfill the bequest to the category. Muhammad insists that 'students' implies plurality, so at least two must receive.
The difference hinges on how to interpret the collective noun.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If the executor gives to one poor student, the distribution is valid per Abu Yusuf but invalid per Muhammad; the executor must seek another recipient to comply with Muhammad's view.
The practical difference is the minimum number of recipients required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإمام القاضي يقول على هذا القياس : إذا أوصى لطلبه علم كورة كذا أو لطلبة علم كذا يجوز، ولو أعطى الوصي واحداً من فقراء الطلبة أو من فقراء العلوية جاز عند أبي يوسف، وعند محمد لا يجوز إلا إذا صرف إلى اثنين منهم
The chief judge says on this analogy: If he bequeaths to the students of knowledge of a certain district or to students of knowledge (in general), it is permissible. And if the executor gives (the bequest) to one of the poor students or to one of the poor Alawites, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, it is not permissible unless he disburses to two of them.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage addresses bequests made to students of knowledge. The chief judge (al-Qadi) affirms on the basis of analogy (qiyas) that a bequest to 'students of knowledge of a certain district' or simply 'students of knowledge' is valid. A dispute then arises between the two great Hanafi scholars, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding distribution. If the executor gives the entire bequest to just one poor student or one poor Alawite (descendant of Ali), Abu Yusuf deems this permissible, presumably because the bequest is for the category, and giving to one individual fulfills the purpose. Muhammad, however, insists that the bequest must be distributed to at least two individuals from the designated group, as giving to only one does not adequately realize the collective intent of the bequest. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but in Hanafi fiqh, the view of Abu Yusuf is often preferred in such matters of charitable bequests.

Key Terms
طلبة علم (talabat 'ilm): Students of religious knowledge, specifically those engaged in Islamic sciences.
العلوية (al-'Alawiyya): Descendants of Ali ibn Abi Talib, considered a noble lineage deserving of charity.
الوصي (al-wasi): The executor of the will, responsible for distributing the bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) All of them

Key Takeaway
In a bequest to 'students of knowledge,' Hanafi scholars disagree: Abu Yusuf permits giving to one poor student, while Muhammad requires at least two.

Bequest to an Uncountable Group – The Case of the Shia
Ruling that bequest to Shia is void if they are not countable

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest to an uncountable group and explain the qiyas (analogical reasoning) used by Imam Muhammad to declare it void.

Core Idea
A bequest to an indefinite uncountable group is void because execution is impossible.

This passage addresses a nuanced issue: a bequest to 'the Shia' and their lovers. Imam Muhammad first clarifies that all Muslims are, in a general sense, Shia (adherents) of the Prophet's family. However, the term has come to denote a specific sect. The key ruling here is that if the bequest is to that specific group and they are not countable (i.e., their number is indefinite), the bequest is void by analogy. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the Hanafi principle that bequests must be executable, and indefinite beneficiaries render execution impossible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two meanings of 'Shia'
Recognize that the passage distinguishes between the general meaning (every Muslim is a shi'a/follower of Ahl al-Bayt) and the specific sectarian meaning. The ruling concerns the latter.
Imam Muhammad's initial statement ('know that every Muslim is a shi'a') is a rebuttal to those who might assume all Shia are outside the fold of Islam.
2
Extract the ruling from the text
The phrase 'قيل الوصية باطلة' (it was said the bequest is void) indicates a transmitted opinion. Note that this is phrased as 'qīla' (it is said), suggesting it is a weak riwayah (nawadir) rather than the relied-upon position.
The authority weight is nawadir, meaning it is a minority report within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the qiyas (analogy) used
The text says 'قياساً إذا كانوا لا يحصون' – by analogy if they are not countable. The analogy is to any bequest to an indefinite group; since the beneficiaries cannot be precisely identified, the bequest fails for lack of executability.
The implicit asl (original case) is a bequest to an unspecified crowd, which is known to be invalid.
4
Determine the practical condition for validity
The underlying condition is that any bequest to a group must be to a group that can be counted or identified. If the group is too large or indefinite, the bequest is void (bāṭil).
This condition applies to bequests of property, not to charitable bequests (e.g., to the poor), which are valid even if the poor are countless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا أوصى للشيعة ومحبيه قال محمد: اعلم بأن كل مسلم شيعة ومحب لآل رسول له، وأما ما وقع عليهم الوهم من أنهم الذين يعرفون بالميل إليهم وصاروا موسومين بذلك دون غيرهم فقد قيل الوصية باطلة قياساً إذا كانوا لا يحصون
And if he bequeaths to the Shia and their lovers, Muhammad said: Know that every Muslim is a shi'a (adherent) and lover of the family of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. As for what has been misunderstood about them – that they are those known for inclining to them (the family) and have become branded with that to the exclusion of others – it has been said that the bequest is void by analogy if they are not countable.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage clarifies a ruling regarding bequests made to 'the Shia and their lovers.' Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani first establishes the principle that every Muslim is, in essence, a Shi'a (follower) and lover of the Prophet's family. However, the term 'Shia' in common usage refers to a specific sect known for their particular devotion to Ahl al-Bayt. The ruling states that a bequest to this specific group is void by analogy (qiyas) if the group cannot be counted (i.e., they are numerous and indefinite). The reasoning is that if the beneficiaries are not precisely identifiable, execution of the bequest becomes impossible, similar to a bequest to an unspecified mass of people. This ruling aligns with the general Hanafi principle that a bequest to an indefinite group is invalid unless it is for a charitable purpose like the poor.

Key Terms
الشيعة (al-Shi'a): The sect specifically known for devotion to the Prophet's family, distinguished from the general Muslim love for Ahl al-Bayt.
يحصون (yuḥṣawn): They can be counted/enumerated; a condition for validity of a bequest to a specific group.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Shia are non-Muslims
B) Because they cannot be counted (indefinite group)
C) Because Imam Muhammad said every Muslim is a Shia
D) Because the bequest was to a specific person

Key Takeaway
A bequest to a group that is not countable or indefinite is void in Hanafi law, as illustrated by the case of bequests to the Shia when their numbers are not enumerable.

Defining the Faqih for a Bequest
Definition of faqih for bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define who qualifies as a faqih for the purpose of a wasiyyah (bequest) and distinguish between a faqih and a mutafaqqih.

Core Idea
Only a fully qualified jurist (faqih) receives a bequest to fuqaha'; a student (mutafaqqih) has no share.

When someone bequeaths to 'poor jurists', the identity of the recipient matters. Not every student of fiqh counts. This lesson unpacks what it means to be a faqih according to Hanafi scholarship, drawing on a classic definition from al-Faqih Abu Ja'far.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key actors
The bequest is made to 'poor jurists' (fuqaha'). This sets the scope: the recipients must be both poor and jurists. Focus here is on the jurist qualification.
2
Parse the definition of faqih
Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far defines a faqih as 'one who has reached the utmost level (ghāya) of fiqh.' This indicates complete mastery, not mere study.
'Ghāya' implies the farthest point; a faqih has no further to go in fiqh.
3
Contrast with the mutafaqqih
The student of fiqh (mutafaqqih) is explicitly excluded. He is not a faqih and has no share in the bequest.
The term 'mutafaqqih' refers to one who is still learning, not yet an expert.
4
Apply the definition to the anecdote
Abu Ja'far notes that in his town, only his teacher Abu Bakr al-A'mash was called a faqih. When a student was addressed as 'faqih', he gave away money, indicating he did not consider himself one.
This shows the strictness of the title in practice.
5
Conclude the legal effect
Therefore, in a bequest to fuqaha', only those who have attained full mastery are eligible. A student receives nothing from the bequest.
The executor must verify the recipient's level of expertise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا أوصى لفقراء الفقهاء حكي عن الفقيه أبي جعفر أنه قال : الفقيه عندنا من بلغ من الفقه الغاية وليس المتفقة بفقيه. وليس له من الوصية بنصيب قال الفقيه أبو جعفر : إنه لم يكن في بلدنا أحد يسمى فقيهاً غير أبي بكر الأعمش شيخنا وقد أهدى أبو بكر الفارسي مالاً كثيراً لطلبة العلم حين نادوه في مجلس أيها الفقيه.
And if he bequeaths to poor jurists (fuqaha'), it is narrated from al-Faqih Abu Ja'far that he said: The faqih with us is one who has reached the utmost level of fiqh, and the student of fiqh (mutafaqqih) is not a faqih. He has no share in the bequest. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far said: There was no one in our town called a faqih other than our teacher Abu Bakr al-A'mash. And Abu Bakr al-Farisi gave much wealth to students of knowledge when they called him in a gathering, 'O faqih!'.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage provides a definition of 'faqih' (jurist) for the purpose of a bequest to poor fuqaha'. Abu Ja'far defines a faqih as one who has attained the highest level of expertise in fiqh (ghāya). A mere student of fiqh (mutafaqqih) is not considered a faqih and therefore does not qualify for the bequest. The anecdote about Abu Bakr al-A'mash illustrates that the title 'faqih' was reserved for only the most accomplished scholars. Even when people addressed Abu Bakr al-Farisi as 'faqih', he gave money to students, perhaps indicating that he did not consider himself a true faqih. This strict definition ensures that the bequest goes to those who have fully mastered fiqh, not to beginners. In Hanafi terminology, 'faqih' is used for the highest rank of scholarship.

Key Terms
الفقيه (al-faqih): One who has reached the utmost level (ghāya) in fiqh, a fully qualified jurist.
المتفقة (al-mutafaqqih): Student of fiqh who has not yet attained mastery; not eligible for a bequest to poor fuqaha'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) A poor faqih
C) A rich faqih
D) A hadith scholar

Key Takeaway
A bequest to fuqaha' requires strict identification of a faqih as one who has achieved expertise, excluding mere students.

Defining 'People of Knowledge' in a Bequest
Defining who are 'people of knowledge' for a bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify who is included and excluded in a bequest to 'people of knowledge' according to the Hanafi school, and apply the definition to analogous groups.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'people of knowledge' means fuqaha and muhaddithun, not philosophers or mutakallimun.

When a testator bequeaths to 'the people of knowledge' of a town, the exact scope matters. The Hanafi school specifies that this includes jurists and hadith scholars, but excludes those who study philosophy or scholastic theology. This lesson parses the passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq to understand the inclusion and exclusion criteria.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default inclusion
The text states that the bequest includes 'the people of fiqh' (fuqaha) and 'the people of hadith' (muhaddithun). These are the default groups that fall under 'ahl al-ilm'.
2
Identify explicit exclusion
The text explicitly excludes those who study 'al-hikma' (philosophy). It notes they are called 'mutafalsifa' (philosophers), not students of knowledge.
3
Identify analogical exclusion
The text mentions that the mutakallimun (theologians) are not explicitly mentioned, but based on Abu al-Qasim's view that books of kalam are not 'books of knowledge' in common custom, they are analogically (qiyas) excluded as well.
4
Understand the rationale
The Hanafi school prioritizes transmitted sciences (naqli) over rational sciences (aqli) in the context of 'ilm when used in a bequest. This reflects the custom and general understanding of 'knowledge' in the community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا أوصى لأهل العلم ببلدة كذا فإنه يدخل فيه أهل الفقه وأهل الحديث ولا يدخل من يتعلم الحكمة. وفي الخانية : ولا يدخل من يتعلم الحكمة مثل كلام الفلسفة وغيره لأن هؤلاء يسمون المتفلسفة لا طلبة علم وهل يدخل فيه المتكلمون؟ فلا ذكر لهذه المسألة أيضاً في الكتب وعن أبي القاسم أن كتب الكلام ليست كتب علم يعني في العرف ولا يسبق إلى الفهم فلا يدخل تحت كتب العلم، فعلى قياس هذه المسألة لا يدخل في الوصية المتكلمون.
And if he bequeaths to the people of knowledge in a certain town, then it includes the people of fiqh and the people of hadith, and it does not include those who study philosophy (al-hikma). In al-Khaniyya: And it does not include those who study philosophy such as the discourse of philosophy and other than it, because they are called 'mutafalsifa' (philosophers), not students of knowledge. And do the theologians (mutakallimun) enter? There is no mention of this issue in the books. And from Abu al-Qasim: The books of kalam (theology) are not books of knowledge, meaning in custom, and they do not come to mind, so they do not fall under 'books of knowledge'. So by analogy of this issue, the mutakallimun are not included in the bequest.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage clarifies the scope of 'people of knowledge' (ahl al-ilm) when used in a bequest to a specific town. The default inclusion comprises scholars of fiqh and hadith. Excluded are those who study 'hikma' (philosophy), who are called mutafalsifa (philosophers), not students of knowledge. As for mutakallimun (theologians), the text notes that this is not explicitly mentioned in earlier books, but based on Abu al-Qasim's view that books of kalam are not considered 'books of knowledge' in common custom, they are analogically excluded as well. This reflects the Hanafi prioritization of transmitted sciences (fiqh, hadith) over rational disciplines like philosophy and scholastic theology when it comes to charitable bequests.

Key Terms
أهل العلم (ahl al-ilm): People of religious knowledge; primarily scholars of fiqh and hadith.
الحكمة (al-hikma): Wisdom or philosophy; considered not part of religious knowledge in this context.
المتكلمون (al-mutakallimun): Scholastic theologians; analogically excluded from the bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group is explicitly excluded from a bequest to 'people of knowledge'?
A) Hadith scholars
B) Jurists (fuqaha')
C) Philosophers (mutafalsifa)
D) Reciters of Quran

Key Takeaway
In a bequest to 'people of knowledge', the Hanafi school includes only scholars of transmitted sciences (fiqh, hadith) and excludes those engaged in rational disciplines like philosophy and kalam.

Who Is a 'Student of Hadith' for a Bequest? — Inclusion Criteria
Determines who qualifies as a hadith student for a bequest based on active engagement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that active hadith study, not madhhab affiliation, determines inclusion in a bequest to 'asḥāb al-ḥadīth'.

Core Idea
A bequest to hadith scholars includes only those who actively read, listen, and seek hadith — regardless of their madhhab.

When someone bequeaths to 'the poor students of knowledge among the hadith scholars,' who qualifies? Hanafi jurists parse the testator's intent carefully. The key is not which madhhab one follows, but whether one actively engages in hadith study. This lesson unpacks the definition of 'asḥāb al-ḥadīth' in the context of a bequest, clarifying that a Shafi'i who only studies fiqh is excluded, while a Hanafi who studies hadith is included.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase and its legal context
Recognize that the testator specifies 'poor students of knowledge among the hadith scholars (asḥāb al-ḥadīth)' attending a particular school. The ruling interprets this phrase to determine who receives the bequest.
2
Extract the inclusion criterion
The passage states that those who 'read the hadith, listen, and are in pursuit of that' are included. This is the operative definition of asḥāb al-ḥadīth.
Key verbs: يقرأ (reads), يسمع (listens), في طلب ذلك (in pursuit of that).
3
Apply the exclusion rule
A student of fiqh (mutafaqqih) who is not part of hadith scholars is excluded, even if he is Shafi'i. Madhhab alone does not confer the title.
The text explicitly mentions the Shafi'i school as an example, but the principle applies to any madhhab.
4
Generalize the principle
The determining factor is the activity of hadith study, not the school of thought. A Shafi'i who does not study hadith is excluded; a Hanafi who does study hadith is included.
This emphasizes the Hanafi focus on actual practice rather than labels.
5
Note the practical implication
When interpreting a bequest, the mufti must investigate the actual practice of potential recipients, not assume based on madhhab.
This protects the testator's intent and ensures the bequest is validly distributed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا أوصى بثلث ماله على فقراء طلبة العلم من أصحاب الحديث الذين يختلفون إلى مدرسة منسوبة في كورة كذا فالمتعلم للفقه إذا لم يكونوا من جملة أصحاب الحديث لا يتناول شفعوي المذهب ويتناول من يقرأ الأحاديث ويسمع ويكون في طلب ذلك، سواء كان شفعوي المذهب أو حنفي المذهب أو غير ذلك، كان شفعوي المذهب إلا أنه لا يقرأ الأحاديث ولا يسمع ولا يكون في طلب ذلك لا يتناوله اسم أصحاب الأحاديث
And if he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to the poor students of knowledge among the hadith scholars (asḥāb al-ḥadīth) who attend a school affiliated with a certain district, then a student of fiqh, if they are not part of the hadith scholars, is not included – even if he is of the Shafi'i school. And it includes those who read the hadith, listen, and are in pursuit of that, whether he is of the Shafi'i school or the Hanafi school or other than that. If he is of the Shafi'i school but he does not read hadith, nor listen, nor is he in pursuit of that, the name 'asḥāb al-ḥadīth' does not include him.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage specifies the criteria for inclusion in a bequest to 'poor students of knowledge among the hadith scholars' who attend a particular school in a district. The key factor is active engagement with hadith: reading, listening, and seeking it. A student of fiqh (mutafaqqih) who does not involve himself with hadith is not included, even if he belongs to the Shafi'i school (which traditionally emphasizes hadith). Conversely, a Hanafi student who actively studies hadith is included. The determining factor is the activity, not the madhhab. This emphasizes the pragmatic approach of Hanafi scholars in interpreting the testator's intent: the phrase 'asḥāb al-ḥadīth' refers to those who practice hadith study, not merely those who follow a school that relies on hadith.

Key Terms
أصحاب الحديث (asḥāb al-ḥadīth): Hadith scholars or students who actively read, listen to, and seek hadith.
شفعوي المذهب (shaf'awī al-madhhab): A follower of the Shafi'i school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A Shafi'i who reads and seeks hadith
C) A Shafi'i who only studies fiqh and does not engage with hadith
D) A Maliki who reads hadith

Key Takeaway
Eligibility for a bequest to 'asḥāb al-ḥadīth' depends on active hadith study, not madhhab affiliation.

Bequest to a Named Group: Countability and Poverty Conditions
General ruling on a bequest to 'sons of so-and-so' when countable and financial status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest to 'Bani Fulan' based on countability and financial status, and identify when the bequest is valid or void.

Core Idea
A bequest to an uncountable or wealthy group is void; only when the group is both countable and poor does it become valid.

In this passage from al-Muhit, the author presents the Hanafi ruling on a bequest made to a specific tribe or clan, 'Bani Fulan'. The validity of such a bequest depends critically on two factors: whether the group can be counted (limited in number) and whether all its members are poor. This lesson unpacks these conditions and contrasts them with a bequest to the general poor, which is always valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the bequest
Recognize that 'Bani Fulan' refers to a specific group (e.g., a tribe or clan). This is not a general charity but a designated class.
The group may include both rich and poor individuals.
2
Determine countability
Is the group limited in number (countable) or not? If the group is large and uncountable (e.g., a large tribe), execution is impossible.
The corrupted text likely reads 'if they are not countable' to indicate the void case.
3
Assess financial status
If countable, check the financial status of the entire group. Are all members poor, or does it include rich individuals?
The bequest to a rich person is not an act of charity to Allah; it goes to the servant.
4
Apply the ruling
If the group is uncountable → void. If countable and all poor → valid. If countable and any rich → void.
The bequest to a mixed group (rich and poor) is void because it includes the rich, making it a gift to servants, not Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في المحيط : ولو أوصى لبني فلان فإن كانوا يحصون فالوصية باطلة لأنا عجزنا عن تنفيذ هذه الوصية لأنه لا يمكنه تنفيذها للكل لأنهم لا يحصون فبطلت الوصية كما لو أوصى لواحد من عرض الناس بخلاف ما لو أوصى للفقراء لأن الوصية للفقراء وقعت الله تعالى والفقراء مصارف ولهذا لا ترتد بردهم وجاز صرفها إلى الواحد منهم عند أبي يوسف لأنه واحد معلوم فوقعت الوصية له بخلاف الوصية لبني فلان لأنها تناولت الأغنياء كما تناولت الفقراء فيقع للغني لا لله تعالى حتى ترتد برده ولو أوصى يحصون، فإن كانوا فقراء جازت الوصية لأنها وقعت لله تعالى، وإن كانوا أغنياء لا يجوز لأنها وقعت للعباد وقد تعذر تنفيذها.
He said in al-Muhit: If he bequeaths to the sons of so-and-so, then if they can be counted, the bequest is void because we are unable to execute this bequest, as he cannot execute it for all because they cannot be counted, so the bequest is void – just as if he bequeathed to one of the common people. Unlike if he bequeathed to the poor, because the bequest to the poor is for Allah, and the poor are channels, and for this reason it is not rejected by their refusal, and it is permissible to disburse it to one of them according to Abu Yusuf, because that one is a known individual, so the bequest falls to him. Contrary to the bequest to the sons of so-and-so, because it includes the rich as it includes the poor, so it falls to the rich, not for Allah, so it is rejected by his refusal. And if he bequeaths while they can be counted, then if they are poor, the bequest is valid because it is for Allah, and if they are rich, it is not valid because it is for the servants and its execution is impossible.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit presents the general ruling on a bequest made to 'Bani Fulan' (the sons of a specific person, often a tribe or clan). The ruling hinges on whether the group can be enumerated (countable) and their financial status. The text appears corrupt but the key principle is: if the group is uncountable (numerous), the bequest is void because execution is impossible. If the group is countable, then the bequest's validity depends on whether they are all poor or all rich. If they are all poor, the bequest is valid because it effectively goes to the poor (for Allah). If they are all rich, it is invalid because it goes to the rich (for themselves) and cannot be executed properly. The contrast is made with a bequest to 'the poor', which is always valid because it is for Allah and can be given to any poor person. The difference is that a bequest to 'Bani Fulan' includes both rich and poor, so if the group is mixed, the bequest is problematic because it cannot be confined to the poor.

Key Terms
بني فلان (banī fulān): The sons/descendants of a specific person; refers to a tribe or clan.
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest or will for the transfer of wealth after death.
يحصون (yuhsawun): They can be counted/enumerated. The opposite is uncountable (لا يحصون).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a bequest to 'Bani Fulan' considered valid?
A) When the group is uncountable and rich
B) When the group is countable and poor
C) When the group is uncountable and poor
D) Always valid regardless

Key Takeaway
A bequest to a specific tribe or clan is valid only if the group is both countable and entirely poor; otherwise, it is void.

Bequest to 'Bani Fulan': Are Females Included?
Intra-Hanafi dispute whether females are included in bequest to 'Bani Fulan'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether females are included in a bequest to 'Bani Fulan' and state the relied-upon position along with its linguistic basis.

Core Idea
In bequests, 'Bani Fulan' defaults to males only; metaphorical inclusion of females is subject to doubt.

The language of bequests often hinges on precise interpretation. When someone bequeaths to 'Bani Fulan', does it include daughters? The Hanafi school split on this question, with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf arguing for a strict literal reading, while Muhammad al-Shaybani favored a broader usage. This lesson unpacks their arguments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the two views: Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf (females not included) and Muhammad (females included when mixed with males).
The relied-upon position is the former, marked as 'asahh'.
2
Analyze Muhammad's argument
Muhammad uses the widespread usage of 'Bani' to include both genders, citing examples like 'Bani Adam' and the Quranic mention of 'brothers' including sisters.
3
Analyze the majority's counter-argument
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue that 'Bani' literally means males; including females is metaphorical, and literal meaning takes precedence. Doubt about inclusion should be resolved against inclusion.
They also note that 'Bani' can be used for males alone, but never for females alone.
4
Understand the linguistic principle
The majority applies the rule: al-haqiqah tuqaddam 'ala al-majaz (literal meaning is prioritized over metaphorical). Since the metaphor involves doubt, the default (males only) remains.
Muhammad's view treats the mixed usage as an extended reality, not metaphor.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states 'wa huwa al-asahh' (it is the most correct), favoring Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Thus, in practice, females are not included unless explicitly stated.
This is the operative position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it is mentioned in some copies that the statement of Abu Yusuf is with Abu Hanifa, and that is the most correct. And according to Muhammad, females enter. For Muhammad: Females, when they mix with males, follow the males, and males dominate over females, for it is said 'Bani Adam', 'Bani Hashim', 'Bani Tamim', and it includes males and females. Hence, if he bequeathed to the brothers of so-and-so, the brothers and sisters would be included under the bequest due to the verse we mentioned. For them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): The reality of this expression is applied specifically to males; it is applied to males and females in the case of mixing metaphorically, and acting upon the reality is obligatory as much as possible. Moreover, in using this metaphor there is ambiguity, because if so-and-so is a father or grandfather, just as the name 'father' is mentioned and intended by it males and females, it is also mentioned and intended by it specifically males without females, because his children may be devoid of females. And the application of this name to specifically males is a used reality, and to specifically females is a non-used metaphor. So in the case of mixing, doubt arises about the inclusion of females under the bequest, so they do not enter due to doubt. Unlike if he bequeathed to Bani Tamim, because the objective is not the individuals and persons, but rather the objective is merely the lineages.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether females are included in a bequest to 'Bani Fulan' (sons of so-and-so). According to some copies, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf agree that females are not included, and this is considered the most correct (asahh). Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that females are included when they are mixed with males, based on common usage (e.g., Bani Adam includes both). Both sides present arguments. Muhammad points to the widespread usage of 'Bani' to include both genders, as in the Quranic usage of 'ikhwa' (brothers) to include sisters in some contexts. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that the literal meaning of 'Bani' is specifically males, and the inclusion of females is metaphorical. Since literal meaning takes precedence, females are not included unless there is explicit evidence. Furthermore, doubt about inclusion should be resolved against inclusion. The practical outcome (thamar al-khilaf) is that a bequest to 'Bani Fulan' is distributed only to males according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but according to Muhammad, both males and females share if they are present.

Key Terms
بني فلان (banī fulān): The sons/descendants; the dispute is about whether the term linguistically includes females.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, always
B) Yes, if they are poor
C) No, because the literal meaning is males
D) No, only if explicitly mentioned

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a bequest to 'Bani Fulan' includes only males, based on the literal meaning of 'Bani' and the principle that doubt does not override the default.
