Bequest to 'Bani Fulan': Inclusion of Grandchildren and After-Born Children
Rules on inclusion of grandchildren and children born after the will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules on inclusion of grandchildren and after-born children in a bequest to 'Bani Fulan' and apply them to scenarios.

Core Idea
Bequest to 'Bani Fulan' includes only direct sons unless none exist; then son's son enters; after-born children are included if born before death.

The term 'Bani Fulan' (sons of so-and-so) in a bequest raises questions: do grandchildren count? What about children born after the will was made? This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq provides the Hanafi answers, drawing a parallel to inheritance law and clarifying that the time of death determines the beneficiaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers two distinct questions: (1) whether grandchildren are included under 'Bani Fulan', and (2) whether children born after the will are included. Distinguish these.
2
Apply the rule on grandchildren
If the testator specified 'men and women', then females enter; otherwise, only males. For 'Bani Fulan', default is direct sons (ولد الصلب). If no direct son exists, the grandson (son's son) stands in his place; granddaughters (son's daughters) are never included.
The grandson is called a 'son' but deficient; deficiency is ignored when no direct son, based on inheritance analogy.
3
Apply the rule on after-born children
The bequest is a transfer of ownership after death. Therefore, beneficiaries are those who exist at the testator's death, not at the time of the will. Children born after the will but before death are included equally.
Example: Four sons at will, one more born before death; all five share equally.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The basis is that 'bequest is the sister of inheritance' (الوصية أخت الميراث). Just as a grandson inherits in the absence of a direct son, he is included in the bequest. Similarly, existence at death matters for both.
This principle is used for qiyas (analogy).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو وجد في الوصية مثل هذا التفسير بأن قال بإخوة فلان رجالاً ونساء دخلت الأخوات فيها وليس لولد الولد شيء. وإن كانوا مع ولد الصلب وإن لم يكن لفلان ولد صلب فالوصية لابن ابنه دون بنات ابنه لأن ولد الابن بيسمى ولداً إلا أنه ناقص في الإضافة والانتساب إليه لأنه يضاف إليه بواسطة والناقص لا يدخل تحت مطلق اسم المضاف كأولاد البنات فعند الإطلاق يحمل على ولد الصلب لأنه أحق بهذا الاسم فإن تعذر حمله على الحقيقة حمل على المجاز تحرياً للجواز ولأن ابن الابن قائم مقام ابن الصلب حال عدم الصلب في الميراث حجباً واستحقاقاً، وسقط اعتبار نقصان الإضافة إليه شرعاً فكذلك الوصية لأنها أخت الميراث. ولو أوصى لبني فلان بالثلث ولم يكن لفلان بنون يوم الوصية فهو لبنيه الذين حدثوا قبل موت الموصي لأن الوصية تمليك من الموصى للموصى له بعد الموت فيعتبر وجود الموصى له وقت موت الموصي ولهذا صحت الوصية بثلث ماله وإن لم يكن له مال عند الوصية وإن كان لفلان بنون أربعة وولد له أخر إن ثم مات الموصي فالثلث للباقين وللمولودين سواء لأنه متى أضاف الوصية إلى بني فلان مطلقاً ولم يسهم تقع الوصية لبنيه الموجودين وقت الموت لا لبنيه الموجودين وقت الوصية لأن الوصية تمليك مضاف على ما بعد الموت فيعتبر الملك وقت الموت حتى لو قال
And if a such interpretation is found in the will, such that he said 'to the brothers of so-and-so, men and women', then the sisters enter it, and there is nothing for the children of sons. And if they are with a direct son, and if so-and-so has no direct son, then the bequest is for his son's son, not his son's daughters, because the son's son is called a son, except that he is deficient in attribution and lineage to him because he is attributed through an intermediary, and the deficient does not enter under the absolute name of the attributed, like the children of daughters. So upon absolute usage, it is carried upon the direct son because he is more entitled to this name. If carrying it upon the reality is prevented, it is carried upon the metaphor for the sake of validity. And because the son's son stands in the place of the direct son in the case of absence of a direct son in inheritance, in blocking and entitlement, and the consideration of deficiency in attribution to him is dropped legally, so likewise the bequest because it is the sister of inheritance. And if he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to the sons of so-and-so and so-and-so had no sons at the time of the will, then it is for his sons who are born before the death of the testator, because the bequest is the transfer of ownership from the testator to the beneficiary after death, so the existence of the beneficiary is considered at the time of death of the testator. And for this reason, the bequest of one-third of his wealth is valid even if he had no wealth at the time of the will. And if so-and-so had four sons and another son was born while he was in a state, then the testator died, the one-third is for those who remain and for the newborns equally, because when he adds the bequest to the sons of so-and-so absolutely and does not specify, the bequest falls to his sons existing at the time of death, not to his sons existing at the time of the will, because the bequest is an added transfer after death, so ownership is considered at the time of death, even if he said
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage contains two related rulings for bequests to 'Bani Fulan'. First, it discusses the inclusion of grandchildren. If the testator explicitly says 'to the brothers of so-and-so, men and women', then sisters are included but not children of sons. In the default case without such specification, if there is a direct son, the bequest goes to him; if there is no direct son, the bequest goes to the son's son but not the son's daughter. The reasoning is that the term 'ibn' (son) includes the grandson by extension, but this inclusion is deficient due to the intermediary. However, since in inheritance law, a son's son stands in place of a son when there is no son, the same applies to bequests because 'bequest is the sister of inheritance'. The second ruling concerns children born after the will. The bequest to 'Bani Fulan' is considered at the time of death: whoever is a son at death, including those born after the will, enters the bequest. This is because a bequest is a transfer of ownership after death, so the identity of beneficiaries is determined at death. An example: if so-and-so had four sons at the time of the will but another son is born before the testator dies, all five sons share the bequest equally. The text cuts off mid-sentence when giving an example of an exception.

Key Terms
ولد الابن (walad al-ibn): Son's son (grandson); considered a son but deficient in lineage.
ولد الصلب (walad al-sulb): Direct son (from the loins); the primary referent of 'ibn'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a testator bequeaths to 'Bani Fulan' and Fulan has no direct son, who among the following receives the bequest?
A) Son's son only
B) Son's daughter only
C) Both son's son and daughter
D) The bequest is void

Key Takeaway
A bequest to 'Bani Fulan' defaults to direct sons; only in their absence does a son's son enter, and after-born sons are included if born before death.

Dispute on Bequest to 'Sons of So-and-So' Involving Females
Intra-Hanafi dispute on interpretation of 'بنو فلان' in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on whether the term 'بنو فلان' in a bequest includes females and evaluate the opposing view of Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
In bequests, 'بنو فلان' literally means sons only; inclusion of daughters requires explicit language.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the interpretation of 'بنو فلان' (sons of so-and-so) when used in a bequest. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the literal meaning of the term excludes females, while Imam Muhammad argues that when females are mixed with males, they are included by common usage. The dispute illustrates key principles of Hanafi usul, particularly the preference for literal meaning (haqiqah) over metaphorical usage (majaz) in legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed phrase and context
The bequest is to 'بنو فلان' where 'فلان' is a father or grandfather. Determine when the dispute arises: when the deceased has both sons and daughters.
The same dispute applies to 'إخوة فلان' (brothers of so-and-so).
2
State the Hanafi majority position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (in the more authentic narration) rule that only male descendants take the bequest. The term 'بنو فلان' is a haqiqah (literal) for males only.
Acting upon the literal meaning is obligatory when possible.
3
Analyze the opposing view of Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad includes females when mixed with males, based on common usage (e.g., 'بنو آدم' includes both genders). He also cites Quran 4:176 for 'إخوة'.
His reasoning: females follow males when mixed.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The majority argue that common usage is metaphorical (majaz). Since literal meaning is possible and doubt (shakk) exists about inclusion, the literal meaning prevails. The Quranic verse specifies inheritance shares, not the linguistic meaning of 'إخوة'.
If the testator explicitly says 'رجالاً ونساء', females are included.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the mufta bihi position (Abu Hanifa), a bequest to 'بني فلان' goes only to sons. Under Muhammad, if there are sons, daughters also share proportionally.
The same applies to 'إخوة فلان': only brothers take, unless explicitly stated otherwise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا باب الوصية للأقارب وغيرهم
وقالوا : على قياس تعليل محمد لهذه المسألة يكون الثلث لهن لأنه ذكر وقال : يحسن أن يقال هذه المرأة من بني فلان إذا كان فلان أباً وجداً وله أولاد بنات فلا شيء لهن، وإن كانوا ذكوراً وبنات فالثلث للذكور خاصة عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما للذكور والإناث.
وذكر في بعض النسخ قول أبي يوسف مع أبي حنيفة وهو الأصح، وعند محمد يدخل الإناث. لمحمد أن الإناث متى اختلطت بالذكور يتبعن الذكور ويغلب الذكور على الإناث فإنه يقال بنو آدم وبنو هاشم وبنو تميم فإنه يتناول الذكور والإناث ولهذا لو أوصى لإخوة فلان دخل الإخوة والأخوات تحت الوصية لما ذكرناه من الآية لهما أن حقيقة هذا اللفظ يطلق على الذكور خاصة وإنما يطلق على الذكور والإناث حالة الاختلاط مجازاً والعمل بالحقيقة واجب ما أمكن مع أن في استعمال هذا المجاز اشتراكاً لأن فلاناً إذا كان أباً أو جداً فكما يذكر اسم الأب ويراد به الذكور والإناث يذكر ويراد به الذكور خاصة دون الإناث لأنه قد تخلو أولاده عن الإناث، وإطلاق هذا الاسم على الذكور خاصة حقيقة مستعملة وعلى الإناث خاصة مجاز غير مستعمل فحالة الاختلاط وقع الشك في دخول الإناث تحت الوصية فلا يدخل بالشك بخلاف ما لو أوصى لبني تميم لأن المقصود ليس هو الأعيان والأشخاص وإنما المقصود مجرد الأسباب والوصية للإخوة على هذا الخلاف تكون وصية للأخوة دون الأخوات عندهما لأن اسم الإخوة لا يتناول الأخوات بحقيقته بل بمجازه ولهذا قال الله تعالى وإن كانوا إخوة رجالاً ونساء فللذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين ﴾ [النساء : ١٧٦] فقد فسر الإخوة بالرجال والنساء، ولو تناول اسم الإخوة الأخوات لم يحتج إلى هذا التفصيل. ولو وجد في الوصية مثل هذا التفسير بأن قال بإخوة فلان رجالاً ونساء دخلت الأخوات فيها وليس لولد الولد شيء.
Chapter of Bequests: Section on Bequest to Relatives and Others. And they said: on the analogy of Muhammad's reasoning for this issue, the third is for them because he mentioned and said: it is good to say: this woman is from the sons of so-and-so. If so-and-so is a father or grandfather and he has children daughters, then nothing for them. And if they are males and daughters, then the third is for the males specifically according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two, for males and females. And it is mentioned in some copies the opinion of Abu Yusuf with Abu Hanifa and it is the more correct, and according to Muhammad, females are included. For Muhammad, when females are mixed with males, they follow the males, and males dominate over females. For it is said: the sons of Adam, the sons of Hashim, and the sons of Tamim, and it includes males and females. Hence, if one bequeaths to the brothers of so-and-so, brothers and sisters enter under the bequest due to what we mentioned of the verse. For the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) that the reality of this expression is applied to males specifically, and it is applied to males and females in the case of mixing only metaphorically, and acting upon the reality is obligatory as much as possible. And moreover, in using this metaphor there is ambiguity. Because if so-and-so is a father or grandfather, just as the name 'father' is mentioned and meant for males and females, it is mentioned and meant for males specifically without females because his children may be devoid of females. And the application of this name to males specifically is a used reality, and to females specifically is an unused metaphor. So in the case of mixing, doubt arises regarding the entrance of females under the bequest, so they do not enter due to doubt, unlike if one bequeaths to the sons of Tamim because the intention is not the individuals and persons but rather merely the causes. And the bequest to brothers upon this disagreement is a bequest to brothers and not sisters according to the two because the name 'brothers' does not include sisters by its reality but by its metaphor. For this, Allah Almighty said: "And if they are brothers, men and women, then for the male is the share of two females" (4:176), so He interpreted 'brothers' as men and women. And if the name 'brothers' included sisters, this detail would not be needed. And if such an interpretation is found in the bequest, such as saying: to the brothers of so-and-so, men and women, then sisters enter therein. And there is nothing for the child's child.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of the term 'بنو فلان' (sons of so-and-so) in bequests. The context is a bequest made to the children of a person who is a father or grandfather. If he has only daughters, Abu Hanifa rules they take nothing because the term 'بنو فلان' literally refers to males. If he has both sons and daughters, Abu Hanifa gives the bequest to the sons exclusively. Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifa in the more authentic narration, while Muhammad al-Shaybani includes daughters when they are mixed with sons, arguing that the term 'بنو فلان' in common usage includes both genders, as in 'بنو آدم' and 'بنو هاشم'. The passage then discusses the parallel issue for bequest to 'إخوة فلان' (brothers of so-and-so). The same two positions apply: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf restrict it to brothers, Muhammad includes sisters when mixed. The proof for Muhammad includes the Quranic verse (4:176) which interprets 'إخوة' as including both when it says 'رجالاً ونساء'. However, the Hanafi majority respond that the verse explains the ruling for inheritance, not the linguistic meaning; the word 'إخوة' is literal for males only, and the specification in the verse shows that without specification, females are not included. The passage concludes that if the testator explicitly says 'إخوة فلان رجالاً ونساء', then sisters are included. Also, it mentions that children of children (ولد الولد) are not included in the term 'ولد' without specification.

Key Terms
بني فلان (banī fulān): A phrase referring to the offspring of a specific person; in legal context of bequests, a subject of dispute whether it includes females.
حقيقة (ḥaqīqah): Literal or real meaning of a word, as opposed to metaphorical.
مجاز (majāz): Metaphorical or figurative usage of a word.
إخوة (ikhwah): Brothers; in bequest context, dispute whether it includes sisters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) Hanafi position, if someone bequeaths to 'بني فلان' and the person referred to has both sons and daughters, who takes the bequest?
A) Only the sons
B) Only the daughters
C) Both sons and daughters equally
D) The bequest becomes void

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the term 'بنو فلان' in a bequest is interpreted literally to include only males, and females are not included unless explicitly mentioned.

Interpreting 'Walad' in Bequests: Literal Meaning and Hierarchical Inclusion
Rulings on interpreting 'ولد' in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for interpreting 'walad' in bequests and apply the hierarchy of literal vs. metaphorical inclusion.

Core Idea
'Walad' in bequests means direct children literally; grandchildren take only metaphorically when no direct children exist.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains how a bequest to 'so-and-so's child' is distributed. The key is whether the testator has direct children (ولدا الصلب). If yes, they take; if not, the bequest goes to grandchildren via sons, but not via daughters. This hierarchy is based on linguistic principles and analogy with inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the testator's surviving relatives
List all living descendants: direct children, grandchildren by sons, and grandchildren by daughters. Note their genders.
Only living relatives at the time of the testator's death matter, except for fetuses born alive.
2
Apply the literal meaning rule
If direct children exist, the term 'walad' is taken literally, so the bequest goes to them. Direct daughters are included because 'walad' covers both genders literally.
Literal meaning takes precedence over metaphorical.
3
If no direct children, apply metaphorical extension
Check for grandchildren by sons (not daughters). If they exist, they take the bequest. Both male and female grandchildren by sons are included. Grandchildren by daughters are excluded because they are not affiliated to the testator through the male line.
The analogy with inheritance (الوصية أخت الميراث) supports this substitution.
4
Understand the basis: linguistic and inheritance analogy
The passage explains that while the term 'walad' for a grandson is deficient in affiliation (ناقص في الإضافة), in the absence of a direct child, the deficiency is overlooked, similar to inheritance rules.
The principle 'الوصية أخت الميراث' is key.
5
Test with a scenario
Consider a testator with a daughter and a son's son. The daughter takes the bequest because she is a direct child. The grandson is excluded because the literal meaning includes the daughter.
If the testator had no children, the grandson would take.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كانوا مع ولد الصلب وإن لم يكن لفلان ولد صلب فالوصية لابن ابنه دون بنات ابنه لأن ولد الابن بيسمى ولداً إلا أنه ناقص في الإضافة والانتساب إليه لأنه يضاف إليه بواسطة والناقص لا يدخل تحت مطلق اسم المضاف كأولاد البنات فعند الإطلاق يحمل على ولد الصلب لأنه أحق بهذا الاسم فإن تعذر حمله على الحقيقة حمل على المجاز تحرياً للجواز ولأن ابن الابن قائم مقام ابن الصلب حال عدم الصلب في الميراث حجباً واستحقاقاً، وسقط اعتبار نقصان الإضافة إليه شرعاً فكذلك الوصية لأنها أخت الميراث. ولو أوصى لبني فلان بالثلث ولم يكن لفلان بنون يوم الوصية فهو لبنيه الذين حدثوا قبل موت الموصي لأن الوصية تمليك من الموصى للموصى له بعد الموت فيعتبر وجود الموصى له وقت موت الموصي ولهذا صحت الوصية بثلث ماله وإن لم يكن له مال عند الوصية وإن كان لفلان بنون أربعة وولد له أخر ثم مات الموصي فالثلث للباقين وللمولودين سواء لأنه متى أضاف الوصية إلى بني فلان مطلقاً ولم يسهم تقع الوصية لبنيه الموجودين وقت الموت لا لبنيه الموجودين وقت الوصية لأن الوصية تمليك مضاف على ما بعد الموت فيعتبر الملك وقت الموت حتى لو قال أوصيت بالثلث لبني فلان هؤلاء وسماهم تقع لبنيه الموجودين وقت الوصية حتى تبطل بموتهم ولا يكون لبنيه الموجودين عند الموت ولو قال لولد فلان دخل الذكور والإناث لأن الولد يتناول الكل حقيقة وكذلك الجنين لأنه ولده وإنما تصح الوصية للجنين بشرط أن ينفصل حياً. وتعليق الوصية بالشرط والإحصار جائزة فإن الوصية بالمعدوم للمعدوم جائز وإن كان له بنات وبنو ابن فالوصية للبنات لأن اسم الولد يتناوله البنات الصلبية حقيقة وولد الابن مجازاً لأن الاسم مشتق من التوليد والتفرع والبنت الصلبية متولدة عنه حقيقة وولد الابن متولد بواسطة، فإن لم يكن له ولد صلب فالوصية لولد الابن الذكور والإناث سواء كان ولد الابن مضافاً أو منسوباً إليه بواسطة الأب، وفي الأضافة إليه نوع قصور فعند الإطلاق ينصرف الاسم إلى الولد الصلبي لأنه أحق وعند عدمه يحمل على ولد الابن مجازاً، ولا شيء لولد البنت لأن ولد البنت غير منسوب إليه ومضاف إليه لأنه من جهة الأباء دون الأمهات على ما مر بشرحه في كتاب الوقف، ولو لم يكن له إلا ولد واحد فكل الثلث له لأن اسم الولد يتناول الواحد فصاعداً
And if they are with the direct child, and if so-and-so has no direct child, then the bequest is to his son's son, not to his son's daughters, because the son's child is called a child, except that it is deficient in affiliation and relation because it is attached to him through an intermediary, and the deficient does not enter under the absolute name of the attached, like the children of daughters. So upon absolute usage, it is taken to mean the direct child because it is more entitled to this name. If it is not possible to take it literally, it is taken metaphorically in seeking validity. And because the son's son stands in the place of the direct son in the case of absence of direct son in inheritance, by exclusion and entitlement, and the consideration of deficiency of affiliation to him is dropped legally, so likewise in bequest because it is the sibling of inheritance. And if he bequeaths the third to the sons of so-and-so, and so-and-so had no sons on the day of the bequest, then it is for his sons who come into existence before the death of the testator, because the bequest is a transfer of ownership from the testator to the legatee after death, so the existence of the legatee is considered at the time of the testator's death. Hence, a bequest of a third of his wealth is valid even if he had no wealth at the time of the bequest. And if so-and-so had four sons and another son was born to him, then the testator died, then the third is for the remaining and the newborns equally, because when he attached the bequest to the sons of so-and-so absolutely and did not specify, the bequest falls to his sons existing at the time of death, not to his sons existing at the time of the bequest, because the bequest is a transfer attached to after death, so ownership is considered at the time of death. So much so that if he said: I bequeath the third to these sons of so-and-so and named them, it falls to his sons existing at the time of the bequest, so that it is nullified by their death and does not go to his sons existing at death. And if he said: to the child of so-and-so, then males and females enter because 'child' includes all literally, and likewise the fetus because it is his child, but the bequest to a fetus is valid only on condition that it is born alive. And attaching the bequest to a condition and restriction is permissible, for the bequest to a non-existent for a non-existent is permissible. And if he has daughters and sons of sons, then the bequest is for the daughters because the name 'child' includes the direct daughters literally and the son's child metaphorically, because the name is derived from generation and branching, and the direct daughter is generated from him literally while the son's child is generated through an intermediary. So if he has no direct child, then the bequest is for the son's child, males and females, whether the son's child is attached or attributed to him through the father. And in the attachment to him there is a type of deficiency, so upon absolute usage the name turns to the direct child because it is more entitled, and in its absence it is taken metaphorically for the son's child. And there is nothing for the daughter's child because the daughter's child is not attributed to him and attached to him because it is from the father's side, not the mother's side, as has been explained in the book of Waqf. And if he has only one child, then the whole third is for him because the name 'child' includes one and more.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage covers several rules about bequests using terms like 'ولد' (child) and 'بني' (sons). It first discusses that when there are direct children (ولدا الصلب), bequest to 'ولد' goes to them, not to grandchildren. But if no direct children, grandchildren take, but only grandsons (sons of sons), not granddaughters, because the term 'ولد' for grandchildren is metaphorical and deficient in affiliation. This is based on analogy with inheritance where grandchildren substitute for children when direct children are absent. The principle 'الوصية أخت الميراث' (bequest is the sibling of inheritance) is invoked. Then it discusses bequest to 'بني فلان' with timing: if at the time of the will the person had no sons, but later had sons before the testator's death, those sons take the bequest because bequest is a transfer after death, so the existence of the legatee is considered at death. If the testator specifies 'هؤلاء' and names them, then only those named take, and if they die before the testator, the bequest is void for them. Then it covers that 'ولد' includes both genders, and even a fetus if born alive. A bequest to a non-existent person is valid if the condition is attached. Then it discusses the hierarchy: direct daughters take over grandsons when both exist, because 'ولد' for direct daughters is literal, while for grandsons it is metaphorical. If no direct children, the grandsons (both male and female) take. Finally, if only one child exists, the whole third goes to that child because 'ولد' includes singular.

Key Terms
ولد (walad): Child; in bequest context, includes both genders literally, and can extend to grandchildren metaphorically when no direct children exist.
ولدا الصلب (waldā al-sulb): Direct children (offspring of the testator himself, not grandchildren).
الوصية أخت الميراث (al-wasiyyah ukht al-mirath): Bequest is the sibling of inheritance; the rules of inheritance inform the rules of bequest in similar situations, such as substitution of grandchildren.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a testator bequeaths 'to the child of so-and-so' and so-and-so has no direct child but has a son's daughter and a daughter's son, who receives the bequest?
A) The son's daughter only
B) The daughter's son only
C) Both the son's daughter and daughter's son
D) The bequest is void

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi bequest law, 'walad' defaults to direct children; grandchildren via sons are included only when no direct children exist, and grandchildren via daughters are never included.

Bequest to 'Bani' (Sons): Timing, Specification, and Gender
Rulings on interpreting 'بني' in bequests with timing and specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for bequests to 'bani' (sons), including the relevant time for existence of legatees and the effect of specification.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'bani' goes to sons existing at death, not at the time of the will, unless the testator specifies named individuals.

This passage also covers the interpretation of 'بني فلان' (sons of so-and-so) in bequests. Unlike 'ولد', which includes both genders, 'بني' is restricted to males. The critical point is that the legatees are those sons who are alive at the testator's death, not at the time of making the will. If the testator names specific sons, only those take, and the bequest becomes void if they predecease him.

Guided Path
1
Determine if the bequest is to 'بني فلان' or 'ولد فلان'
The term 'بني فلان' refers only to male offspring (sons). If the testator uses 'ولد', both males and females are included.
This is a key difference in gender scope.
2
Establish the relevant time for legatee existence
For an absolute bequest to 'بني فلان' (without specification), the legatees are the sons existing at the testator's death. Sons born after the will but before death are included; sons who died before death are excluded.
This is because bequest is a transfer of ownership after death.
3
Check for specification by name or 'هؤلاء'
If the testator says 'بني فلان هؤلاء' and names them, then only those named sons take. If they die before the testator, the bequest is void for them, and no other sons can take.
This overrides the default time rule.
4
Consider bequest to a fetus
A bequest to 'ولد' includes a fetus if born alive. This applies to 'بني' only if the fetus is male and born alive.
The condition of live birth is crucial.
5
Apply the tamlik principle
Understand that bequest is a conditional transfer (تمليك) that takes effect after death. Therefore, the existence of the legatee is considered at that time, not at the time of the will.
This is why a bequest can be valid even if the testator had no wealth at the time of the will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms
بني فلان (banī fulān): Sons of so-and-so; in bequests, it refers only to male offspring, and the timing of their existence is considered at the testator's death.
تمليك مضاف (tamlik mudāf): A conditional transfer of ownership that becomes effective after death; characteristic of bequests.
جنين (janīn): Fetus; a bequest to a fetus is valid if born alive.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a testator bequeaths 'the third to the sons of Zaid' and Zaid has four sons at the time of the will, and later a fifth son is born, and then one of the original four dies before the testator, how is the bequest divided?
A) Among the four sons who were alive at the time of the will
B) Among the three sons who are alive at death (the survivors of the original four and the newborn)
C) Among the four sons: the three survivors of the original four and the newborn
D) The bequest is void because the number of sons changed

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi bequest law, the default rule for 'بني فلان' is that the legatees are the sons alive at the testator's death; specification can override this.

Bequest to the Eldest Children (Akabir)
Ruling on bequest to 'akabir' (eldest children) with age criterion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a bequest made to 'the eldest children' and identify the age criterion used to determine the beneficiaries.

Core Idea
In a bequest to 'the eldest children', the criterion is age above fifty; those below fifty are excluded.

This lesson examines a specific bequest formulation: 'to the eldest of the children of so-and-so'. Unlike general bequests to children, this requires an objective measure to determine who qualifies as 'eldest'. The Hanafi school provides a clear age-based rule that resolves ambiguity and ensures the testator's intent is fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest wording
The testator says 'to the eldest (akabir) of the children of so-and-so'. The key term is 'akabir' which must be interpreted.
This is a formulation that appears in Islamic wills.
2
Determine the age threshold
The Hanafi school defines 'akabir' as those above fifty years of age. Children aged exactly fifty or below are not included.
The threshold is based on custom and practical age criteria.
3
Apply to the given example
In the example, children aged 70, 60, and 40: only those above fifty (70 and 60) receive the bequest. The 40-year-old is excluded.
The bequest is divided equally among the qualifying children.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أوصى بالثلث لأكابر ولد فلان وله أولاد بعضهم أبناء سبعين وبعضهم أبناء ستين وبعضهم أبناء أربعين فالوصية لأبناء ما زاد على الخمسين أو في النصف الأول شيء ء فكذلك السيد إذا قال أكابر رقيقي أحرار ولو قال ثلث مالي بين بني فلان ولأحدهما ثلاث بنين وللآخر واحد كان الثلث بينهم على عدد رؤوسهم، وإن لم يكن للآخر ابن رد نصف الثلث إلى الورثة. ولو قال بين أعمامي وأخوالي وله عم لأن أقل الجمع في باب الوصية والميراث اثنان لما بينا، وإن كان له واحد أو عمان وليس له خال رد نصف الثلث للورثة. ولو قال لأخواتي وله أخ واحد وهو يعلم أو لا يعلم فله نصف الثلث، ولو قال ثلث مالي لفلان ولبنيه وللمساكين فإذا لفلان ابن واحد فالثلث بينهما أرباعاً لفلان سهم ولابنه سهم وللمساكين سهم ويرجع سهم إلى الورثة لأنه قال لبني فلان والابن الواحد لا يكون بنين ويكون الابنان بني فلان لأن اسم الجمع يطلق على الابنين. ولو أوصى بثلثه لآل فلان أو لأهل بيت فلان وليس له بيت ولا قرابة فإنه يعطى الرجل الذي سماه وعياله الذي يعوله من ولده وتدخل امرأته فيهم. الفتاوى : رجل أوصى بثلث ماله لبني فلان وهم ثلاثة قبل موت الموصي ؛ فإن كان أبوهم حياً فالثلث بينهما نصفان وإن كان ميتاً بطل ثلث الوصية فالثلثان بينهما نصفان .

قال الفقيه أبو الليث وبه نأخذ لأن أباهم لو مات لا يبقى له ولد سواهما فانصرفت الوصية إلى عددهما فصار كأنه قال ثلث مالي لفلان وفلان فلما مات أحدهم بطلت وصيته . وإذا أوصى بثلثه لقرابة بني فلان وهم لا يحصون دخل مواليهم وموالي مواليهم وموالي الموالاة وحلفاؤهم يقسمه بين من يقدر عليه منهم بالسوية لأن كل فريق من هؤلاء ينسبون إلى فلان بالبنوة قال عليه الصلاة والسلام إن مولى القوم منهم. وحليف القوم منهم والحليف من
And if he bequeaths the third to the eldest of the children of so-and-so, and he has children, some of them sons of seventy, some sons of sixty, and some sons of forty, then the bequest is for those who exceed fifty, or in the first half something... similarly, the master if he says: the eldest of my slaves are free. And if he says: a third of my wealth between the sons of so-and-so, and one of them has three sons and the other has one, then the third is between them according to the number of their heads. And if the other has no son, half of the third is returned to the heirs. And if he says: between my paternal uncles and my maternal uncles, and he has a paternal uncle because the minimum of a plural in the chapter of bequest and inheritance is two, as we clarified; and if he has one or two paternal uncles and no maternal uncle, half of the third is returned to the heirs. And if he says: to my sisters, and he has one brother, whether he knows or does not know, then he gets half of the third. And if he says: a third of my wealth to so-and-so and his sons and to the poor, then if so-and-so has one son, the third is between them in fourths: for so-and-so a share, for his son a share, and for the poor a share, and one share is returned to the heirs, because he said 'to the sons of so-and-so' and one son does not constitute 'sons', while two sons do constitute 'sons of so-and-so' because the plural noun is applied to two. And if he bequeaths his third to the family of so-and-so or to the household of so-and-so, and he has no household or relatives, then it is given to the man he named and his dependents whom he supports from his children, and his wife enters among them. The Fatawa: A man bequeathed a third of his wealth to the sons of so-and-so, and they were three before the death of the testator; if their father is alive, the third is between them equally two halves, and if he is dead, one third of the bequest is void, so the two thirds are between them two halves.
So-and-so
and sons
and maternal uncle, the third
between them
paternal uncle
Al-Faqih Abu Layth said, and we take with it: because if their father dies, no child remains for him except the two, so the bequest turns to their number, so it is as if he said: a third of my wealth to so-and-so and so-and-so. So when one of them dies, his bequest is void. And if he bequeaths his third to the relatives of the sons of so-and-so, and they are countless, then their clients (mawali) and the clients of their clients and the clients of wala' and their allies enter, and it is divided among those who can be found from them equally, because each group of these are attributed to so-and-so by sonship. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed, the client of a people is one of them.' And the ally of a people is one of them, and the ally is from...
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on various bequest formulations. The first ruling: if someone bequeaths to the 'أكابر' (eldest) of so-and-so's children, the criterion is age above fifty, though the text is somewhat garbled. Then it discusses bequest to two groups each with multiple sons: distribution is per capita, and if one group has no sons, that portion returns to the testator's heirs. Next, bequest to 'أعمامي وأخوالي' (paternal and maternal uncles) requires at least two from each group for the bequest to be valid in full; if one group is missing, half returns to heirs. This is because the minimum plural in bequest and inheritance is two. Similarly, bequest to 'أخواتي' (my sisters) when only one brother exists: the brother takes half the bequest, and the other half returns to heirs. Then bequest to 'فلان ولبنيه وللمساكين' with a single son results in division into four shares: one each for the man and his son, one for the poor, and one returns to heirs because 'بني' requires at least two. Then bequest to 'آل فلان' or 'أهل بيت فلان' goes to the named man and his dependents, including his wife. Then a fatwa from al-Faqih Abu Layth al-Samarqandi about bequest to 'بني فلان' when they are three before the testator's death: if their father is alive, the bequest is split between the father and the sons; if the father is dead, the bequest to the sons is valid, but if one son dies, his share goes back to the testator's heirs because the bequest was effectively to two individuals. Finally, bequest to 'قرابة بني فلان' (relatives of so-and-so) includes clients (mawali) and allies (hulafa'), and they all share equally, based on the hadith 'The client of a people is one of them' and 'The ally of a people is one of them.'

Key Terms
أكابر (akābir): Eldest; in the context of bequest to 'أكابر ولد فلان', it refers to the eldest among the children based on age, specifically those above fifty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths to 'akabir' of his children and his children are aged 60, 50, and 40, who receives the bequest?
A) Only the 60-year-old
B) The 60 and 50-year-old
C) All three
D) None

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest to 'akabir' is interpreted using an age threshold of fifty: only children above fifty qualify.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Bequest to Groups of Sons (Bani Fulan)
Ruling on bequest to two groups of sons with per capita distribution and return of shares.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the distribution of a bequest made to two groups of sons and apply the rule that if a group has no sons, its share returns to the testator's heirs.

Core Idea
A bequest to two groups of sons is divided per capita, and if one group has no sons, half the bequest returns to the testator's heirs.

This lesson deals with a bequest formulation to 'the sons of so-and-so' and 'the sons of another'. The Hanafi school clarifies how to distribute the bequest when the numbers of sons differ, and what happens if one group has no sons at all. This prevents the bequest from being wasted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
The testator says 'a third of my wealth between the sons of so-and-so and the sons of another'. There are two groups, each possibly having multiple sons.
The groups are distinct based on paternity.
2
Distribute per capita
The bequest is divided according to the number of individual sons (heads), not per group. So if one group has three sons and the other has one, the bequest is divided into four shares.
This ensures equal treatment of all individual beneficiaries.
3
Handle missing group
If one group has no sons at all (e.g., the person has no son), then half of the bequest (the share intended for that group) returns to the testator's heirs.
The rationale is that the bequest was conditional on the existence of sons.

Source Text

Minimum Plural in Bequests (Uncles and Sisters)
Rulings on bequests requiring a minimum of two beneficiaries in a group.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the minimum plural for groups in bequests is two, and determine the distribution when only one member of a group exists.

Core Idea
In bequests, the minimum plural is two; if only one exists, half the bequest returns to the heirs.

This lesson covers two rulings: bequest to paternal and maternal uncles, and bequest to sisters. In both cases, if the testator has only one relative from a category (e.g., one paternal uncle, or one brother instead of sisters), the bequest is only partially effective. The Hanafi school bases this on the principle that the plural in bequests requires at least two.

Guided Path
1
Identify the group
The testator says 'to my paternal uncles and maternal uncles' or 'to my sisters'. These are plural forms.
The Arabic language uses plural for three or more, but in legal context, the minimum for effective bequest is two.
2
Check the actual number
Count how many paternal uncles and maternal uncles exist. If a group has only one (or none), then the share for that group is halved or returned.
For uncles, even if both groups together have enough, each group is considered separately.
3
Apply the rule
If the testator has only one paternal uncle and no maternal uncle, then half of the bequest (the part intended for uncles) goes to that one uncle, and the other half returns to the testator's heirs. Similarly, if he has one brother but no sisters, the brother takes half of the bequest meant for sisters.
The rule applies whether the testator knows the actual number or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Bequest to Named Sons: Timing Determines Beneficiaries
Ruling on the temporal scope of a bequest to named individuals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a bequest to named individuals is confined to those alive at the time of the bequest and apply it to determine the validity of shares.

Core Idea
A bequest to named sons goes only to those alive when the testator speaks, not when he dies.

When a testator says 'I bequeath one-third to these sons of so-and-so' and names them, the bequest vests immediately in those named individuals who are alive at that moment. This lesson examines how the timing of the bequest determines the beneficiaries and what happens if a named son dies before the testator.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its wording
Focus on the testator's phrase: 'I bequeath one-third to these sons of so-and-so' with naming. This is a bequest to specific individuals, not a general class.
The key is the demonstrative 'these' (هؤلاء) and the naming.
2
Determine the time reference
According to the Hanafi school, the bequest is tied to the time of utterance, not the time of death. The legatees must be alive when the testator speaks.
This differs from bequests to unspecified groups like 'the sons of so-and-so' without naming, where the time of death is considered.
3
Apply the ruling to a scenario of death before testator
If a named son dies before the testator, his share becomes void and reverts to the testator's estate. It does not pass to the deceased's heirs or to other named sons.
The bequest is contingent on the legatee surviving the testator only if the wording implies it; here the existence at bequest time is decisive.
4
Distinguish from bequest to an unnamed group
Contrast with a bequest 'to the sons of so-and-so' without naming: in that case, the bequest goes to those alive at death, including those born after the bequest.
The presence of naming (تسمية) restricts the class to the named individuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أوصيت بالثلث لبني فلان هؤلاء وسماهم تقع لبنيه الموجودين وقت الوصية حتى تبطل بموتهم ولا يكون لبنيه الموجودين عند الموت
I bequeath one-third to these sons of so-and-so and he named them: it falls to his sons existing at the time of the bequest, so that it becomes void by their death and is not for his sons existing at the time of death.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the effect of a bequest to named individuals. When the testator says 'I bequeath one-third to these sons of so-and-so' and he names them, the bequest applies only to those sons who are alive at the time the bequest is made. If any of them die before the testator's death, their share becomes void and does not go to their heirs; it reverts to the testator's estate. The bequest does not benefit sons who are born after the bequest or those who were not named. This is because the bequest is a contract that is tied to the specific individuals named at the time of utterance. The principle is that a bequest to a defined group goes to those who are existent and qualified at the time of the testamentary declaration, not at the time of death.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyya): A bequest or testamentary disposition of one-third or less of one's estate to a non-heir.
بني فلان هؤلاء (bani fulan ha'ula'): These sons of so-and-so – specific named individuals at the time of bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator says 'I bequeath one-third to these sons of Zaid' and names them, but one of the named sons dies before the testator, what happens to that son's share?
A) It goes to the deceased son's heirs.
B) It becomes void and reverts to the testator's estate.
C) It goes to the testator's other heirs proportionally.
D) It is given to the testator's closest relative.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to named individuals is effective only for those alive when the testator makes the bequest; death of a named legatee before the testator voids his share, which returns to the estate.
